# 太平经钞

**The Taiping Jing Chao**
**Title:** *Excerpts from the Scripture of Great Peace*
*Compiler unknown; according to scholarly consensus, likely abridged by the Tang-dynasty Daoist Lüqiu Fangyuan from the original* Taiping Jing*. Comprising ten scrolls, each corresponding to one of the original scripture’s seventeen-part divisions.*

**Source:** *Zhengtong Daoist Canon*, *Taiping* Section

---

**Taiping Jing Chao, Scroll One of the Jia Division**

**The Supreme August Emperor of the Golden Watchtower, the Later Sage Thearch and Teacher, the Chronologer of Cyclical Qi, the Advent of Balanced Energy, the Portents of the Coming and Going of Worthies and Sages, the Meritorious Practices of the Seed People, and the Foundational Establishment of the Law**

Someone asked: *"The Three Sequences turn like a wheel—what departs must return. The people must have a lord. May we know his surname and given name?"*

*"Excellent! Why do you ask this again?"*

*"True teachers are rare to encounter, and propitious times pass swiftly. Overcome with longing, I humbly seek to hear of this. Though dull and reckless, my reverence runs deep."*

*"Ah, this is no transgression. Heaven has moved you to ask, that later generations may be enlightened. Those who awaken will discern the true and cast off the false. Were I to remain silent, I fear Heaven would grow despondent, and chaos would never be pacified at the proper time. Sit in peace, and I shall recount it to you. You will then understand clearly, without doubt."*

*"The heavens and earth of antiquity and those of today share the same beginning and end, no different in essence. At first, all was good; later, evil arose. Between them, rise and decline alternate—one success, one failure. The Yang’s nine and the six complete a cycle, and when the six nines are fulfilled, great dissolution follows. Heaven and earth dissolve into chaos, and all beings perish. Only those who accumulate goodness escape, becoming the* **Seed People** *forever."*

*"Though the Seed People possess wisdom and understanding, their capacities still vary, not yet perfectly unified. Thus, they require a* **Teacher-Lord** *(*Junshi*). When the lord is sagely and the teacher enlightened, their teachings ensure immortality. Through cultivation, they attain sagehood—hence the name* **Seed People***. The Seed People are sages and worthies, the kind who attain* **long life**.*"*

*"The supreme lord of long life is titled* **The Supreme True and Upright Primordial Wondrous Qi, the August Emperor of the Golden Watchtower of the Upper Clarity, the Later Sage Ninefold Mystery Thearch** *(*Jiuxuan Dijun*). His surname is* **Li***, a scion of the Most High Supreme One and an heir of the Jade Emperor’s Void and Nothingness. His qi first manifested in the* **Taihuang** *era, the fifteenth year of the* **Taihuang Emperor** *(*Taihuang Shijun*), in the* **bingzi** *year. His form took shape in the first year of* **Huangping** *(*Huangping Yuannian*), the* **jiashen** *year. On the third day of the ninth month in the seventh year of* **Shanghe** *(*Shanghe Qinian*), the* **gengyin** *year—a* **jiazi** *day at dawn, when the forces of punishment and virtue aligned—he was born in the* **Li Valley** *between the* **Tian’gang Sacred Realm** *and* **Renwu Pavilion** *on* **Penglai Mountain** *in the* **Northern Mystery Jade Kingdom***. His mother, the* **Mysterious Void Mother of the Supreme Mystery** *(*Shangxuan Xusheng Zhi Mu*), dwelt in the* **Ninefold Mystery Chamber** *within the* **Yin Valley of the Mysterious Void**.*"*

*"At the onset of her pregnancy, she dreamed of dark clouds, the sun, and moon entwining her form, while the six qi’s lightning stirred her spirit. Through a profound union with the Yang Dao, she conceived the* **Perfected One** *(*Zhenren*). On the morning of his birth, three suns rose in the east. After his delivery, nine dragons spat divine water. Thus, his clan took its name from the* **Spiritual Valley** *(*Linggu*), and his given name from the radiance of the luminaries."*

*"At three years of age, his body embodied the Dao and congealed the true. His words blossomed like golden flowers. At five, he often gazed at the sun, rejoicing in its dawn, and faced the moon, sighing at its waning. Above, he observed the Yang qi’s brilliance; below, he witnessed the Yin Dao’s decay. Thereupon, he gathered his hun and harmonized his po, guarded the womb’s treasured spirit, recorded his essence, replenished his blood, and fortified his fluids to solidify his sinews."*

*"At seven, he learned to swallow light and ingest mist, chewing the sun’s roots. By fourteen, he possessed a golden countenance and jade complexion. He abandoned worldly attachments and transcended emotions, embracing transformation to save the world. His purity moved the* **Primordial Simplicity** *(*Taisu*), and he received the teachings of the* **Three Origins** *(*Sanyuan*). He studied the* **Three Caverns** *(*Sandong*) and mastered the* **Nine Methods** *(*Jiufang*)."*

*"At twenty-one, he dwelled in solitude, tempering his sharpness. At twenty-eight, he harmonized with the world while preserving his light. At thirty-five, he disseminated the* **Mysterious Ford** *(*Xuanjin*), and his merit and virtue spread far. At forty-two, he received the scriptures and was named* **Later Sage Thearch** *(*Housheng Dijun*). He was no different from those who had attained the Dao and become Thearchs in former heavens. His investiture was recorded for the present age—hence the title* **Later Sage***. The Dao of the Former Sage and the Later Sage is one and the same."*

*"He ascended to the halls of* **Upper Clarity** *(*Shangqing*), wandered the palaces of* **Great Ultimate** *(*Taiji*), and governed the ten directions of heaven. He was enfeoffed to oversee the billions upon billions of beings, inspecting the celestial rivers, seas, earth’s sources, and mountain forests. None failed to look up in obedience. He presided over the nine layers and ten tiers of heaven—hence the title* **Ninefold Mystery** *(*Jiuxuan*)."*

*"At seventy, he determined the limitless span of his life, adapting to the proper times for concealment and manifestation. He edited the arts of* **not dying** *and compiled the methods of* **long life***. The treasured scriptures, talismans, and diagrams, along with the wondrous techniques of the Three Antiquities, were sealed in jade caskets, attended by divine officials. Their transmission followed strict protocols, their concealment and revelation governed by signs. He established canons and set forth teachings for the* **Seed People***. Those who cannot practice these are not* **Seed People**.*"*

*"Now, as heaven and earth unfold, the era of pure wind recedes. The* **Huangping** *qi has withdrawn, and calamities surge unchecked. Since the age of the* **Upper Thearch** *(*Shanghuang*), and through the reigns of the Three and Five Sovereigns, wars, epidemics, floods, and fires have arisen in relentless succession. All stem from the billions of beings whose hearts are crooked and forms deceptive, who destroy the* **Five Virtues** *(*Wude*), contend through the* **Six Emotions** *(*Liuqing*), indulge in violence, and vie in aggression. They encroach upon one another, disregarding elders and juniors, confounding noble and base. Thus, the Two Modes lose order, the Seven Luminaries deviate from their paths, the Three Powers transform anomalously, omens and portents proliferate, spirits and ghosts clash, beings perish, and disasters strike repeatedly. Yet they remain blind and unrepentant, letting myriad evils run rampant beyond count."*

*"There are four great evils: war, disease, flood, and fire. When the Yang’s nine completes a cycle, and the solitary Yin flourishes, waters overflow. When the hundred sixes complete a circuit, and the Yang prevails, fires erupt. Before the time of Yao, there is no need to recount further. From the Tang onward, I shall briefly outline what is to come. You should heed and remember this, and urgently prepare to avoid calamity."*

*"After Yao’s flood, Tang suffered fire. Since then, minor floods and fires have occurred across the land, summoned by grave sins—not the great* **Yang Nine** *or* **Hundred Six** *cycles. Within the great Nine and Six, there must be major and minor* **jiashen** *years. The* **jiashen** *is the appointed time when ghosts confront humanity. Disasters vary in severity, and blessings and misfortunes differ in depth. As regions and years change, so do their shifts. For those of middling capacity, the appointed time arrives as foretold. For those above or below the middle, they may rise or fall, advance or retreat—ascending and descending without fixed order."*

Those who do evil hasten their doom, while those who do good prolong their years. Without diligent progress, one cannot attain the Dao, and may only extend their allotted time according to the measure of their merit. Thus, the **Hundred Six** and **Yang Nine** cycles may arrive early or late, their great calendric constants adjusted in depth and degree.

Counting from the *dinghai* year of the Tang era, forty-six years later, the *jiashen* year between them was a minor *jiashen*, bringing warfare, plague, and fire—disasters alternating, though not yet the great flood. Minor floods spread widely, their severity varying by year and region. Fifty-five years after another *dinghai*, the *jiashen* year between them was a major *jiashen*, when all three calamities struck together, followed by a great flood that swept all away.

Whenever a major or minor *jiashen* arrives, the wicked are eradicated, and the good are spared. The good become the **Seed People**, while the wicked become the **Chaotic Dregs**. Before the appointed time is over, myriad portents arise in profusion: pestilential toxins surge above, warfare and fire rage below, and floods burst forth from no fixed direction, drowning the wicked in turn. During this fifteen-year span—extending to thirty years—annual disasters grow severe, the worthy and sagely go into hiding, and the great Dao’s divine beings dispatch perfected immortals and superior adepts to traverse the land, teaching with patient guidance. They exhort the high and urge on the low: those who follow become the Seed People, while those who resist are drowned, becoming the Chaotic Dregs, their wickedness utterly purged. Of the Seed People, the most virtuous—barely one in ten—remain, while of the middling and lesser good, half are destroyed, and the surviving half flourish and grow day by day. Only then do sagely rulers, enlightened masters, and great ministers descend and appear.

After the minor *jiashen* and before the *renshen* year, if the ruler of the minor *jiashen* is sagely and wise, stern yet benevolent, harming neither principle nor order, he may extend his years and attain long life. Through devoted study, he may even achieve immortality, though without deep mastery of the **Scriptures of Great Peace** or prolonged practice of its teachings, the era of Great Peace will be brief, and his name cannot be fixed. Those who practice it have their names inscribed in the Azure Register by the **Controller of Destiny**; those who do not are recorded in the Black Script. The Black Script means death; the Azure Register means life. The ledgers of life and death reside in the **Hall of Light** in Heaven. The Dao of Heaven is impartial, favoring only the good. Those who cultivate and fulfill the Great Peace become the Great Peace. Those who achieve the Lesser Great Peace align their virtue with the Lord of Great Peace. The Lord of Great Peace whose name is fixed is Lord Li. In the *renchen* year, on the sixth day of the third month, he will manifestly appear in the world, riding the **Three Pure Radiance Chariot**, followed by ten thousand flying carriages and dragons. He will elevate the good as Seed People and scholars as immortal officials, establishing disciplines and statutes to reward virtue, suppress evil, curb the roots of sin, and supervise those who advance in blessed deeds. Those who persevere without slackening will achieve perfection as divine transcendents, aligning their virtue with the Emperor. Those who slacken and fall into evil will have their wickedness daily recorded, destined to become the later Chaotic Dregs.

The lofty and wise, with keen insight and unwavering clarity, must diligently progress, inwardly cultivate the Emperor’s teachings, and remember the great divine lord’s assistants without fail. The sagely ruler, enlightened ministers, and numinous officials will aid people in attaining deathlessness, becoming Seed People forever, ascending as immortal transcendents, and ultimately attaining the rank of the **Later Sage**. The Later Sage, Lord Li’s Grand Preceptor, is surnamed Peng. He studied the Dao before Lord Li and holds the position of **Left Perfected of the Grand Tenuity**. During the era of the **Human Sovereign**, he was commanded by the **Lord of the Dao of the Sovereign** to protect and invest the people, serving as Lord Li’s Grand Preceptor, governing from the **Northern Pond Palace of the Grand Tenuity** at the **Luminous Upper Terrace**. Every two thousand five hundred years, he changes his name, traversing the Great Void, circling the Eight Darknesses, ascending to the Utmost Above, and descending to the Utmost Below. Rare are the true officials who have glimpsed his radiant countenance.

The **Lord of the Azure Lads of the Fangzhu Palace** is the Later Sage Lord Li’s **Grand Minister**.
The **Southern Culmen Lord of the Great Cinnabar Palace** is the Later Sage Lord Li’s **Grand Guardian**.
The **Lord of the Great Simplicity of the White Mountain Palace** is the Later Sage Lord Li’s **Grand Tutor**.
The **Governor of All Perfected of the Western City Palace** is the Later Sage Lord Li’s **Grand Steward**.

These five—one master and four assistants—are collectively called the **Assistants**. The term *assistant* signifies a father and a support: revered like a father, they ensure the master’s teachings are carried out. Together, they are called assistants; separately, they are the **Left Assistant**, **Right Assistant**, **Front Deliberator**, and **Rear Attendant**. The *attendant* voices opinions, initiates actions, fills omissions, and completes tasks, making decisions and proclaiming them—this is the steward. The *deliberator* ponders unresolved matters, illuminating and clarifying them—this is the tutor. The *assistant* (right) ensures certainty and prevents errors—this is the guardian. The *assistant* (left) aids the ruler and follows the master, guiding all into the Dao—this is the minister. The four and five assess omens, thoroughly weighing approval and disapproval, promoting and expanding the true transformation—together, they are called the **Assisting Masters**.

In times of leisure, when facing forward, one may consult the **Deliberating Tutor** for unresolved questions; when looking back, the **Attending Steward** for overlooked concerns; to the right, the **Guarding Assistant** for unclear matters; and to the left, the **Assisting Minister** for what remains obscure. By consulting the four assistants—guardian, tutor, steward, and minister—success lies with the master; none can be lacking. The sagely emperor set this model for later generations to follow.

Inwardly, there is the **Guardian**, who manages affairs—this pertains to the right, the treasure of quiescent perfection. Outwardly, there is the **Master**, who manages affairs—this pertains to the left, where movement returns to stillness. This is most difficult, hence the focus on the assistants and master. When looking forward, there is the **Tutor**, who expounds and discusses the Dao’s essence. When looking back, there is the **Steward**, who decides right and wrong. The remaining public ministers, officials, immortal transcendents, and sage ranks—three hundred sixty-one in number—command thirty-six thousand, who in turn lead three hundred sixty thousand. The people number ten, a hundred, a thousand, ten thousand, and myriadfold. Twenty-four perfected beings are constantly sent to secretly instruct those with sincere hearts, all subordinate to the **Grand Minister of Fangzhu**. This cannot be fully described; one must carefully contemplate the great and independently investigate the small.

Excellent! Today’s questions have resolved my doubts, and I have heard your instructions anew.

It is asked: What practices did Lord Li consistently follow to attain such lofty transcendence? May we hear of the Grand Preceptor’s and the four assistants’ studies?

Excellent indeed! You ask on behalf of those who are foolish, who wander lost and do not believe in the Dao, whose learning lacks firmness, whose progress and retreat lack constancy, and who thus fall into lowly and bitter states—hence your earnest inquiry. Now I shall explain it to you.

From the beginningless past until now, accumulated deeds have endured for ages; a single good or evil act cannot be fully recounted, and speaking of them brings no benefit. Here, I shall take only the recent practices by which one attains lofty nobility: the **Numinous Writ of Purple Texts** is the essential.

The **Great Lord of the Azure Lad**, Preceptor of the Lofty Dawn in the Jade Treasury of the Eastern Flower, purified himself in the Yellow Chamber of the Cold Numen Elixir Hall for three years before ascending to the **Golden Portals of the Supreme Clarity**. There, the Four Celestial Emperors reside, with the **Lord of the Great Peace Dao** stationed at their left and right, dwelling in the **Cavern-Real Jade Terrace of the Great Void**, within the **Jade Chamber of Equanimity** and the **Golden Flower’s Inner Sanctum**. Fifty thousand handmaidens—transcendent maidens and perfected beings—stand in attendance. Poisonous dragons and lightning tigers, celestial apes of the highest heavens, array themselves in venomous postures, guarding the gates and holding the passes. Giant toads a thousand fathoms long patrol the ramparts, while flying dragons and darting sparrows, leviathan roc and wondrous birds, clack their beaks and brandish their claws, filling the vast courtyard. The celestial majesty blazes resplendent, its radiance streaming in eight directions. Dark banners flutter in the wind, dancing pennants and canopies swirl. Jade trees chime with resonant tones, their gemmed branches murmuring of their own accord. Divine songs are sung in unison, phoenixes cry in profound harmony, spirit consorts join in chorus, unicorns dance and simurghs glide. The celestial harmony rings in eightfold resonance, uniting the nine harmonies and hundredfold gatherings.

The Azure Lad prostrated himself forward and received the **Numinous Writ of Purple Texts**, each oral transmission and secret formula contained within the scriptures numbering twenty-four. The first: **True Records** must be examined with care and memorized in darkness. The second: **Transcendent Taboos** must be studied in detail and preserved without forgetfulness.

The third: **Exploring the Flying Root**, one must swallow the essence of the sun.
The fourth: **Ingesting the Luminous Numinous Talisman**.
The fifth: **Ingesting the Moon’s Radiance**.
The sixth: **Ingesting the Yin-Generated Talisman**.
The seventh: **Restraining the Three Hun**.
The eighth: **Controlling the Seven Po**.
The ninth: **Wearing the August Image Talisman**.
The tenth: **Ingesting the Resplendent Elixir**.
The eleventh: **Ingesting the Yellow Water**.
The twelfth: **Ingesting the Returning Water**.
The thirteenth: **Consuming the Ring of Steel**.
The fourteenth: **Consuming the Phoenix Brain**.
The fifteenth: **Consuming the Pine Pear**.
The sixteenth: **Consuming the Plum Jujube**.
The seventeenth: **Ingesting the Water Decoction**.
The eighteenth: **Tempering White Silver and Purple Gold**.
The nineteenth: **Ingesting the Cloud’s Marrow**.
The twentieth: **Forging White Silver and Purple Gold**.
The twenty-first: **Crafting the Weight**.
The twenty-second: **Consuming Bamboo Shoots**.
The twenty-third: **Consuming Swan’s Dried Meat**.
The twenty-fourth: **Wearing the Five Spirit Talismans**.

Mastery of these twenty-four practices grants boundless transformation, allowing one to transcend beyond the Three Realms and wander freely within the Six Directions. No calamity can harm them, no demonic or malevolent forces dare oppose them—all submit of their own accord. Their rank attains the ultimate in the Daoist lineage, and their grace flows to all beings, both hidden and manifest, who rely upon it.

Those who disbelieve or refuse, who remain ignorant or blind, choose darkness for themselves, forever estranged from the Dao. They wallow in suffering and venomous affliction, entangled in the mire of vexation. Though great compassion pities them, nothing can be done.

Alas! Those of noble aspiration—act swiftly, act swiftly, and do not betray these words.

It is said: Excellent, excellent! Today my doubts are questioned, and I have heard the command anew.

*Excerpt from the First Scroll of the* **Abridged Canon of Great Peace, Supreme Purity Section, First Volume** *concludes.*

---
*[Note: The following colophon and scholarly annotations are not part of the translation but are retained for editorial context as per the original text.]*
#1 According to textual analysis, this scripture is believed to be a fabrication by Shangqing Daoist practitioners of the Northern and Southern Dynasties, rather than an authentic excerpt from the original *Abridged Canon of Great Peace, First Volume*. The *Abridged Canon of Great Peace, Gui Section* is considered to preserve the original text of the *First Volume*. See the Dunhuang catalog for reference, as well as Wang Ming’s *On the Errors in the Abridged Canon of Great Peace*.
*Excerpt from the Second Scroll of the* **Abridged Canon of Great Peace, Second Volume***.*

**Harmonizing Yin and Yang in Accordance with the Dao’s Law**

To restore youth and prevent aging—when the Great Dao returns, all people’s years shall be tested and verified. Close your eyes and look inward: a pure, radiant white appears. If at dawn you lie calmly upon your mat, or dwell within warmth and steam, at this time let neither sinew nor bone stir, nor your mouth speak. Every stretch and bend brings ease; the heart rejoices, suffused with a sense of blended moisture. The nose breathes freely, and sweetness arises in the mouth—these are the signs.

Thus, those who follow Heaven and Earth enjoy enduring governance; those who follow the four seasons see their kingship flourish day by day. The Dao employs no arcane phrases—its use lies in the alternation of one yin and one yang. Those who attain its governance prosper; those who lose it fall into chaos. Those who attain its governance become spirit-like.

Moreover, those who clearly lose its governance render the Dao unworkable. Ponder this meaning deeply, and you will merge with the Dao as one.

To record the body’s alignment is to let the spirit make one self-aware of the method. Heaven employs the Dao to generate humanity, granting each person one body and one law: sevenfold interwoven yin and yang, half yin and half yang, only thus can they complete one another. Therefore, the upper part models itself on yang, the lower on yin; the left follows yang, the right follows yin. Yang delights in life, yin delights in killing. Yang embodies the Dao, yin embodies punishment. Yang is goodness, and the yang spirit aids it; yin is evil, and the yin spirit aids it. Accumulate goodness without cease, and Dao-fortune will arise, bringing daily auspiciousness.

Yang resides in the head, yin in the feet. Thus, the ruler values virtue and power while employing punishment below—this is the model to follow. The petty man inverts this, devaluing virtue and power while elevating punishment—yet he too follows this model. Therefore, humanity is the root and handle of the Dao, the leader of the spirits. One must understand this intent and skillfully nurture oneself to attain longevity. Those who fail to nurture their bodies incur the blame of the spirits; the spirits abandon them, and how can their bodies fare well?

In doing good, do not dare stray from the guiding cord, nor deceive yourself. In doing good, the spirits know it of themselves; in doing evil, the spirits know it of themselves. These are not other spirits—they are the spirits within your own body. Speech issues from the heart and belly, yet others come to know of it—this is the spirit within the body informing them.

Thus, calming the spirit and settling the body is the foundation of governance and the sign of longevity. The affairs of non-action arise from this. First cultivate the self to discern fortune and misfortune. Therefore, the wise and sagely understand: they cultivate the self, not others. They deeply ponder the Dao’s intent and thus achieve Great Peace. The noble person attains it and flourishes; the petty person practices it and collapses. Cultivate the One to repel the perverse.

When Heaven and Earth first opened, the root was prized—it is the origin of qi. To bring about Great Peace, contemplate the root. Failing to reflect on the root is called great confusion; undertakings will fail, and disasters will converge. This is not humanity’s fault but the loss of the root. Abandoning the root to seek the branches brings incurable misfortune—thus, one must ponder deeply.

The One is the root of the Dao, the beginning of qi, the point to which life attaches, and the master of the multitude of hearts. To know its reality, recognize that it resides at the center as the root—the dwelling place of life. Therefore, one must deeply understand it and return to benevolence and worthiness to put it into practice.

The human root lies within; branches and leaves are without. Command the One to return all outward things; urgently govern the inner and pursue the distant by tending to the near. Those who guard the One receive the aid of celestial spirits; those who guard two receive the aid of earthly spirits; those who guard three receive the aid of human ghosts; those who guard four or five receive the protection of things. Thus, guarding the One extends life; guarding two sets a date with misfortune; guarding three brings chaotic governance; guarding four or five invites daily calamity. Deeply ponder this meaning—it is called knowing the Dao.

Therefore, the One of the head is the crown; the One of the seven regulators is the eye; the One of the abdomen is the navel; the One of the vessels is qi; the One of the five viscera is the heart; the One of the four limbs is the palms and soles; the One of the bones is the spine; the One of the flesh is the intestines and stomach. Those who firmly guard it and understand the Dao’s intent—those who attain the Dao make people benevolent; those who lose it make people greedy.

Govern the body with joy, guard the form and follow the thoughts, focus the mind to repel disaster. What is joy in the Dao? Joy harmonizes yin and yang. In all matters, act in silence, enabling people to grasp the Dao’s root. Thus, when primordial qi delights, great prosperity arises; when nature delights, things grow strong; when Heaven delights, the Three Luminaries shine; when Earth delights, it achieves constancy; when the Five Phases delight, they do not harm one another; when the four seasons delight, what they generate flourishes; when the ruler delights, the world knows no illness; when crawling creatures delight, they do not harm one another; when the myriad things delight, they abide in their constancy; when people delight, they do not fret or change their hearts; when ghosts and spirits delight, they benefit the emperor and king.

Thus, joy is the essence of Heaven and Earth’s good qi, which summons the numinous. Stillness generates luminosity, and luminosity is how one awaits the spirits. Those who can communicate with the numinous have the Dao as their neighbor and attain long life and enduring existence.

Seeking the Dao is often bitter, for one cannot return to the heart’s intent. Now, by shifting customs and altering trends, directing the heart’s aim—who would dare contend with this? Does not the music of Great Peace emerge from the palace? It firmly purifies the state, secures the body, and enters the Dao. The barbarians retreat, numinous omens appear, celestial portents return, and malevolent spirits depart.

The human spirit is born within but roams without. If it wanders untimely, it harms the body. If one can recall it and return, self-governance will not fail. How to recall it? Ensure the inner chamber is empty, with no one nearby. Paint an image matching the color of the viscera, corresponding to the qi of the four seasons. Hang it in the window’s light and contemplate it. Above is the image of the viscera; below are the ten directions. When lying down, focus on the nearby hanging image and contemplate without cease. The spirits of the five viscera can report the qi of the twenty-four seasonal nodes; the spirits of the Five Phases will come to the rescue, and all illnesses will be cured.

Men contemplate male images, women contemplate female images, each using a one-chi measure as the standard, shifting with the four seasons. In spring, ten azure lads; in summer, ten crimson lads; in autumn, ten white lads; in winter, ten black lads; and in the four seasons’ transitions, twelve yellow lads. These twenty-five spirit-persons, true persons together, constitute the method of upright Dao and virtue. Yang transforms into yin, yin transforms into yang; when yin and yang unite, the Dao may be practiced.

Heaven requires earth to bring forth life; earth requires heaven to achieve completion. Spring and summer require autumn and winter; day requires night. A ruler requires ministers to establish governance; ministers require a ruler to carry out their duties. Thus, jia requires yi, zi requires chou—all mutually complete the Dao’s governance. To act rightly is to follow heaven’s course, not to conform to human desires, for all such conformity is contrary to the heavenly Dao. Like the Eastern Sea, though lowly, it delights in water, and all rivers flow into it, thereby attaining its Dao. The leviathan emerges from its depths, and the luminous moon-pearl is born there—such is the efficacy of attaining the Dao. When Daoists gather, they must obtain methods for extending years and extraordinary auspicious responses. When the worthy gather, governance is peaceful; when scholars gather, minor disorders are settled; when the five weapons gather, great defeat ensues.

A ruler should uphold the Dao; ministers should uphold virtue. Dao and virtue are like the outer and inner layers of a garment. If heaven were not vast, it could not encompass the myriad things. All things are half good and half evil—all must be endured. The ruler emulates this, as does the empress and the inner palace. These two exemplify the way of compassionate parents. Thus, when parents raise children, they love the good and pity the wicked, thereby harmonizing the household’s Dao.

The sun resembles the ruler; the moon resembles the great ministers; the stars resemble the hundred officials. When the worthy collectively shine, the myriad things harmoniously arise. Thus, the pure ascend to heaven, the turbid descend to earth, and harmony resides in humanity. This is the method of harmonizing the numinous spirits.

I desire that the myriad spirits of heaven and earth be harmonious and kind, no longer wantonly harming people, that heaven and earth remain joyful, all spirits rejoice, and people suffer no afflictions. When the emperor obtains heaven’s power, his undertakings are blessed—how could this be interrupted? Thus, the sage who upholds the Dao, in times of clarity and stillness, partakes of morning food, and all spirits call out to speak with him, as if one now calls a guest. The hundred spirits declare themselves heaven’s officials, heaven’s envoys; the host of essences are earth’s officials, earth’s envoys; the hundred ghosts are envoys of harmony. These three are the envoys of yin, yang, and harmony, aiding heaven and earth in governance and together promoting the emperor’s benefit.

The method of guarding the One and illuminating it is the root of longevity. The myriad spirits may be mastered, emerging from the gate of radiant light. When the One’s essence is illuminated, like fire at its birth, guard it swiftly and do not lose it. It begins as true red, ends as true white, and over time becomes true azure. Profound clarity extends ever farther, then returns to govern the One, so that within there is no obscurity. All illnesses depart; guarding it without slack is the art of ten thousand years.

The method of guarding the One and illuminating it: illumination has the light of the rising sun and the brightness of midday—this is the foremost good, attaining heaven’s longevity. Dwelling in tranquility, one may preserve it for ten thousand generations without loss.

The method of guarding the One varies in excellence. What is the Dao? It is the origin of the myriad things, that which cannot be named. Within the six directions, nothing can transform without the Dao. Primordial qi practices the Dao to generate the myriad things. Great and small, heaven and earth—none are born without the Dao. Thus, primordial qi is formless, governing the formed; it unfolds primordial qi and is born not apart from the Dao.

The natural is the natural of the myriad things. Without practicing the Dao, one cannot envelop heaven and earth, each attaining its place, enabling the high to remain unaware of danger. Heaven practices the Dao, unceasing day and night, swifter than wind and rain, yet still fears losing the Dao’s intent—how much more so for kings? The Three Luminaries practice the Dao without rest, thus appearing in the heavens and illuminating the eight directions. If they lose the Dao, their light vanishes.

When the king, the hundred officials, the myriad things, and all living beings reside together, the five stars observe their transgressions. If the king restores virtue, the Virtue Star comes to guard him. If he practices martiality, the Martial Star comes to guard him. If he practices gentleness, the Gentle Star comes to guard him. If he practices strength, the Strong Star comes to guard him. If he practices trustworthiness, the Trust Star comes to guard him. Though distant, their response is near. Heaven and humanity are one—how can one not be cautious?

In spring, the king should be warm; in summer, hot; in autumn, cool; in winter, cold—this is the king’s virtue. The king’s qi communicates with the emperor’s qi; the minister’s qi corresponds to the chief ministers; the subtle qi corresponds to petty officials; the auspicious qi aligns with the inner palace; the declining qi corresponds to the people; the qi of execution and death corresponds to prisoners—each category remotely stirs the other through the Dao. If the king’s qi does not arrive, the king’s grace cannot be bestowed.

The ancient sage-kings reflected on the Dao through this, thus discerning the signs of success and failure and examining their meaning. When the king practices the Dao, heaven and earth rejoice; when he loses the Dao, heaven and earth produce calamities and anomalies.

When the king calmly contemplates virtue and practices the Dao to secure his person, seeking longevity and self-nourishment, harmonizing the way of husband and wife, so that yin and yang each attain their place, heaven and earth are at peace. Though heaven and the emperor are separated by ten thousand myriad li, they respond to the Dao—is this not wondrous? This is called *The Divine Formula Book*.

Primordial qi is natural, together constituting the nature of heaven and earth. When the six directions and eight quarters rejoice, good responses arise; when they do not rejoice, evil responses arise. Their forms resemble reflections, their sounds harmonize with echoes.

The Three Qi—Great Yin, Great Yang, and Harmony—together govern, mutually stirring one another. Humanity is the pivot—thus one must deeply understand this. When all value their lives and nurture their bodies, they know to honor their superiors and love their subordinates, delighting in life and hating death. When the Three Qi rejoice, together they form Great Harmony, and responses emerge in unison.

But when the multitude of worthies is gathered, and they aspire only to the Dao of longevity, they bring tranquility to their superiors and become the treasures of the state. To nurture one’s nature is to nurture one’s people.

Heaven shows no partial favor, yet its blessings are steadfast. The divine shows no partial kinship, yet the virtuous manifest its efficacy. Within a single body, one may become worthy, divine, or base—why is this? It is due to error, for the numinous is revealed. Thus, the Dao of guarding the One is to nurture one’s nature, and this lies in learning.

Among the multitude, those who encounter many auspicious responses are trustworthy; those who encounter none have erred in conduct. Through divination, right and wrong become known. What the scales discern is human sentiment. Heaven’s illumination of humanity is no different from a mirror. Examine this meaning carefully, align with Heaven’s will, and find repose with the true spirits—how could this not be auspicious?

In accomplishing affairs, not a fraction is lost, for one seeks the harmonious intent of Heaven and Earth. When Heaven and Earth are in balance, the myriad things are at peace; when the sovereign is just, the myriad people are well-governed.

If one acts purely in Yang, the Earth will not fully yield its bounty; if purely in Yin, Heaven will not fully bring forth life. Only by uniting the Three Powers—Yin and Yang in mutual accord—does harmony reside within.

The sages of antiquity brought about Great Peace by seeking the harmonious heart of Heaven and Earth. If a single qi is obstructed, a hundred affairs go awry. When the Three Qi harmonize, the laws of emperors and kings flourish. By penetrating the harmonious discourse of Heaven and Earth, one follows the Great Enterprise, roams with the Three Qi, and enables the ruler to be without cares. Worthies emerge in full, assisting and elevating the emperor, bringing great joy to Heaven.

Simply by fully aligning with Heaven and Earth, not losing even a fraction, one swiftly attains Great Peace, and auspicious responses arise in unison.

Primordial qi has three names: Great Yang, Great Yin, and Harmony. Forms have three names: Heaven, Earth, and Humanity. Heaven has three names: sun, moon, and stars, with the North Star as its center. Earth has three names: mountains, rivers, and level land. Humanity has three names: father, mother, and child. Governance has three names: ruler, minister, and people—all desiring Great Peace.

These three must always be held close as heart and mind, not losing even a fraction, so that they share a single concern and unite as one household. Then Great Peace is swiftly attained, and longevity is assured without doubt.

Thus, the male resembles Heaven, and his thoughts dwell on the female—this is the clear manifestation of Heaven’s design for humanity. The minister serves as Earth’s conduit; Earth constantly aspires to ascend and align its heart with Heaven. Thus, the myriad things born of Earth ever rise upward without cease, and clouds and mist coalesce into rain.

Therefore, the loyal minister’s concern is ever upward, tirelessly mindful of his lord—this is the clear manifestation of Earth’s design. The people embody the discourse of Harmony, for Harmony is what regulates the myriad things. Harmony is the infant, born of father and mother; its life belongs to the father, its lineage to the superior, yet it is entrusted to the mother. Thus, in distress, it yearns for its lord and father. These three reflect the images of husband and wife, father and child.

They ought to communicate freely, unite their strength in shared concern, so that the Three Qi merge into Great Harmony. From Great Harmony arises the qi of Great Peace. If these Three Qi are severed, and even one fails to reach, Great Harmony does not arrive, and Great Peace does not emerge.

Yin and Yang depend on Harmony. When the qi of Harmony is attained, the myriad things flourish, the people are harmonious, and the king’s governance brings Great Peace.

The ruler is Heaven; if his grace does not descend, things have no means to be born, and people cannot attain longevity. If the ruler’s heart is not open, Heaven’s heart cannot reach below. If wife and child do not receive the lord and father’s decree, the household becomes rebellious. If the minister’s qi cannot ascend, Earth’s qi cannot be fulfilled—how then can loyal ministers assist the enlightened king in governance? To wound Earth’s heart is to leave widows in the chamber, ever grieving in sorrow, so that no good minister may advance.

If the people’s qi does not ascend, how can the qi of Harmony arise? Harmony is meant to harmonize with the emperor and king, to regulate the myriad things, each attaining its proper governance. Now, if the Three Qi do not communicate well, how can Great Peace be achieved? The method of the peaceful and joyous ruler lies in this.

The ruler must transform the myriad things with virtue and power, enabling each to find its place. One who cannot transform the myriad things cannot be called a ruler. It is like a husband and wife who together bear a child—they are called parents, an image of a household. Without the ability to bear a child, how can they be called parents? Thus, one who cannot transform and give life to the myriad things cannot be called the parents of the people.

Fire can transform the Four Elements and itself becomes the fifth, thus earning the image of a ruler. Wood’s nature is harmonious and focused, yet with fire it scatters into ash. Metal’s nature is hard and unyielding, yet with fire it softens. Earth’s nature is greatly yielding, yet with fire it hardens into tile. Water’s nature is cold, yet with fire it warms. Fire itself aligns with the Five Phases, yet its transformations are boundless; its nature is active and ascendant.

Yin submits to Yang, ministers submit to rulers, and fire’s illumination is clear and penetrating, discerning right from wrong—thus it earns the name of ruler, while the others cannot. Earth does not transform immediately but does so over time—thus it is called the Queen Earth. The other three serve as assistants, images of ministers.

The Dao can transform all things, thus Primordial Qi guards the Dao, circulates its qi, and gives birth to Heaven and Earth. They stand without pillars, and the myriad things are born without fixed categories, extending to later generations in transmission, speaking of their kinds.

It is like grasses and trees growing on Earth—do they have fixed categories? It is Primordial Qi guarding the Dao that brings forth such things. Naturally guarding the Dao and acting, the myriad things each find their place.

Heaven guards the Dao and acts, thus it is called divine and boundless, an image of the ruler and father, able to regulate and transform all things, truly embodying the Dao’s intent. Earth guards the Dao and acts, uniting the five directions with the center, to which the myriad things return.

The Three Luminaries guard the Dao and act, thus nothing escapes their illumination. Thunder and lightning guard the Dao and act, therefore they can stir all under Heaven, riding qi to come and go. The four seasons and five phases guard the Dao and act, thus they transform the myriad things, giving them constancy. Yin and yang, female and male guard the Dao and act, thus they transmit through generations. In all matters, great or small, if they guard the Dao and act, there is no misfortune. If the Dao is lost today, great chaos ensues.

Thus when yang is at peace, the myriad things generate themselves; when yin is at peace, the myriad things complete themselves. When yin and yang govern the Dao, instruction extends to ministers, transformation flows to the people, receiving mandate from Heaven, receiving form from Earth, receiving teaching from masters—only then does one hear the essential Dao of all under Heaven.

Those who guard the root become kings; those who guard the stem become ministers; those who guard the floating blossoms are good, yet disordered and without constancy. The emperor is the child of Heaven; the empress is the child of Earth. These are the first numinous qi of Heaven and Earth. Heaven and Earth always desire joy, not sorrow or suffering, cherishing them so—this is the heart-mind of Heaven and Earth, their intent and qi foremost.

Thus when the ruler suffers sorrow, the qi of the four seasons and five phases fall into discord, and the taking of life becomes irregular. The method of suspending images to return the spirit.

The spirit is born within: in spring, ten Green Lads; in summer, ten Red Lads; in autumn, ten White Lads; in winter, ten Black Lads; and in the four seasons, twelve Yellow Lads—this is the way men store the spirit. The spirit of women follows the same number. Men contemplate men, women contemplate women, all using a one-chi measure as the standard, drawing them well to make them beloved. If one cannot maintain joy and restraint, the hun and spirit swiftly return.

The formula for resolving inherited burdens.

Since the opening of Heaven and Earth, baleful qi has never ceased—once cut off, it later arises again. Why is this? Lifespan is Heaven’s most precious treasure. It is bestowed through private virtue and cannot be falsely attained. To know this treasure: when the six directions of Heaven and Earth, the eight distant realms, and the myriad things all remain free of grievance and entanglement, all rejoice greatly—only then is longevity increased. If even one matter brings displeasure, it immediately harms and brings death.

In human conduct, some strive to do good yet often meet with misfortune; others strive to do evil yet often meet with fortune. Those who claim themselves worthy are mistaken. Those who strive to do good yet meet misfortune bear the inherited burdens of their ancestors’ transgressions, as disasters flow forward and backward, accumulating to harm them. Those who do evil yet meet with fortune inherit the deep accumulations of their ancestors’ great merits, which flow to benefit them. If one performs great merits ten thousand times over, even if their ancestors left lingering misfortunes, these cannot reach them. Instead, the merits pass onward, flowing to their descendants as inherited blessings.

Five generations form a small cycle, and after ten generations, the effects return to their origin. Some perform minor good deeds yet cannot escape imprisonment; their ancestors’ flowing evils and inherited burdens strike them, cutting off their line and leaving no descendants—truly a grievous wrong.

Inherited burdens are divided into three celestial ranks: the Emperor’s burdens flow for thirty thousand years, ministers’ for three thousand years, and the common people’s for three hundred years. All bear and pass on these burdens in succession, rising and falling with the decline and flourishing of governance, never ceasing. If one now follows this principle, modeling governance on the Heavenly August Emperor to sever these burdens, they must ponder deeply and never forget.

Humans possess three lifespans, corresponding to three qi: the life of Great Yang, Great Yin, and the Harmonious Center. The upper lifespan is one hundred twenty years, the middle eighty, and the lower sixty. One hundred twenty corresponds to Heaven’s great reckoning, completing the boundary of Heaven and Earth in a single year. Eighty corresponds to the division of Yin and Yang, the eight pairs that align with Earth, distinguishing the myriad things—those that die depart, while those that live remain. Sixty corresponds to the qi of the Harmonious Center, attaining the hexagram *Dun* in the sixth month. *Dun* means escape and disappearance, thus governing the meeting of life and death.

If one ceaselessly practices good, surpassing these lifespans, it is called transcending the world. If one ceaselessly practices evil, falling short of these three lifespans, it is called premature death. Those who die in the womb or before maturity bear the innocent inherited burdens of their ancestors’ transgressions.

Those with frequent head ailments suffer from Heaven’s displeasure. Those with frequent foot ailments suffer from Earth’s displeasure. Those with frequent internal organ illnesses suffer from the warring qi of the five phases. Those with frequent limb ailments suffer from the disharmony of the four seasons’ qi. Those with frequent deafness and blindness suffer from the three luminaries losing their proper measure. Those with frequent chills and fevers suffer from the contention of Yin and Yang qi. Those with frequent confusion and disorder suffer from the myriad things losing their place. Those with frequent afflictions by ghosts and spirits suffer from the anger of Heaven and Earth’s deities. Those who often die of warmth-related illnesses are slain by Great Yang qi. Those who often die of cold are harmed by Great Yin qi. Those who often die suddenly are struck by excessively harsh punitive qi. Those who often suffer from bloating or shortness of breath suffer from the discord of the eight solar terms.

Now, Heaven and Earth’s Yin and Yang have entirely lost their proper places, thus harming the myriad things. If the Emperor’s governance is disharmonious, floods and droughts occur without pattern, bandits arise frequently, and punishments are made harsher—yet this only increases chaos, entangling and unresolved. The people all cry out to Heaven, while the court’s governance is disordered, losing its rhythm and constancy. The myriad things are harmed, moving even the Azure Heaven above. The three luminaries rage and change erratically, the constellations move in disorder—thus, only the utmost Dao can save them. I know Heaven’s intent does not deceive you.

Heaven’s might, once unleashed, cannot be restrained. To incur guilt before Heaven is to invite premature death.

From the opening of Heaven and Earth since the Great Beginning, sages each comprehended one aspect with perfect clarity, knowing it truly without doubt. Thus, each established one great enterprise, enabling later generations to cultivate it without error. Therefore, sages each excelled in one great enterprise yet could not fully know the Dao of Heaven—hence, their virtues differed. This is like Heaven and Earth: how much more so for humans? Heaven and Earth each excel in one aspect: Heaven excels in height and clarity, Earth in depth and turbidity, while the Harmonious Center nurtures the myriad things. Even they cannot encompass all—how much less can ordinary people?

*Hai* is the northwest extreme of Heaven and Earth; *Si* is the southeast extreme. If *Hai*’s cold does not close in due time, the following year’s *Si* will be harmed in return. *Zi* is the north extreme of Heaven and Earth; *Wu* is the south extreme. If this winter’s *Zi* does not properly store and conceal, *Wu* will bear the inherited burden and perish in return. *Chou* is the northeast extreme of Heaven and Earth; *Wei* is the southwest extreme. If *Chou* does not timely bring forth life, the sixth month will suffer its punishment in return. The nature and movement of Heaven and Earth are all thus.

Now, if the Emperor dwells within the hundredfold layers, governing with virtue and benevolence, his grace extends ten thousand *li*, and the people receive his favor. Fathers are kind, children filial; households are sufficient, and people do not turn to wickedness. If the Emperor within loses his virtue, beyond ten thousand *li*, officials and people lose their proper roles—though they are separated by countless *li*, the cause is one.

Practicing good words is not as effective as practicing good conduct in oneself.

The Perfected One asked the Divine Person: “In my life, what can I do to always be joyful?”

The Divine Person replied: “Do you recall the ancient, vast Perfected One? The reason he aged after others was that he abandoned the depraved and solely cherished the true Dao. The true Dao is constantly preserved, while the depraved vanish. While all people suffer hardship, I alone endure—this is constant joy. Shining brightly and rejoicing alone, what resentment could there be? Even if one ultimately cannot attain long life, what can be done?”

The Divine Person said: “Accumulated practice nears completion; thoughts of goodness nears life. The Dao is the scripture of the boundless. In ancient times, the Divine Persons governed, taking Perfected Ones as ministers to rule the people—thus the people knew not that above them there was an emperor, and through the Dao’s natural non-action, they governed themselves. Next, the Perfected Ones governed, taking Immortals as ministers; though they did not see the people, the people occasionally knew there was an emperor, hearing his teachings and revering their lord. Next, the Immortals governed, taking Daoists as ministers; their rule bore slight traces of punishment and law, and the people’s hearts stirred with fear, giving rise to cunning and deceit. Next came hegemonic rule, where ministers were not carefully chosen, the people suffered many grievances, and chaos arose. As governance receded, disorder drew near, and control could no longer be restored.

Thus, to think of the divine is to summon the divine; to think of the Perfected is to summon the Perfected; to think of the Immortal is to summon the Immortal; to think of the Dao is to summon the Dao; to think of wisdom is to summon wisdom. When the sage’s concentrated thoughts turn to the worthy, the spirit of the worthy comes to aid him; when thoughts turn to depravity, the ghosts of fools come to delude him. Whatever a person may contemplate can be summoned—only the excellence or inferiority of what is thought differs.

Therefore, when a superior scholar becomes ruler, he thinks of the divine and Perfected; when a middling scholar becomes ruler, his mind is penetrating and full of wisdom; when an inferior scholar becomes ruler, he cannot think deeply and merely follows fate as it unfolds.

The Perfected One asked: “How can one know whether an emperor’s thoughts are good or evil?”

The Divine Person replied: “It is easily known. When an emperor thinks of benevolence and goodness, auspicious signs appear solely for him, and prophetic texts arise solely for him. Emperors of benevolence and clarity are born of Wood and Fire; those of martial wisdom are born of Metal and Water; those of gentleness and harmony are born of Earth. Heaven’s descending omens never err.”

The Perfected One asked: “In ancient times, extraordinary prophetic texts and rare methods—who was worthy to receive them?”

“Officials and commoners who obtained them presented them to their king. When the emperor’s *qi* of the times was harmonious and good, governance grew ever clearer, Daoist arts and worthy sages emerged to assist him, and the emperor’s Way daily grew stronger. The barbarians were pacified and vanished; he governed with folded arms, punishments ceased of themselves, and the people knew no warfare. Is this not proof of an emperor’s good thoughts? Even without seeing the man, one already knows.”

The Perfected One asked: “How does the Divine Person know this?”

The Divine Person said: “By attaining it without sound. When the ruler desires benevolence and cherishes life, he models the Way of Heaven; when ministers desire gentleness, compliance, and nurturing, they follow the Way of Earth—then good omens appear. Thus Heaven and Earth do not speak yet endure forever; their governance is uniquely divine. The divine and numinous do not speak yet attain long life as Immortals—all through inner illumination and outer obscurity, which is the origin of the ten thousand Ways.

The divine and numinous move in and out without lairs or nests; pure and tranquil, without sound, they lie at ease upon their pillows, and their spiritual radiance arises of itself. How could this not be joyous and auspicious? Those who use their mouths excessively deplete their essence; those who exert their strength excessively weary their bodies; those who employ force excessively harm themselves—from these arise misfortune and calamity. Heed my words and do not think recklessly. Good thoughts may bring virtue, but evil thoughts return to harm oneself. Between safety and danger, the difference is as fine as a hair’s breadth—beware of mixed thoughts.

When a person loses the Dao, their fate is cut off; when one truly understands the Dao’s intent, life may be preserved. Strive to nurture your essence and do not consume yourself. Study under an enlightened teacher, and misfortune and chaos will not arise.”

The Perfected One dared not disregard the Divine Person’s words.

The Divine Person said: “Learners act for themselves, not for others. Thus each should cherish and draw near to themselves. Through long accumulation in studying the Dao, one becomes a divine Perfected One, utterly distinct from the multitude—such are my words.”

The Perfected One asked: “How can one know the efficacy of the Dao?”

The Divine Person said: “Resolve it through an enlightened teacher, practice it in oneself. The body transforms and changes form, entering the same gate as the divine Way, becoming neighbors with the Perfected, sharing a door with the Divine Person. Seek it within yourself—how could misfortune be seen? If one loses the Dao’s intent and instead seeks it in the four wilds, searching in vain, one reaches old age in poverty. Thus severed from the root, one claims the world has no Dao, ever alone in sorrow and suffering—this is the greatest calamity. The great person, losing it, cannot level their governance; the middling scholar, losing it, brings chaos to their lord; the benevolent person, losing it, has no way to act as a worthy; the petty person, losing it, destroys themselves. The conduct of the ancient worthies and sages is the same as today’s; the ruin of the ancient petty people is also the same as today’s—clear evidence indeed.”

The Perfected One asked: “How can one know whether a person will rise or fall?”

The Divine Person said: “When a great person is about to rise, extraordinary texts appear, and the worthy assist in governance. When a household is about to rise, those who seek will find life, and the goodness of their descendants can be known.”

The Perfected One asked: “How can one summon such worthies?”

The Divine Person said: “All through thought. With unceasing concentrated thought, all things come. How wondrous is the Dao’s governance—can one not strive to practice it?”

The Divine Person said: “The Three Bonds and Six Disciplines endure in good fortune because they uphold the Dao and do not lose their governance—thus they are always auspicious. Heaven’s lifespan does not override human wishes. The nature of Wood is benevolence; thinking of benevolence thus summons the East, for the East governs benevolence. The five directions are all like this. All matters under Heaven follow their kind—thus when an emperor thinks of tranquility, his governance is also tranquil, for like calls to like.

The ancients who studied emulated it in themselves; today’s scholars emulate it in others. The ancients studied to secure themselves; today’s scholars pursue superficial ornamentation, not accumulating essence in themselves but accumulating essence in texts—this is to be ignorant of the root.”

*Excerpts from the Tai Ping Jing, Concluding Section of Scroll Two of the Yi Division*
*Beginning of Scroll Three of the Bing Division of the Tai Ping Jing*

Distinguishing between poverty and wealth, when the ruler enacts this, it establishes good fortune—prohibiting the severance of the earth’s lineage to promote the flourishing of men and women, thereby restoring the king’s governance. What is called wealth in the world? What is called poverty? Indeed, those who possess much are wealthy, and those who possess little are poor. Yet your words, while correct, are also fundamentally untrue. Can the deceitful, the false, the thieves, and the bandits truly be called wealthy? Today, the common people are many, and the emperors few—how can this be called poverty?

Wealth, in its meaning, is complete sufficiency. Heaven deems all things fully born as wealth and sufficiency. Thus, in the era of the Upper August, qi emerged, and the twelve thousand things were born in diversity—this was called wealth and sufficiency. In the era of the Middle August, things diminished and could not fully sustain the twelve thousand things, thus it was called minor poverty. In the era of the Lower August, things were even fewer than in the Middle August—this was called great poverty. Without auspicious responses, when good things do not arise, it is extreme poverty. When all things emerge and the earth nourishes them without harm, this is the earth’s wealth; when it cannot nourish things, it is great poverty.

Heaven is the father, earth the mother—when these parents reach extreme poverty, their children grow poorer by the day. In ancient times, the emperor who governed the world with the Dao could bring forth the twelve thousand things—this was the ruler of supreme wealth. When good things fell short by two-thirds, it was the ruler of middle wealth; by one-third, the ruler of lesser wealth. When rare things did not arise, it was the ruler of extreme poverty.

The ancient emperors of the Dao dwelled in seclusion, contemplating virtue and power, and the myriad things were naturally sufficient—was this not joyous? When the emperor practices the Dao, the celestial spirits aid his transformation; when he practices virtue, the earthly spirits aid his governance; when he practices harmony, the human spirits aid his rule; but when he practices ornamentation, it becomes the path of hidden deceit. Thus, deceitful spirits assist him, and his governance runs counter to the will of Heaven, harming the good.

Ruling the world with military force, subduing people through punishment and execution, is like thieves and bandits inflicting harm through execution. The original intent of the emperor’s laws is retribution by kind. Heaven delights in giving life, thus it is called the Lord and Father. Earth delights in tranquility and nourishing the myriad things, thus it is called the Mother. Using the heart to cherish and love all things—this is called benevolence. These two are good, thus they are called teachers and elders.

Greatly aligning with Heaven and Earth, harmonizing yin and yang, with no grievances between men and women, brings timely rain, harmonizes the two qi, and the earth gives birth to the myriad things. When the emperor’s Dao governs, it swiftly brings Great Peace.

If chaste men do not bestow and chaste women do not transform, yin and yang do not unite, and the lineage of the world is extinguished—when two people together sever the lineage of Heaven and Earth, coveting hollow and false reputations, they leave no descendants, losing the true essence. This is the world’s greatest harm. If Heaven were to remain chaste, timely rain would not fall; if Earth were to remain chaste, the myriad things would not be born. Not bestowing, not giving birth—this harm is great indeed.

When Heaven is about to send rain, it first stirs wind and clouds so that people may know. The reason for this is to prompt them to gather and store. Now, as the qi of Great Peace is about to arrive, fearing that people will not cease their evil, it first awakens them. The emperor should model himself on Heaven and Earth, first observing the virtuous Dao in royal affairs.

**The Method for Resolving Karmic Debt:**
Since the opening of Heaven and Earth, emperors, ministers, and the people have borne karmic debt, and this is why teachings have emerged. From emperors and ministers to the common people, all who bear karmic debt pass it to later generations—this is due to their inability to nurture goodness, losing their guiding principles, thus incurring karmic responsibility.

For example, if parents lose virtue and commit wrongs in their village, their descendants will surely be harmed by the village—this is the proof of karmic debt. In ancient times, emperors, ministers, and the people each knew the way to nurture themselves—how could there have been karmic debt?

Heaven does not deceive people: sow millet, and you reap millet; sow wheat, and you reap wheat. It depends on the effort expended, whether the harvest is good or bad. Resolving the enmity of karmic debt for the August Heaven, resolving the calamity of karmic debt for the Earth, resolving the distress of karmic debt for the emperor, resolving the transgressions of karmic debt for the myriad people, resolving the responsibility of karmic debt for the twelve thousand things—there is nothing better for resolving karmic debt than abiding by the One. If one abides by the One for long, Heaven will take pity.

The One is the guiding principle of Heaven and the root of the myriad things. Contemplate its root, and it will extend to its branches. When the sages of old were about to act, they observed the celestial patterns above and examined the earthly principles below, clarifying root and branch, witnessing their evident effects.

The people of the world have four hardships—what are they? A child, born of parents, in youth cannot leave their thoughts of their parents—this is the first hardship. When grown and self-reliant, a woman desires marriage, a man desires a wife, yet they cannot overcome their passions, and their love prevents separation—this is the second hardship. Once in love, they bear children; as husband and wife age, their appearance is no longer lovely, but their young children are lovable and must be raised—this is the third hardship. When the children grow, they no longer need to be raised, but the parents themselves age and do not understand how to conduct themselves—this is the fourth hardship.

After these four hardships, if one can find a wise teacher and contemplate guarding the Dao, it may yet be well. Those of high talent with heavenly mandate may transcend the world; the next may attain longevity; the next may briefly enjoy their bodies. When the hun and po reside beneath the earth, they may yet find joy. Why is this? Beneath the earth, all newly deceased arrive and are questioned about their deeds in life, their records clearly established, and they are held accountable for their actions. Thus, one must prepare in advance for safety and peril.

The ruler should contemplate Great Peace, aligning with the heart of Heaven, so that hun, po, and spirit constantly unite with qi. Those who cannot bring peace to their governance do not align with the heart of Heaven, do not gain Heaven’s favor, and are deemed to have no merit before Heaven. In the end, their hun, po, and spirit will be held solely accountable beneath the earth, uniting with evil qi.

The ancient supreme sage-rulers understood this well, thus they exerted themselves to do good.

The foolish do not ponder deeply, thus in life they incur Heaven’s reproach, and in death they incur Earth’s reproach—how can this not be terrifying? Swiftly transmit my writings so that all under Heaven may practice them, each reflecting on their own essence, their thoughts aligning with the Great Dao. Once they recognize the origin of their transgressions, the burden of inherited responsibility shall be lifted. Heaven and Earth will rejoice greatly, reverting to the ancient age and doubling its blessings.

Heaven is One, yet it acts through Earth as Two—what is the meaning of this? Now Earth is Two, yet it acts through Man as Three—why is this? Earth serves as Heaven’s agent, and Man serves as Earth’s agent. Thus, when Heaven is pleased, it immediately causes all things upon Earth to rejoice. Though Earth nurtures all beings, if goodness prevails, the people dwell in goodness—this is the clear effect of their mutual agency.

The causes of order and chaos are manifold. Those who do not align with Heaven’s heart must return to their root. When human speech proliferates, it too leads to chaos. But if one returns to the root, what cause for concern is there?

Thus, a single word that achieves its purpose is the root. A second word that suffices forms a coherent phrase. A third word that suffices instead becomes an explanation of difficulties, for the farther one strays from truth, the more explanations are needed. A fourth word that suffices instead becomes literary embellishment. A fifth word that suffices instead becomes falsehood. A sixth word that suffices instead leads to failure. A seventh word that suffices instead leads to ruin. An eighth word that suffices instead leads to separation and estrangement, growing ever more distant. A ninth word that suffices instead leads to great chaos. A tenth word that suffices instead leads to destruction and annihilation. Thus, upon reaching ten, one must reform, for further transmission only brings ruin.

In all matters, when destruction occurs, one must return to the root. Therefore, return and hold fast to the One as the origin. Hence, numbers begin with One and end with Ten—this is the natural principle governing order and chaos.

Thus, the sages of antiquity, when consulting the oracle, first divined once: its auspice or inauspice was decisive. By holding to the root, the celestial spirits would descend with their message. A second divination summoned the earthly spirits to speak. A third divination summoned the human spirits to speak. Beyond this, all is deception, unworthy of divination, and the hexagrams lose their accuracy. Human discourse, when excessive, is not to be treasured.

How excellent! The celestial numbers begin with One and end with Ten—why is this? Heaven is One, and below it, Earth is Two. Yin and Yang unite to give birth to all things. The first signs of life emerge as primordial qi arises in the *zi* hour, turns northeast to spread roots in the *jiao* constellation, then moves east to sprout and grow, shifts southeast to develop branches and leaves, turns south to flourish, moves west to ripen, and turns northwest to reach completion. When things come to an end, they must begin anew, thus the *hai* hour: two embracing one, the beginning of the Three Sovereigns. Therefore, *hai* is the kernel, the first coagulation of the seed—hence water begins to congeal in the tenth month. *Ren* means "to bear," for what is borne must grow day by day. Thus, *zi* means "to multiply." When Three achieves the harmony of Yin and Yang’s qi, all is complete, and it returns to the beginning, hence the name *jiazi*. The Dao of Heaven in generating things must circulate fully, uniting the qi of the four seasons and five phases to bring them to completion. Thus, it is rooted in Heaven and Earth, circulating through the eight directions, and the numbers end at Ten.

Question: Of the governance of emperors and feudal lords, which is most excellent?
Answer: To extend compassion without harm, acting as Heaven does—this is most excellent. In governance, nothing surpasses emulating the great image of Heaven. Yet there must be an order of priority. What does this mean?

The highest good is to cherish life, desiring it as urgently as one craves water—only then is it acceptable. Next is to delight in the goodness of others as if it were one’s own. Next is to bestow upon others: when seeing someone in poverty, one should feel their sorrow as keenly as if suffering hunger and cold. Next is to establish laws, ensuring that fear alone deters transgression. Next, for those guilty of grave crimes, governance should prevent them from falling into wrongdoing. Next, when someone commits an offense, if unavoidable, ensure it does not implicate their family or neighbors. Next, if the offense extends to neighbors, one should identify the guilty party while taking care not to sever their lineage. Humans are the stewards of Heaven, Earth, and the divine luminaries. To harm and disrupt the body of Heaven and Earth is to invite profound calamity. Do not bring the burden of inherited responsibility upon descendants. Constantly aspire to Great Peace to dissolve the obstructions of punishment.

I expound for Heaven and Earth, composing this for rulers of supreme virtue, that they may eliminate the burdens of inherited responsibility since the opening of Heaven and Earth. If this discourse is neglected, one will surely incur the resentment of the August Heaven and the Sacred Earth, and bear the burden of responsibility before the enlightened and virtuous rulers of the past—such a transgression would be grave indeed.

I have collated and examined the Daoist scriptures of high, middle, and low antiquity, gathering the wise to read them together and survey the texts of Dao from past and present. If one scripture yields one good precept, record it. If one good technique is found, note it down as the matter arises. One scripture yields one goodness, ten scriptures yield ten goodnesses, a hundred yield a hundred, a thousand yield a thousand, ten thousand yield ten thousand, and a hundred million yield a hundred million goodnesses. Record them accordingly, then assemble the wise to deliberate, removing redundancies. From this, compile the essential texts to fully grasp the profound intent of Heaven, Earth, humanity, and the myriad things in ancient and modern times. Condensing the insights of nine sages—could there be any injustice?

The king’s governance, rejoicing in this, will resolve the inherited burdens of his predecessors. Humans are the foremost of the myriad things. The formless spirit-people, composed of refined qi, are charged with governing primordial qi. The great spirit-people govern Heaven, the perfected people govern Earth, the immortals govern the four seasons, the great Daoists govern the five phases, the sages govern Yin and Yang, the worthies govern documents and receive teachings, ordinary people govern plants and the five grains, and servants govern wealth and goods.

Heaven appoints offices according to nature, never overriding their inherent inclinations—each follows its kind without error. To act contrary invites great harm. Thus, all the common people under Heaven’s charge must comply with this principle. The sages of antiquity deeply understood this, never deviating from Heaven’s intent, thereby gaining Heaven’s favor. The nine ranks each govern with ease, securing Heaven’s favor; when the nine qi harmonize, they bring about Great Peace. These nine matters mutually generate and complete one another—if even one qi fails to harmonize, some will not arrive. If primordial qi is disharmonious, the formless spirit-people will not come. If Heaven’s qi is disharmonious, the great spirit-people will not come. If Earth’s qi is disharmonious, the perfected people will not come. If the four seasons are disharmonious, the immortals will not come. If the five phases are disharmonious, the great Daoists will not come. If Yin and Yang are disharmonious, the sages will not come. If the myriad things are disharmonious, the common people will fall into chaos, goods and wealth will diminish, and servants will flee. When any office fails in its duty, the harm is thus. Obtaining these nine ranks can dispel the inherited burdens of ten thousand generations of kings. These nine ranks ascend to the formless spirit-people and descend to servants—each regulates a single qi.

Therefore, the superior scholar who cultivates the Dao must first consume qi, seeking to harmonize with primordial qi. He should fast in a thatched chamber, avoiding all evil, refining his form daily, and never yielding to desire. Thus, he may move freely between realms, aiding the immortals and perfected in governing Heaven’s primordial qi. Such is the divine scholar, an official of Heaven. Unrestrained and unbound, if he truly attains this, he is called a Heavenly Scholar. Heaven reviews the virtuous, rejoicing greatly, and in turn benefits humanity.

Though one who attains the Dao and departs this world may not serve an immediate purpose, he can harmonize Yin and Yang’s qi to benefit the myriad things. The ancient kings sacrificed to the celestial deities for the sake of these divine officials. All, from sages to servants, have their limits—the highest are the formless spirit-people, the lowest are servants. The spirit-people move by riding qi; thus, where there is qi, there is spirit, and when qi ceases, spirit perishes. This is the luminous decree of August Heaven, by which the governance of human rulers is judged, and the effects of success or failure are made manifest.

The interplay of punishment and virtue is the manifest efficacy of Heaven and Earth’s governance through Yin and Yang spirits, serving as the model for all things and the people. Thus, in the eleventh month, great virtue resides in the *nine-one* position, dwelling beneath the earth. At this time, virtue abides within the chamber, so the inner realm possesses qi, and the myriad things return to it. The *six-four* position, situated in the four wilds, holds the outward form, so the outer realm lacks qi and dissipates. The outer expanse is empty of all things, and the multitudes of scholars and commoners all return, following the king’s virtue into the depths of the Yellow Springs.

In the twelfth month, virtue resides in the *nine-two* position, in the *chou* hour, dwelling within the earth’s center yet to emerge. At this time, virtue abides in the Bright Hall, and the myriad things follow virtue upward but dare not appear, for punishment looms above. In the first month, the *yin* hour, virtue resides in the *nine-three* position, and all things without exception follow its flourishing power, rejoicing in their emergence upon the earth. At this time, virtue dwells in the courtyard.

In the second month, virtue resides in the *nine-four* position, in the *mao* and *si* hours, neither fully departed from the earth nor yet reaching Heaven, but precisely at the boundary. Virtue abides at the gate, so all things delight in peering outward from the gate. In the third month, flourishing virtue resides in the *nine-five* position atop the *chen* hour, reaching the center of Heaven. At this time, virtue abides in the outer pathways, so all things emerge and dwell outside.

In the fourth month, the *si* hour, virtue resides in the *nine-six* position, extending to the six distant boundaries and eight frontiers. Flourishing virtue pervades the eight directions, and the auspicious qi of Yang responds in kind. The teeming living things depart from the four chambers and the wilds. At this time, punishment resides at the roots of the myriad things, dwelling within the inner chamber. The lower chamber is empty, while the upper flourishes, and none fail to delight in following virtue to govern. This is the great manifest efficacy of governance through virtue.

Now, I have heard of employing virtue but have not heard of employing punishment. Yet, in the fifth month, punishment resides in the *six-one* position, in the *wu* hour beneath the earth. The inner realm lacks qi, and the earth below is empty. At this time, punishment abides in the void, and the inner realm is empty of all things, which all dwell outside.

In the sixth month, punishment resides in the *six-two* position, in the *wei* hour, dwelling within the earth’s center yet to emerge.
