At this time, punishment abides in the Bright Hall, its qi within, while virtue’s qi is without. The teeming living things all delight in exposing themselves and returning to flourishing virtue. In the seventh month, punishment resides in the *six-three* position, in the *shen* hour, abiding in the courtyard. The myriad things dare not enter and firmly delight in dwelling outside.

In the eighth month, punishment resides in the *six-four* position, in the *you* hour, not yet reaching the Heavenly boundary. At this time, virtue abides at the gate, and all things delight in peering from the gate, rejoicing in entering and following virtue to return. In the ninth month, punishment resides in the *six-five* position, atop the *xu* hour, reaching the center. At this time, punishment abides in the pathways, and none of the myriad things fail to perish by dawn, following virtue to conceal themselves. Thus, the inner realm flourishes daily, while the outer is empty and desolate.

In the tenth month, punishment resides in the *six-six* position, in the *hai* hour, extending to the six distant boundaries, eight frontiers, and four wilds. The teeming living things all conceal themselves and flee, following virtue’s movement into the Bright Hall. Crawling creatures carry their young within, while the wilds outside are empty of scholars and multitudes. This is not because punishment is favored, but rather that those who employ it are seen as perverse. Yet if the heart inwardly harbors punishment to govern the multitudes, their numbers dwindle daily.

In the fifth month, harboring one measure of punishment within causes one group of the multitudes to rebel. In the sixth month, harboring two measures of punishment causes two groups to rebel. In the seventh month, harboring three measures causes three groups to rebel. In the eighth month, harboring four measures causes four groups to rebel. In the ninth month, harboring five measures causes five groups to rebel. In the tenth month, harboring six measures causes the multitudes of the six directions to rebel. Thus, the outer realm is utterly empty of all things, all fleeing inward—this is the manifest proof.

Therefore, governance through punishment appears reverent outwardly but harbors rebellion within, so the multitudes diminish daily. Conversely, in the eleventh month, harboring one measure of virtue within draws one group of the multitudes inward. In the twelfth month, harboring two measures draws two groups inward. In the first month, harboring three measures draws three groups inward. In the second month, harboring four measures draws four groups inward. In the third month, harboring five measures of flourishing Yang virtue draws five groups of worthy ones inward. From the fourth month onward, the six virtues cause all things to emerge and appear, and none fail to teem and return, both within and without. This is the manifest model of Heaven’s Bright Hall.

In the second and eighth months, virtue and punishment are evenly matched, so the myriad things are half-damaged by cold. Punishment daily harms and kills, inspiring dread and fear, and thus fails to win the people’s strength. The sages of antiquity ruled through virtue and the Dao, not through physical force or punishment. They established models and laws, setting forth teachings and decrees for emperors and kings to follow in governance.

When the kingly Way is about to flourish, it takes its model from virtue; when it is about to decline, it takes its model from punishment. In establishing laws and institutions for emperors and kings, one must first clarify Heaven’s intent, inwardly illuminating the Dao of Yin and Yang—then Great Peace will arrive.

The Heavenly Master thus joins with the August Heaven and Earth, constantly concentrating their essence and thought, their hearts deeply attuned to Heaven and Earth’s intent, like overlapping compasses or interlocking squares, not deviating even by a hair’s breadth. Knowing what Heaven and Earth constantly sorrow over, and foreseeing their great taboos—what are these?

The spirits of Heaven and Earth deeply lament and suffer from people’s disobedience and lack of filial piety. What does this mean? Within Heaven and Earth, the three qi of harmonious balance unite as one family to nurture the myriad things. Heaven governs life and is called Father; Earth governs nurturance and is called Mother; humanity governs governance and is called Child. The Child receives the mandate from the Father and is lovingly nurtured by the Mother. As a child, one must respectfully serve the Father and love the Mother—what does this mean?

The Father’s teachings have their measures and seasons, so he instructs and brings forth life in accordance with the four seasons. Wicked people oppose the Father’s intent, causing Heaven’s qi to lose its governance. This is like a household where the father is angry with his child, and father and child are at odds. Yin overcomes Yang, the lower deceives the upper, ministers neglect their duties, and demonic forces flourish. The positions of Heaven and Earth are like the distinction between male and female in humans—their likes and dislikes are the same. Heaven nurtures human life, and Earth nurtures human form.

Now, all who jointly harm their Father and Mother—how is this so?

The qi of the four seasons is Heaven’s governance in motion, yet people oppose it, thus harming their Father. Earth is their Mother, from whom they receive clothing, food, and nurturance; yet instead of loving and benefiting her, they turn to harm her. Human conduct is most unseemly, defying all reason. They bore into the earth, launching vast earthworks—some digging deep to the Yellow Springs, others several fathoms down. The Mother alone grieves in sorrow, while her many children, utterly lacking in filial reverence, constantly vex her with resentment and stifled distress, yet she has no means to voice her plight. In ancient times, the sages moved with the seasons, yet even they could not fully grasp the intent of Heaven and Earth. Ordinary people, ignorant of the earth, do not perceive her pain and suffering, nor do they sense her influence upon Heaven. Thus, when the Father’s calamities recur, the Mother grows wrathful and ceases to nurture the myriad things. When both Father and Mother are enraged, how can their children escape disaster?

Heaven and Earth are supremely compassionate, yet for the great crime of filial impiety, they grant no pardon—how can one not tremble? Great earthworks bring great disasters; small earthworks bring small disasters. It is the Earth’s wrath that summons the spirits to generate such calamities. If earthworks do not immediately result in disaster, it is because the land is good and kind. Where disaster strikes, the land is fierce and malevolent. The ruler’s harm extends even to distant lands—what does this mean? It is like a good and kind person who, though wronged, endures for a time, yet never forgets the grievance. The wicked cannot endure even for a moment before disaster befalls them.

The Earth’s body is vast, while humans, in comparison, are as small as dust. How can their digging possibly cause harm? Yet consider this: a person stands a fathom tall, ten spans in girth, and in the crevices of their teeth dwell tiny, insignificant worms. When these worms gnaw at the teeth, causing great pain, the person wails for a long time, and the teeth eventually fall out entirely. The disparity between humans and Heaven and Earth is like that between these worms and a person. Even if one’s teeth were as hard as metal or stone, these tiny, fleshy worms could still cause such harm. Now, if a strong and mighty man were powerless to resist a pint of mites gnawing at him, he would be stricken with pain and unable to lie down—severe cases would confine him to bed. Even fleas, lice, and other tiny creatures, when gathered in great numbers, can torment a person, causing restlessness and sores. Parasitic worms can kill, while fleas and lice bring only vexation and discomfort. The harm humans inflict upon Heaven and Earth is no different.

To dig into the earth and reach the springs is to draw the Earth’s blood; to uncover stone is to expose her bones; soil is her flesh. To take her blood, break her bones, and pierce her flesh, then cast bricks, stones, and hardwood into her depths—these are wounds upon her body. Earth is the Mother of all things, yet she suffers such afflictions—how can she remain at peace?

All who dwell upon the Mother’s body have their own hidden vulnerabilities. Digging one foot into the earth reaches the realm touched by the sun, where qi belongs to Heaven. Two feet down lies the realm where things grow, where qi is harmonious. Three feet down enters the Earth’s yin body, and beyond this, all digging harms her form.

To equalize virtue and power, to adjust values and prices, is to open the hearts of the foolish. Now, if I were to bestow upon you a thousand pounds of gold to offer to the state, would this win the favor of Heaven and Earth, regulate yin and yang, eradicate all disasters, grant the emperor long life, and bring about great peace? Or if I were to present a jade disc of myriad hues to the state, treasuring and hoarding it as the world’s rarest gem—would this cause the qi of the Six Directions to harmonize fully, summoning all auspicious signs, driving back the barbarians, and ensuring no harm for ten thousand miles?

I have now fully expounded the Way to you. By following it, the emperor can secure the favor of Heaven and Earth, delighting all the spirits under heaven. Even the crawling and creeping creatures will rejoice, the barbarians will retreat in submission, auspicious signs will appear in full, disasters will vanish entirely, the state’s lifespan will be prolonged, and the people will enjoy long life.

If you truly embrace goodness and practice the teachings of this text, pondering its essential meaning, all will respond as if in echo. It is like aligning a compass with a square—there will be no deviation.

To give a state a thousand pounds of gold is not as valuable as imparting a single essential word to bring about great peace, eliminate disasters, and secure the realm. Ancient emperors never lacked for wealth or goods; what they lacked were *shi*—men of worth. They grieved that great sages did not come, that the people did not gather, and that all sought to attach themselves to foreign lands, growing ever more distant. This is what fails to accord with the will of August Heaven.

Even if one were to amass gold, jade, and rare treasures stretching a thousand miles and towering to the heavens, it would never attract the great sages, immortals, or divine beings to aid the emperor’s governance. Yet this text is attended by the divine officials of the Three Luminaries, who constantly observe and illuminate it.

The conduct of the ruler’s ministers and people should be such that they constantly worry for their sovereign day and night. Their desire to bring peace stems from their concern for his suffering, and they rejoice when the emperor governs effortlessly, while the people and ministers emulate his filial piety and kindness.

When the ruler aligns with the heart of Heaven above and the intent of Earth below, and the central realm ensures that all people are reverent, without grievances or resentment, even the crawling creatures will turn toward virtue. All things will find their proper place, Heaven and Earth will be harmonious and joyful, and the ruler’s lifespan will be extended. From the eldest to the youngest, none will commit evil in the realm. They will cherish their ruler, fearing his aging, and Heaven and Earth will surely send divine beings bearing elixirs to instruct the emperor in their use, granting him boundless longevity.

What, then, is the conduct of the finest ministers and children? The foremost conduct of a filial child is this: when their parents grow old and frail, they dwell alone in quiet contemplation, pondering how to obtain the art of immortality to serve them. They scorn wealth and treasure the Way, seeking only to sustain life. They play the zither and sing to bring joy to their parents, guiding their hearts toward the Dao. They delight in remaining with them for all time, never knowing old age.

Ever seeking rare methods, they journey to distant lands, their sincerity moving Heaven, their efforts unceasing until their strength is spent. With clothing and food just sufficient for themselves, they no longer amass treasures for posterity, lest their parents be burdened with guarding them. Such is the foremost conduct of the finest filial child.

When the finest disciples receive the Dao and virtue from their masters, mindful of the grace that enabled their growth into adulthood, they remain ever in the company of the wise and gentle, never straying from their ranks. Some attain rank and position to repay their parents; others delve deeply into the savor of the Dao, mastering the art of self-nurturance. All people are born of their parents, attain the completion of Dao and virtue through their masters, and gain honor and esteem from their rulers. Dwelling alone, they ponder how their ruler, master, and father will age, and how to repay them. They constantly strive to seek rare methods and extraordinary texts for their masters, that they may requite their merit. Some further study under the worthy, entrusting their masters to them and speaking on their behalf. Some enable their superiors to become the state’s finest aides, benefiting the emperor’s governance. Such are the noble disciples of the High Antiquity.

The Three Sovereigns and supreme sages of old overcame others through the utmost Dao and governance by virtue, never by might, severity, cunning, or deceit. Those who overcome others through might, severity, cunning, deceit, and punishment are but bandits and thieves. Bandits and thieves rely solely on these to subdue others—how then do the noble distinguish themselves, making their difference clear and manifest?

Thus, rulers of Dao and virtue ever regard severity, might, cunning, and deceit as the conduct of bandits and thieves. The Celestial Master’s writings often speak of the *qi* of the Supreme August and the advent of Great Peace—what does this mean? The sages established laws in accordance with symbolic meaning, abiding in the One and delighting in divination above all. *Divination* means inquiry. To constantly delight in acting above and inquiring without cease is the loftiest path. Thus, the character *shang* (上, "above") is a single stroke rising upward with *bu* (卜, "divination"); the character *xia* (下, "below") is a single stroke descending with *bu*. Constant inquiry and descent lead to the lowest extreme, so those who delight in descending further can no longer ascend.

The character *huang* (皇, "august") means "to become king in a single day." The upper *yi* (一, "one") is the number of Heaven; attaining the One, one gains the illumination of the sun, and with great brightness, becomes king. The One and the sun-king combine to form *huang*. The One is Heaven, and Heaven is also the ruler. The sun embodies the ruler’s virtue, and the king is also the ruler’s superior. These three rulers together form *huang*, signifying resplendent virtue, foremost under Heaven, with none above.

*Tai* (太) means "great," signifying accumulation as vast as Heaven, with nothing greater than Heaven. *Ping* (平, "peace") means governing with supreme impartiality, ordering all affairs so that none remain unbalanced. It is like the earth, which abides below and upholds equilibrium. It is like sowing and reaping: planting good yields good, planting evil yields evil; toil in cultivation brings a bountiful harvest in return. Heaven’s *qi* delights in descending, Earth’s *qi* delights in ascending; the two *qi* interpenetrate to form the harmonious *qi* of the center, mutually receiving and nurturing the myriad things without harm. Thus is it called *Great Peace*.

When the *qi* of Heaven and Earth harmonize as one, they jointly engender the myriad things. When man and woman unite in heart, they bear children. When father, mother, and child unite in heart, they form a household. When ruler, minister, and people unite in heart, they form a state. The emperor is Heaven’s noble child; as a child heeds his father’s teachings, he should act in accordance, alleviating Heaven and Earth’s concerns and thereby gaining their protection. Thus, he constantly strives to act with diligence.

If celestial patterns do not manifest, it is because the times know order and disorder, and the Dao does not emerge in vain. The emperors of old perceived the subtle and knew the manifest; acting in accordance with the moment and following the *qi*, they attained Heaven’s favor, their intentions ever auspicious. To act contrary brings discord between water and drought, *qi* in conflict and opposition, disasters accumulating into unceasing calamities and prodigies—these are called *portents and anomalies*. The multitude of worthies grow confused, unaware of the Dao of compliance and opposition. Were they to know it, when encountering Great Peace, they would govern with ease; when encountering middling peace, they would act with effort; when encountering disorder, they would rely on the Dao to aid and prepare themselves. It is like preparing for summer at the summer solstice and for winter at the winter solstice—this is the meaning.

The Dao of Heaven moves in constant cycles; to comply with it brings prosperity and flourishing, to oppose it brings peril and ruin. When the Dao of Heaven contends, its mandate is harmed; when the sun and moon lose their measure, the constellations move in disorder. Those who can employ it act with their own strength, daring not conceal the worthy, illuminating above and below, and enabling all to find peace.

Moxibustion and acupuncture serve to harmonize and pacify the three hundred and sixty meridians, unblocking the *qi* of yin and yang to dispel harm. The three hundred and sixty meridians correspond to the three hundred and sixty days of the year, each meridian governing a day, moving in accordance with the four seasons and five phases, circulating throughout the body, converging within the crown of the head, and striking within the viscera. All respond to the four seasons in their movements; when ill, they fail to conform to their measures, their coming and going losing regularity, sometimes binding, sometimes injuring, sometimes flowing smoothly, sometimes reversing. Thus, they must be treated.

Fire is the essence of the Great Yang, the clarity of impartial justice, used to examine treachery and eliminate harm and evil. Acupuncture is the essence of the Lesser Yin, the substance of Venus, used with righteousness to cut and strike. When treatment succeeds in all one hundred cases, or in ten out of ten, this is the celestial canon of meridians and apocrypha; when truly in accord with the meridians, the spirits are commanded. When treatment succeeds in nine out of ten, missing one, and in harmony with the meridians, the essence is commanded. When treatment succeeds in eight out of ten, it is the human canon; human intention commands. Below this, illness cannot be treated, and harm may instead result. To treat the *jia* meridian when the *yi* meridian is afflicted is called *delirium*, failing to recognize the meridian’s solitary injury and severance.

Thus, to delight in knowing whether the celestial Dao is spiritually responsive or not is to place a single patient before oneself, naming it the *root text of the meridians*—like the root text of the scriptures and Dao—enabling the multitude of worthies to recognize the illness. Some excel in the upper, some in the lower; the three hundred and sixty meridians each have their insights. Taking the actions in which they commonly excel, the therapeutic methods are recorded: those that succeed in ten out of ten are correct, while all others are not.

Gathering the collective practices of healing and deeming those that cure as scripture ensures that none among the treated remain without resolution. My Dao is like the cyclical progression of *jiazi* and *yichou*, the six *jia* phases succeeding one another, the Five Agents turning in mutual accord, the four seasons revolving to return to their origin. Though the scrolls may be numerous, each has its recordable essence—like the human body, where head and feet serve one another in turn. One word omitted gives rise to another; the worthy follow in succession to lend support. Harmonizing yin and yang in speech, the outer and inner correspond as if by compass and square. At first recitation, it may seem tasteless, but with prolonged reflection and unwavering devotion, verification will come. Disasters depart from the body, spirit returns to gather, and people naturally become prudent and free of malevolence, living without punishment or penalty, while the transformative power of the Dao reaches its utmost beauty.

By clearly following my text, one averts blame and wards off calamity; calamity ceases of itself, and the people naturally attain longevity. The origin, having never obtained its root, knows no end or beginning. When ten out of ten correspond, it is the scripture of *Taiyang*. When nine out of ten correspond, it is the scripture of *Taiyin*. When eight out of ten correspond, it is the scripture of *Zhonghe*. When seven out of ten correspond, it is the scripture of *Poruination*. When six out of ten correspond, it is the scripture of *Excess*. When five out of ten correspond, it is the scripture of *Ignorance*—this may be called a text of half-fortune and half-misfortune. Fourteen out of ten is a perverse text. Thirteen out of ten is a text of great chaos. Twelve out of ten is an abandoned text. Eleven out of ten is a text of dissipation. From seventeen out of ten downward, it is unusable—a text that misleads people. The extent of harm inflicted will in turn harm the practitioner. Prolonged misuse without cessation violates the law, leading to the extinction of posterity—this is the text of ten out of ten.

Those who delight in attaining its truth need only observe the sacred words of the sages of high antiquity, the sages of middle antiquity, and the sages of later antiquity. By harmonizing their speech and examining their deeds, it can be known. Further, reflect on the Daoist scriptures of high antiquity, middle antiquity, and later antiquity; when the three are united by kindred resonance, it becomes knowable once more. All written texts are the discourse of Heaven—why then do they heal in their time? If one can master their words and rectify their speech, principle is attained; if not rectified, obscurity and chaos ensue. Correct speech and detailed discourse must lead to goodness, while ominous speech and words must bring resentment.

To attain goodness, one need only rectify the root. When the root is rectified, it aligns with celestial patterns and accords with the sacred words. A second revolution aligns with heavenly principle, a third becomes human culture, and a fourth becomes the myriad things. Yet when the myriad things arise, superficial flourishes lead to chaos and ruin. When celestial patterns emerge, they serve to examine the primordial rectitude of the origin, removing excess and establishing its essence. Clarifying the principles of all texts is the Dao of Heaven. Those who grasp correct speech align with the intent of Heaven. Perversity invites malevolent qi, causing Heaven and Earth to lose their harmony, the myriad things to lose their proper places, and emperors and kings to suffer anxious toil, leading to further disorder. Thus, one must urgently examine and rectify it.

From reflection to reflection, from antiquity to the present, all has been fully prepared. The reproaches of spirits and deities are not like those of ordinary people, which can be easily evaded or escaped. By winning the favor of spirits and deities, one can resolve the worries of the world, pacify emperors and kings, and ensure that the myriad things each attain their proper place. I uphold the Three Realities; the qi of *Taiping* arrives, deceit and falsehood depart, and treachery and cunning are extinguished.

The Perfected One asked: How many great urgencies are there in the world? How many minor urgencies? How many things bring misfortune and calamity yet are not urgent?

The Divine Person replied: One should refine oneself and speak in full. Generally, what is put to use in the world is urgent; what is not put to use is not urgent.

The Divine Person said: This appears correct but is not. There are things that must always be urgent and cannot be abandoned; abandoning them would leave the world extinct and devoid of people. Those principles that harmonize and coalesce without name are the great urgencies. Among the world’s great urgencies, there are two; among minor urgencies, there is one. All else is not urgent—it merely wearies the ears and eyes of people, inviting calamity, destroying families, and ruining states. Or it may sever posterity, all from attending to non-urgent affairs and thereby bringing such disasters.

Thus, when a person is born and receives their mandate, they partake of the body of Heaven and Earth, embracing primordial qi in spontaneity. Without drinking or eating, they live by inhaling and exhaling the qi of yin and yang, unaware of hunger or thirst. Over time, they drift far from the spiritual Dao and gradually lose their root. Later generations, ignorant of the true Dao, daily drift toward falsity, becoming subject to hunger and thirst. Without drink or food, they die—this is the first great urgency. Heaven and Earth, in their compassion, together produce things that can be consumed. Yet having eaten and drunk, one falls under the governance of yin and yang, subject to transmission, unable to centrally govern the continuity of Heaven and Earth. Transmission should mirror Heaven and Earth: one yin, one yang; one man, one woman—only then can generation continue.

When yin reaches its extreme, yang is born; when yang reaches its extreme, yin is born. Yin and yang transmit to one another like cold and heat, a principle of spontaneity. Thus they can generate one another, perpetuating the continuity of Heaven and Earth through the ages. If the continuity of Heaven and Earth is severed, what becomes of husband and wife, father and son, ruler and minister, master and disciple? The one who comprehends the teachings of Heaven assists the emperor in transforming and completing the world. Thus, food and drink and the union of man and woman are mutually necessary—these are the two great urgencies.

Clothing is that on which one depends. With clothing, the worthy are born; without it, the unworthy arise. Thus, clothing serves to ward off harm. Therefore, the sagely emperors and enlightened kings of antiquity did not imitate the colors of dark and yellow but merely protected against cold and heat. The continuity of yin and yang in food and drink must not be severed; severing it would leave the world without the Dao of ruler and minister, father and son. Upholding these three, one completes the celestial years, transmits the celestial continuity, and though it ends, it begins anew, without end.

The sages of antiquity governed by this principle; all else is not urgent but merely invites calamity. Man is Heaven, woman is Earth, and clothing and food are *Zhonghe*. Beyond these three, all else is false and unnecessary for life—indeed, it often brings calamity and treachery, disrupts governance and balance, prevents the arrival of harmonious qi, causes the Dao of Heaven to go awry, and weighs heavily on the concerns of the noble person.

The six passions that delight the heart cannot be restrained by man; yielding to them invites calamity. The noble lose their governance, the petty spawn thoughts of theft and plunder, families perish, and states fall—never has this not arisen from indulgence in what is not urgent. The world grows impoverished, beset by sorrow, suffering, and disasters. Inferiors deceive their superiors, and daily they drift toward extravagance, thus inviting sorrow and suffering, failing to complete their celestial years. This compels the young to ceaseless toil, mountains and rivers are drained, primordial qi is severed, earthly qi weakens, and the nurturing of the myriad things falters. Heaven’s disasters and transformations follow, the people gradually dwindle, and deceit and falsehood arise anew.

Such is the harm wrought by what is not urgent, yet men seek to please their eyes and ears without awakening to the profound and vast perils. The Perfected One again asked the Divine Person: When a filial son serves his parents, after their passing does he serve them as he did in life? Or is there a difference? To serve them more than in life, or less?

Man is born of his parents, grows to maturity, and when he sees them depart, never to return, he can no longer receive their teachings and admonitions. Yet in his comings and goings, he may still repay them; his thoughts and imaginings cannot cease. To serve them more than in life—is this not excessive?

The Divine Person replied: Your words are but the filial speech of the common world, not the intent of the Great Dao. Man in life resembles Heaven and belongs to Heaven; man in death resembles Earth and belongs to Earth. Heaven is the father; Earth is the mother. One does not serve the mother more than the father. Life is yang; death is yin. One does not serve yin more than yang. Yang is the Way of the ruler; yin is the Way of the minister. One does not serve the minister more than the ruler. To serve yin more than yang is to cause the qi of yin and yang to rebel, giving rise to disasters. To serve the lesser more than the greater is to cause governance to rebel, inviting great calamity.

When yin qi prevails over yang, inferiors deceive their superiors, ghosts and malevolent spirits flourish, and though men walk by day, epidemics never cease. Yang qi is obstructed, the Way of the ruler declines, and the Way of the minister grows strong. Thus, the enlightened emperors and kings of antiquity exalted yang as paramount and humbled yin as their duty.

The sun is yang; the night is yin. When the sun is long, the night is short; when the night is long, the sun is short. When the sun is abundant, living men thrive; when the night is abundant, ghosts and spirits thrive. Man accompanies the sun; ghosts accompany the stars. The sun is yang; the stars are yin. Thus, when the sun appears, the stars flee; when the stars appear, the sun retreats. When yin prevails, ghosts and spirits bring harm—such is the harm wrought by yin.

In high antiquity, men governed mourning with sincerity alone, and their funerary rites did not exceed those of life. Human hearts were pure and simple, and illness was rare. In middle antiquity, governance gradually lost its standards, drifting toward extravagance. Resources were exhausted for funerary rites, and sacrifices grew lavish. Ghosts and spirits multiplied, the people suffered frequent epidemics, and malevolent spirits wrought havoc without end. In later antiquity, sacrifices to other spirits flourished, exalting yin. Serving ghosts and spirits harmed the living, ministers usurped the ruler’s authority, women dominated households, warfare erupted violently, deceit and flattery arose daily, and governance decayed. The Way of the ruler was no longer practiced. All this arose from exalting yin over yang, which the Way of Heaven abhors, bringing forth these disasters and misfortunes. Can one not be cautious?

The Master inscribed the text. The Master said: My name is "Eleven [with *ming* as the limit]." *Bingwu* and *dingsi* are the ancestral beginnings. Four mouths govern the principles of the myriad things. The child’s cap uses the corner to enliven its right. The hidden dragon must not be used; *kan* is the record. Those who behold it live long, dwelling [between Heaven and Earth] and nothing more. Governing a million people, one may await immortality. Those who skillfully heal illness must not act recklessly. Rejoicing in the marketplace of Chang’an, one may make men’s lives as long as the Queen Mother of the West, like the four seasons cycling endlessly. The ninety-character text is transmitted to the fangshi.

The Perfected One asked the Divine Person: I do not yet grasp the meaning and direction of the ninety-character text on life previously bestowed. I wish for a thorough explanation to bequeath to later generations, that it may be preserved and not forgotten.

The Divine Person replied: I will explain it to you directly. The Master said: My name is "Eleven, with *ming* as the limit." The Master refers to the divine teacher of the August Heaven. *Yue* means "words." I now speak the correct words of Heaven, having been personally sent down to fully expound them to emperors, kings, and the myriad people, resolving the karmic retributions of bearing and shouldering across billions of generations.

*Wu* means "I," the divine messenger urgently dispatched by Heaven. Today, the disasters of bearing and shouldering flow in four directions. From their very roots to their later principles, all lose their governance, with no means to halt or sever them. They harm one another, causing profound calamity, which Heaven regards with grave concern.

*Zi* refers to the characters now arrayed in the celestial text, accumulated in writing. *Shi* means that the text and the celestial truth are sincere and aligned, tenfold without error, not a single deception. Those who obtain it and are wise will deeply reflect: their ancestors all bore karmic burdens. If these are not halted, the misfortunes of bearing and shouldering, great and small, will all be removed.

*Yi* is the essential principle, the correct path to begin with guarding the One. Guarding the One without cease, one’s brightness grows daily, and Heaven’s confusion is dispelled. *Ming* is the limit; the limit is sufficiency. Sufficiency means that for those who practice this Way, each day brings benefit, shining brightly, no longer shrouded in darkness and ignorance.

*Shiyi* is the scholar. *Ming* as the limit is red. Red qi refers to this, which will again flourish in great brightness. The limit is the sufficiency of the myriad things. When the myriad things first sprout, they straighten their roots to grow from their foundation. Practicing this Way, its method returns to the primordial qi, attaining the heart of Heaven and Earth. It is the first and finest, governance that accords with the Way of the Supreme Sovereign.

*Bingwu* and *dingsi* are fire, red.

The *bingwu* day is pure yang; the *dingsi* day is pure yin. Yin and yang govern harmony, and when yang qi returns to harmonious union, all under Heaven accords with it. Those who act do so for the benefit of emperors and kings; yin brings misfortune and harm.

The *zu* is the ancestor, the first, symbolizing the virtue of the Three Sovereigns. The *shi* is the return to the original beginning. Practicing this Way is to revert to the transformation of the Three Sovereigns above.

Four mouths govern the ordering of the myriad things. "Four and obtaining the mouth" refers to speech. All who daily recite my writings will obtain the celestial orthodox script and characters. When their aspirations align, they unite with the heart of Heaven, enabling the myriad things to each find their proper place without further disorder—hence the ordering of the myriad things.

The child’s headband uses horn to govern the right: this is recitation. Reciting this scripture without cease, all matters will suddenly be rectified. Above, one gains the heart of Heaven, ever joyful, without further betrayal.

The *qianlong* does not act; *kan* serves as the guiding principle. The *qianlong* is Heaven’s yang qi, returning to the initial nine, the *jiazi* year’s winter solstice day, when Heaven and Earth first arise. The dragon is the lesser yang of the east, the spirit of wood. Thus, the Dao of Heaven follows wood to generate the fire phase. When things are about to flourish, they must first open their gates and doors.

When the true person reaches the appointed month, they should reveal this scripture in a place of luminous clarity. *Kai* means to open, to make unimpeded. Opening to the south further purifies and expands the yang qi, dissolving the accumulated misfortunes of *chengfu*. *Qian* means to conceal. The Dao, having reached its destination, returns to hiddenness. *Wu yong* means "do not dare" or "not yet." Those who first see the text do not yet know how to practice it. *Yong* means to govern, to act.

Today, this scripture should be used to eliminate disasters. In the *xuanjia* year, it should be employed, yet at that time, rulers may not deeply grasp its meaning and thus fail to apply it. Hence, "do not act" means that Heaven does not yet dare to entrust sole faith in it for immediate implementation. Those who believe and apply it will see affairs respond like an echo, serving as clear proof that it accords with the Dao of Heaven.

*Kan* as the guiding principle refers to *zi* as *kan*. *Jia* is Heaven’s guiding rope, the rope being yang. *Kan* is water, yin, the guiding principle. Thus, Heaven and Earth constantly unite their guiding ropes and principles. In the initial *xuanjiazi*, this scripture emerges for virtuous rulers to govern and transform, establishing guiding principles—hence *kan* as the guiding principle.

This is the scripture of the Supreme Sovereign above, revealed for virtuous rulers below as the true canon to sever evil. With *xuanjia* as the beginning and *zi* as the root, it is thus arranged in sequence by *jiazi*. Those who obtain and see it will enjoy long life.

The *ren zheng* refers to the human ruler, the singular emperor or king. Those of superior virtue easily awaken and know to practice the scripture of the Way. Relying on auspicious signs, they do not doubt the Dao of Heaven. Deeply grasping its meaning, they attain longevity, fulfilling their destined lifespan.

*Chang* means boundless; *jiu* means to endure, to dwell between Heaven and Earth and live. Dwelling between Heaven and Earth, one should study the true Dao. Florid and ornate writings cannot grant enduring life. All the accumulated misfortunes of *chengfu* stem from the lack of a substantive Dao—today, these are severed.

Governing the myriad people, immortality may be awaited, for its principle is correct. Heaven uses this scripture to rectify the hearts of all worthies, each ordering their illnesses, guarding the true and expelling the false. "Immortality may be awaited" means that when all under Heaven hear of the true Dao, they will swiftly and entirely cast off [falsehoods], aiding the virtuous ruler in governing with the true Dao to enliven people—hence immortality may be awaited.

Those who skillfully govern illness must not deceive or endanger. All people are foolish, neglecting the spirits of their bodies and indulging in deceptive and false writings. Without cause, they endanger themselves, incurring Heaven’s severe punishment and bearing the great responsibility of *chengfu*. Thus, Heaven causes them to abandon florid writings and each guard the true and real, preserving their daily efforts to practice, ensuring lasting benefit without further deception or peril.

"Joy in the marketplace of Chang’an." Joy is the supreme joy when the qi of the Supreme Sovereign’s Great Peace arrives. Alas! Its virtue is vast and unmatched. *Chang* means that practicing this Way, one’s virtue is good and boundless. *An* means no further peril or ruin. Those who practice this Way will see the obligations of *chengfu* between Heaven and Earth entirely dispelled, achieving lasting peace, vast and unburdened, without further sorrow.

The *shi* (marketplace) is where Heaven gathers people together. Practicing this scripture, the nation’s people will flourish like those in a bustling city. "Enabling longevity like the Queen Mother of the West" means enabling people—referring to emperors and kings of great virtue who delight in practicing the correct writings. *Ruo* means to follow. Those who greatly follow my writings will align with the Dao of Heaven, attaining great fortune without misfortune.

*Xi* (west) means that all people nest the true Dao in their hearts. *Wang* (king) means that the emperor, practicing the Dao of Heaven, will greatly prosper and reign. Its principle is good, supreme. *Mu* (mother) is the proof of longevity, the elder of spirits. It is like the four seasons returning to their beginning.

*Bi* (comparison) is like the transmission of the four seasons, mutually generating and completing one another without further harm. Its principle is without punishment. Ninety-character strategies are transmitted to the *fangshi*.

Nine is the ultimate; practicing this Way, one’s virtue ultimately harmonizes with the heart of Heaven and Earth, yin and yang, and the myriad things. Ten is the mutual resonance of tens, without contrived writings. *Zi* (characters) refers to the celestial writings above and below, circulating and pervading the Dao to completion. *Chuan* (transmission) means trust; thus, writings are made to preserve the talismanic trust and transmit it.

*Fang* is great rectitude. Holding this Way and hastening to entrust it to a virtuous ruler can dispel the misfortunes of *chengfu*, and its principle will achieve great rectitude.

The *shi* (士) refers to those of unwavering resolve and singular purpose. Such individuals of singular purpose possess upright hearts and are receptive to teaching and instruction; sending them to transmit this Way, the efficacy of my strategies shall become manifest.

Heaven admonishes through celestial writings. When Heaven offers minor admonitions, its countenance alters; when major admonitions arise, Heaven trembles and splits. If its admonitions go unheeded, destruction follows. The Three Luminaries—when minor admonitions occur, minor affairs cause the stars to change hue; when major admonitions arise, the Three Luminaries lose their proper measure and dim. If unheeded, destruction follows. Earth—when minor admonitions occur, it quakes and sways; when major admonitions arise, the land collapses and the earth splits. If unheeded, destruction follows. The Five Phases—when minor admonitions occur, disasters arise; when major admonitions arise, the Wood Phase brings insects that kill people, the Fire Phase brings poison that kills people, the Metal Phase brings tigers and wolves that kill people, the Water Phase brings aquatic creatures that kill people, and the Earth Phase brings officials and commoners to cruelly harm and kill one another. If unheeded, destruction follows. The Four Seasons—when minor admonitions occur, cold and heat fall out of balance; when major admonitions arise, cold and heat reverse their positions, and the seasons lose all proper order. If unheeded, destruction follows. The thirty-six *jingqi*—when minor admonitions arise together, disorder erupts, and pests emerge, some flying, some crawling; clouds and winds multiply yet bring no rain, leaving emptiness without substance. When major admonitions arise, floods and droughts lose all measure, killing and harming the myriad things and the people. If unheeded, destruction follows. Flying and crawling creatures—when minor admonitions occur, they harm people; when major admonitions arise, birds and beasts devour people, and locusts swarm in great numbers. If unheeded, destruction follows. Ghosts, spirits, and numinous beings—when minor admonitions occur, they rise up to afflict and sicken the people; when major admonitions arise, they bring execution and the extermination of entire households. If unheeded, destruction follows. The Six Directions—when minor admonitions occur, winds and rains erupt in chaos, raging and venomous, harming the people. When major admonitions arise, they impose tyranny beyond reason, causing stones to fly from the earth, shaking the pillars of Heaven, shattering houses, and moving mountains and hills. If unheeded, destruction follows. The voices of Heaven and Earth—when minor admonitions occur, thunder and lightning grow slightly fierce; when major admonitions arise, thunderbolts strike repeatedly. If unheeded, destruction follows. Officials and commoners—when minor admonitions occur, their countenances change; when major admonitions arise, they inflict much harm and violence. If unheeded, destruction follows.

When Heaven and Earth and the Six Directions of the Eight Extremities all issue major admonitions, seeking rectification, the writings of the Yellow River and Luo River emerge. Heaven’s luminosity bears witness to the world, and the *Ruiying Shu* (Record of Auspicious Responses) appears to admonish and rectify the ruler. The world responds in unison; if unheeded, destruction follows.

The cycles of the celestial Dao converge when their time arrives, and the sequence resumes in due order. Thus, the sages and worthies of antiquity pondered day and night without dare of slackening. Losing even a hair’s breadth, they perceived the subtle and knew the manifest, never straying from the heart of August Heaven. Therefore, they preserved their persons, pacified their people, nourished the myriad things, and knew no peril or destruction. Calamities and misfortunes could not approach, for their plans and calculations aligned with the intent of Heaven.

What Heaven aids, it aids those who are easy to instruct, those of utmost sincerity, those who are reverent and compliant, those who are easy to enlighten, and those who are vigilant. Heaven’s favor toward emperors and kings is most profound. Yet when myriad errors and changes accumulate to this point, and its teachings go unheeded, it abandons them to their fate. The spirits of Heaven and Earth no longer offer admonitions for rectification. Disasters and anomalies increase daily, the people dwindle and decline, and their proper roles are lost.

The sagely emperors and enlightened kings of antiquity, from dawn to dusk, governed with effortless grace. They deeply pondered and examined the heart of Heaven, never daring to stray from it. Thus, they served August Heaven as a father, August Earth as a mother, the sun as an elder brother, and the moon as an elder sister. They rectified the celestial patterns, preserved the Five Phases, followed the Four Seasons, and observed their movements to reflect upon and correct their own conduct, thereby knowing their gains and losses.

*Excerpt from the Third Scroll of the Bing Section of the* Taiping Jing *Abstract Concluded*
*(Note: The character* huo *活, "active/living," was originally miswritten as* zhi *治, "to govern." Corrected according to the "Jie Shi Ce Shu Jue" section of the original text. See the collated edition.)*

#2 *‘Million’* originally miswritten as *‘hundred regions’*; corrected according to the scripture.

**Abstract from the Fourth Scroll of the Ding Section of the** *Taiping Jing*: *The Diagram of the Womb and Embryo, Yin and Yang’s Compass and Square, and the Rectification of Conduct to Dissolve Evil*

The divine being spoke, the perfected one entered within. Child, you have already understood—diminish the self, and your intent shall be fulfilled.
Externally, principle rectifies itself. With eyes closed, gaze inward to commune with the spirits.
Speak not, and you align with the Dao. Yin and Yang mutually enfold, sealed by Heaven.
The art of long life may open your eyes.

Child, do not harden your bowels; rather, harmonize and expand.
Heaven and Earth receive harmony like the deaf and blind.
To know its intent, observe the child within the womb.
Abstain from food for ten months, and the spirits will commune.
The natural Dao has no superior—without seeing, qi dwells in the twelvefold abode.

Thus, returning to infancy averts misfortune.
Aging reverses to youth, uniting with the Dao.
Therefore, the twelvefold image is drawn:
The upright attain goodness; the unworthy alone meet misfortune.
The Dao of Heaven endures, never lost or perishing.
Its form cycles like the four seasons, returning home.
Aging reverses to beginnings—hence, long life.

Child, ponder its intent without deviation.
Accumulate virtue, amass conduct, and the Dao will naturally form.
Talent falls short of effort; the Dao returns to its person.
If not its person, the Dao does not act in vain.
The Dao is like the wind—silently abiding beside you.
Use it, and it exists; neglect it, and it vanishes.

The worthy have their dwelling; the unworthy, their domain.
Life and death reside in the body, ever fixed in conduct.
Heaven commits no error—humans bring ruin upon themselves.
Ponder its intent carefully; act not recklessly.

Heaven bestows long life upon those who guard the Dao and exert effort.
Humans refuse to do so—hence, they incline toward death.
Remember my admonition: the Dao, transmitted to its person, is easily practiced.
The sages of antiquity passed down the Dao, swearing blood oaths.
The Dao of Heaven is weighty; fools treat it lightly.

The Dao is the teacher of the ten thousand things.
Those who attain it are enlightened; those who lose it are deluded.
Though Heaven and Earth are vast, they do not lose even a hair’s breadth.
The wise and sagely nurture themselves to compare with the spirits.
Their discourse unites the governance of Yin and Yang, the pivot of Heaven and Earth.
The sages of antiquity deeply understood this—thus, they distinguished themselves with the essence of Heaven’s Dao.
Internally, they ordered the self; externally, they dissolved calamities.
What should not be done brings shared sorrow with Heaven and Earth.
Distinguish the four modes of governance.

For the officers of emperors and kings, all ministers should age, while the young are not suited to govern the world.
I observe Heaven’s qi: of late, it has been repeatedly disharmonious.
The fault sometimes lies with officials who fail in sincerity, causing the seasonal qi to fall out of balance.
The lord of men is unclear; disasters and harms arise together, and Daoists are also harmed.
Even the Three Luminaries of Heaven and Earth suffer affliction—thus, there is no true clarity.
Daoists alone escape unscathed.

Though I alone have long enjoyed Heaven’s favor, I dare not presume to preserve myself.
From youth, I served my teachers and inquired of affairs, yet could not fully comprehend them.
The Heavenly Master resolved their essential intent, lest I never again attain such knowledge.

Governance has four methods:
The principle of Heaven,
The principle of Earth,
The principle of Man—
When the three qi reach their utmost, then the principle of all things moves and acts.
I wish to hear their intent.

The principle of Heaven: when ministers age, the lord treats them as a father.
Though ministers are lowly, why treat them as teachers and fathers?
Though their rank is humble, their virtue and power are weighty.
Treating them as teachers and fathers means learning from their virtue and power,
Aligning strategies to pacify the world.

The principle of Earth: befriend ministers as those of shared aspiration and heart.
Yin submits; mother and child share rank, womb-mates share sorrow.
Though ministers’ rank is humble, their virtue harmonizes the lord’s governance.

The principle of Man: humble the self, for ministers are young and small,
Like a father begetting a child. The child is young and small, unable to devise strategies for the father—hence, minor disorder arises.
Those who govern the world regard all ministers as teachers and fathers.
Thus, a father loves his child—what peril could arise?
Teachers and fathers resolve the eight directions’ perils for their child—what loss could occur?

The principle of Earth: all ministers under Heaven are the lord’s friends.
Those of shared aspiration align strategies in fellowship, sharing sorrows to secure their positions.
Earth submits and upholds the above, fully receiving Heaven’s intent—all attain Heaven’s heart.
What time would not be peaceful?

The principle of Man: attaining the qi of central harmony.
Harmony may advance or retreat, hard to discern—like a young child unable to plan for the father, deceiving him.
Young ministers cannot deeply plan for the lord—hence, they deceive him.
The young grow with the sun and moon, their learning shallow, lacking awe—thus, they deceive.
Hence, governance of the young is disordered.

The principle of the moving and acting: lacking principle and righteousness, the ten thousand things know little, possessing no virtue and power.
The moving and acting of the ten thousand things have no above or below, seeking only victory—hence, disorder and defeat arise.

The principle of Heaven: humans cherish life and do no harm.
The principle of Earth: following goodness, minor harm may occur.
The principle of Man: mutual benefit and many desires lead to frequent mutual harm, deceit, and peril.
The principle of the moving and acting: ultimately, no success—no above or below, seeking only victory.

Between Heaven and Earth, it is common to employ those unsuited to their abilities,
Forcing what they cannot do, making difficult what they cannot,
Observing their inability to act, their inability to speak,
Not pitying and teaching them, but instead blaming them,
Causing grievances to bind, multiplying resentment and disputes.
The people are sorrowful, suffering, and impoverished, gazing upward to call to Heaven.
Sincere grievances and bound qi move the six directions—
Hence, disasters and anomalies arise in profusion, accumulating in myriad forms, not swiftly removed.
The harm is grave—this reveals the hearts and minds of the world’s people.

Ultimately, no success is achieved; anomalies never cease.
How can the qi of Great Peace arise?
Thus, the failure to attain the qi of Great Peace lies precisely here.

The ten thousand things under Heaven each have their proper place.
One should employ their strengths, what they can do,
And not force what they cannot.

All things cherish the qi of yin and yang. It is like fish that cannot traverse high mountains, yet when water is present, they may depart regardless of height or depth. Great trees cannot rise without bounds—they grow within rivers and seas.

Thus, the sage-kings of antiquity, in receiving their charge, took from the five soils what was fitting for each. Their creatures thrived in goodness and excellence, flourishing abundantly, and the state grew rich. Now, ancestral temples offer sumptuous feasts, and all under Heaven is at peace, free from suffering. Malign qi ceases, no longer moving to cause harm.

If one does not examine the land before planting, the myriad things will not complete their natural spans but perish prematurely. Grievances remain unresolved, leading to untimely ends, which move August Heaven above. The harvest fails, the state falls into dire poverty, food lacks savor, ancestral temples hunger and thirst, all under Heaven is mired in sorrow, and the people turn to mutual harm. Rulers and ministers deceive one another, inner and outer realms speak in discordant tongues. The fault arises precisely here—this is the root of great harm, the path to peril and ruin.

Those who obtain this text and read it often suffer from not mastering it. Those who master it perceive its meaning with their eyes, yet if they do not deeply ponder its intent, if they do not study it with precision, even possessing this text brings no benefit. To obtain it and not exert oneself in practice—how does this differ from not obtaining it at all? To see food and not eat—how is this different from having no grain? To see broth and not drink—can thirst be quenched? This is not to grieve for others but to harm oneself. Can one not reflect carefully?

Thus, the sage exerts effort in thought, the noble person in study, day and night without ceasing. They delight in emulating Heaven’s ceaseless revolution, as the hundred rivers flow and gather to form the great seas.

Take heed of my words.

Heaven’s affairs each follow their own laws. Decrees may be assigned, the Dao may be enacted, yet their emergence may come sooner or later, their signs gradually appearing. It is like the myriad things: they first sprout in *zi*, grow in *mao*, branch in *wu*, mature in *you*, and conclude in *hai*. Though their signs may be foreseen, their outcome cannot be assured.

Each matter has its proper time for action. When its light and shadow are first glimpsed, though the event has not yet arrived, its path may be prepared in advance. Heaven’s portents always appear ahead, never trailing behind. When the right person is found, the way is opened; those who see and are aided by it succeed. If one does not comprehend this and acts without success, it is because the person is not the right one.

Thus, this serves as clear proof. The Dao is examined and spoken of, and in ten thousand cases, not one is lost. If the person is right, the way is opened for them; if not, it remains closed. When the right person is found, illnesses may be dispelled, disasters and anomalies vanish of themselves, and the barbarians submit without need of arms—they all fade away on their own.

All things have their proper arrangements and deployments. With the right person, they proceed naturally; without, they withdraw. In all matters, if the right person is not found, one must not force action. One must not forcibly take what is not one’s friend, nor forcibly plant what is not suited to the land—what is planted will not grow. If words are not good, if the inner does not find its proper place, how can it endure?

The six extremes and eight directions each have their fitting uses. Their creatures all manifest, yet each matter differs. The great person who obtains this uses it to pacify the state; the middling person becomes a worthy minister; the petty person uses it to preserve themselves.

Responding to Heaven’s principles, harmonizing above and below, calamities are dispelled, treachery and deceit are severed, and the roots of ominous texts are cut off.

The people of high antiquity all had hearts that were open, eyes that were bright, and ears that were clear. They foresaw what had not yet come to pass, deeply contemplating the future, moving even the unresponsive. Their distinction was self-evident, and no undertaking of theirs failed. What they spoke and taught was always steadfast and penetrating. They did not lose the heart of August Emptiness, yearning for the boundless wisdom and words of the boundless.

They knew the lengthening and shortening of human lifespans, each having its allotted portion. They constantly harmonized yin and yang to grasp their waxing and waning, taking the essential from above, below, and the center. They made covenants with the multitude of spirits, yet none dared transgress the great taboos of Heaven and Earth. What they revered and obtained accorded with Heaven’s will, and documents were submitted upward to the Heavenly Sovereign.

When the Heavenly Sovereign received the documents and saw their self-imposed restraints clearly delineated, only then were decrees issued, preventing self-reproach. The upright advanced of themselves, their voices heard without report, resounding clearly above and below. Laws and regulations never missed their appointed times. Fearing they might fall short, they never failed to reproach themselves. Constantly wary of faults, they were overseen by recording spirits who reported them. They never slackened, and when faults were seen, they were demoted and replaced.

Thus, they repeatedly admonished themselves, reiterating their words to ensure they did not deviate from what was said. This is what Heaven expects to be revered, what the gods and spirits look up to—all must follow the law without ceasing, ever fearful of failing to reach their mark. What they received was not uniform, yet all required an open heart and mind, lest they miss their appointed time.

Spirits have their ranks, high and low, and serve one another. If they do not act as spoken, they are promptly recorded and set apart. Their hearts are filled with sorrow, ever as if starving and thirsting for food.

When the Heavenly Sovereign speaks, the decrees are issued accordingly, appointing overseers. The documents are not few, and one must grasp their intent, for each has its own reliability.

The people of high antiquity, in matters of gain and loss, observed the inner and outer, above and below, gazing to the four directions and beyond the four corners. They saw the guiding principles, as months and years advanced, and spiritual communications renewed. What limit was there to this?

The degrees of the stars each have their principles, never shifting. Matters follow one another in succession, with no room for doubt. All knew the origins of fortune and misfortune, thus establishing the calendar and its records.

Three hundred and sixty days, with both major and minor reckonings, were held without missing the smallest fraction—this was the short month. Spring, summer, autumn, and winter each had their proper principles. The clepsydra’s rise and fall, the water’s swiftness or slowness, the division between new and old—all were made known, never missing by even a fraction.

Each month was set in place, with the twenty-four solar terms. The arrows before and after numbered seven or eight terms, as did the long days. These were used to enter and exit the sacrifices to the gods of Heaven and Earth, enabling the hundred officials to follow the clepsydra’s marks. If the appointed times were missed, the failure to respond incurred multiple offenses.

Thus the division of day and night followed the lengthening and shortening of days, with one hundred marks as the cycle, never allowing the slightest deviation. In a state of virtue, the days grew longer and the water flowed more slowly, each inch precisely corresponding to the regulated measure. Yet in many states today, this is not observed—the days and months are slightly shorter, with each mark reduced to eight or nine parts. Thus the elderly, whose years should be weak, paradoxically grow robust, while their lifespans naturally diminish. How can they endure for long? If a state has many ministers, the pivot and balance of governance move sluggishly. The young may enjoy fleeting fortune, barely drawing breath, yet even without overt wrongdoing, they will face retribution.

The radiance of Heaven and Earth resides in the south, where *sì* and *wǔ* hours share a single domain, and *lí* serves as the true eye. In the affairs of the Hall of Light, the sun shines from south to north, the advance and retreat of *yang* qi never straying from its constant course. As *yin* and *yang* press upon one another, reaching toward the *zǐ* direction, cold and warmth align in perfect accord, their illumination penetrating all naturally—most delightful indeed.

The Way of nurturing life lies in the interplay of lesser *yang* and greater *yang*, where wood and fire flourish in mutual glory, each attaining its desire. What conflict could arise? Inner and outer harmonize in succession, without misnaming anything. Above, it extends to the imperial radiance; below, to the realm of silence. In tranquil spontaneity, the myriad things bloom in splendor, all clearly discernible. Without effort, it achieves completion—this is what Heaven reveres. Those who receive its name are guided by the pivot and balance, where life and death have their appointed times. The Registrar of Destinies upholds the ledgers, the records of fate flowing unimpeded, never failing to summon in response.

When seeking something, the spirit-led registers verify the truth before ascending to the Heavenly Lord, who presides over all. The spirits who report do not stray from his side, and both within and without, they are revered. They dare not act on private whim, ensuring that all ascents and descents occur without missing their proper time. The officials of greater *yin* dare not slacken, diligently tending the gates and chambers of the celestial bureaus. Fearful of speaking out of turn, they instead support one another in goodness and essential ways, recording names on memorials. Once instructed, they act without deviating by even a fraction.

In ancient times, sages of profound wisdom perceived all without obstruction, their vision unhindered. Receiving the Way of spirit illumination, they understood it clearly, for it possessed its own laws, never straying from constancy. From the *Tàichū* era onward, calendars have varied in length, profound and subtly wondrous. From antiquity to the present, the essence of calendrical systems lies in their establishment and completion. Through mental calculation and observation, all that is accomplished below aligns with the work above, the numbers corresponding like a plumb line. Years, months, and days are tallied, their great divisions accounted for.

Now Heaven and Earth rejoice in abundant years, and the emperor should sit in tranquil rule, free from care. The people need only wander at leisure, with few duties, while the five grains no longer command their former value, their worth unmeasured. The world engages in brewing fine wine to share in drink, and market roads flourish to excess—this is called the "Water Decree," yet the conduct of fire harms the transformation of *yang*.

When a person drinks even one measure of wine and becomes drunk, wild pulses arise. Trade and duties are neglected, leading to brawls and deaths. Some are wounded or robbed; others arrive at the market early only to return belatedly. Some fall prey to villains, or tumble from heights, or are struck by carts and horses. The harms of wine are manifold, beyond counting. Consider the markets across the Four Seas—how much grain is consumed in a single month? Hundreds of millions of *dǒu* and *hú* vanish, while senseless killings occur daily.

Some are left childless, their lineages severed. Others incur the enmity of parents, who plot harm. Still others bring calamity upon their descendants. Local officials and magistrates cannot resolve these matters, beating their chests and crying to Heaven, moving the imperial spirits. This disrupts the *qi* of *yin*, *yang*, the four seasons, and the five phases, reversing the governance of the August Emperor of Great Peace and causing the *qi* of Great Harmony to flow contrary to its course.

All this stems from needlessly compelling the people to brew wine, wasting the five grains and inviting such disasters. If a virtuous ruler were to issue clear commands, declaring to officials and people: "From this day forward, anyone who dares to sell or drink even one *dǒu* of wine without cause shall receive thirty strokes of the cane and three days of penal labor. For two *dǒu*, sixty strokes and six days; for three *dǒu*, ninety strokes and nine days." The duration of penal labor should correspond to the measure of wine consumed, and wine-sellers shall be subject to the same. All shall be made to repair city walls, roads, and government buildings—this is the great work of earth.

Earth overcomes water, suppressing and extinguishing its excess, preventing water from harming *yang* beyond measure. Water is greater *yin*, the people; if it prevails, it will injure the king and deplete the essence of *yang*—the harm is profound. Repairing roads fosters the flourishing of the great Way, with like influencing like, gradually establishing Great Peace.

Examining the myriad things of Heaven and Earth, *yin* and *yang*, above and below, they govern and nurture one another in mutual affection. Establishing merit and achieving renown, one’s heart governs a single household, so that people no longer harbor hatred but instead delight in unity of purpose. The *qi* of Great Harmony will emerge daily, bringing great peace. The Six Directions will share one heart, the Eight Regions one plan. Where governance aligns with human intent, all will respond with joy.

This is the primordial *qi* of Heaven and Earth, uniting the positions of *yin* and *yang*. Wickedness and perversity will silently vanish, the rebellious will all submit, and the great and numinous Way will be revealed—the spirits and deities will cherish it. I now ascend to expound the Dao and virtue to August Heaven, descend to distinguish the measures of mountains and rivers, and establish laws for emperors and kings. The worthy among them will cultivate good intentions.

Thus I resolve the great grievances of Heaven and Earth, freeing the emperor from sorrow and toil. The people will love one another, and all things will find their proper place. The constant laws of Heaven remain unhidden. In ancient times, sagely emperors and enlightened kings valued great ministers, cherished recluses, benefited the people, and refrained from harm. Ministers, in turn, were loyal and trustworthy, never deceiving their ruler—thus their governance was divine.

A wise father constantly seeks to bring peace to his son, and the son constantly seeks to bring joy to his father. When the two join forces with one heart, no household matter remains unaccomplished. But if they do not unite in purpose, the family’s Way falls into chaos. Duties are neglected, leaving them destitute and impoverished. Strife and division arise, leading to mutual harm. Even flesh and blood, born of the same body and bound as limbs, turn against one another—how much more so when gathering people of different surnames to serve as ruler, teacher, and father?

Thus the sage perceives the subtle and knows the manifest, and therefore places great emphasis on caution and vigilance.

The teacher is yang, loving his disciples and guiding them with the virtuous Way, so they understand to revere Heaven and cherish Earth, honor their superiors and benefit their inferiors. The disciples, in turn, respectfully serve their teacher with obedience, diligence, loyalty, and trustworthiness. When the two join forces with one heart, they study the ancient laws and institutions of past and present, practice the words of the sages, clarify the boundaries of Heaven and Earth, and govern the myriad things, allowing each to find its proper place. Accumulating virtue without cease, they become the worthy assistants of emperors and kings, joining in counsel to together bring about Great Peace.

If they do not unite in strength and purpose, failing to transmit the essential Way, but instead pursue superficial and external words, deceiving one another and endangering themselves, they defy Heaven’s principles of order, disrupt the words of the sages, and leave the Six Extremes indistinct—becoming a great calamity for the world. If emperors and kings follow such teachers, they lose the principles of governance, turning instead to become the great enemies of Heaven and Earth, failing to receive the intent of the divine spirits. This is the greatest harm to the world.

Human life is endowed with both yin and yang; movement and stillness, anger and joy all have their proper times. When the time for the union of male and female has not yet come, it is the duty of yin and yang to govern the effects of generation. The Way of Heaven is completed through threefold union; thus a child walks at three years, and three times three makes nine, bringing the harmonious Way to fulfillment. Before knowing the union of male and female, the timely thoughts within cannot yet be expressed.

The number of Heaven is five, the number of Earth is five, and the number of humanity is five. Three fives make fifteen, and the internal qi stirs. Four fives make twenty, aligning with the qi of the four seasons to express desire. The four seasons govern generation, and thus desire seeks to generate. Five fives make twenty-five, and the qi of the Five Phases is sufficient to bear expression. Five sixes make thirty, and strength is attained. Thus Heaven causes constant thoughts of expression to circulate the continuity of Heaven and Earth, to propagate kind, and to meet at thirty years before exemption. In old age, one declines; the young cease to engage in inner chambers.

All creatures that crawl upon the earth are but reflections of Heaven and Earth; the rest cannot do so. Thus, in one day and one night, Heaven and Earth together nurture twelve thousand things, bringing them all to life. Night is deep—this is yin; day is dry—this is yang. Each day, Heaven and Earth together nourish these twelve thousand things to completeness. The law of Heaven is that yang unites with essence to become rain, yang’s expression descending into the earth to join with it, together generating the twelve thousand things. Of these, two thousand are auspicious and virtuous beings.

The twelve thousand things each possess their own spirit and have their own rulers. They must follow a single great Way to achieve free flow. The Way of Heaven moves above and below, all going to pay homage to their ruler—just as people following a single great Way go to pay homage to their king. The spirits of the twelve thousand things, born together with Heaven and Earth, emerge along a single great Way, some great, some medium, some small.

What does this mean? It means that among the twelve thousand things, there are great and small, and their Ways are likewise great and small, each generating, containing, and moving in its own manner. Thus, the upper Way spans ten thousand paces as its measure; the next spans a thousand paces; the next, a hundred paces; the next, ten paces; and the next, one pace. Altogether, five Ways correspond to the five directions. They should together descend to generate upon the earth, together ascend to pay homage to Heaven, and together follow a single Way.

Therefore, the great Way spans ten thousand paces, containing the middle Way of a thousand paces, the small Way of a hundred paces, the fine Way of ten paces, and the minute Way of one pace. Things have their greatness and smallness, each containing their own coming and going. All receive Heaven’s expression above and in turn generate below to express upon the earth, emerging to together ascend and pay homage to Heaven.

Thus, the great Way may be extended but must not be recklessly closed, for closing it will prevent mutual containment. Some will fail to be born, or be injured and die, unable to emerge—causing people to be cut off without descendants. The injured injure others; the dead kill others. The sages of antiquity dared not abolish or sever the great Way, for they clearly saw Heaven’s prohibitions.

By what Way of Heaven can one be harmed? The Way is Heaven, is yang, and governs generation. Virtue is Earth, is yin, and governs nurturance. If many things cannot be born, it is known that the Way of Heaven is harmed. Where there is failure to generate, it is known that Heaven’s continuity has been severed. If one thing fails to be born, one continuity is cut off; many failures mean many cut-offs, few mean few. By the number of things, one knows the harm to Heaven’s continuity.

When the Way flourishes, it governs generation, and the myriad things all live. When virtue flourishes, it governs nurturance, and the myriad things and people are all nourished, without grievances. Among the five writings, the virtuous are made to use blue for the base and red for the characters. Why? Our Way is the true record of red and blue. Blue represents life, benevolence, and having a heart; red is the true color of the Great Yang of Heaven. Our Way is the Way of Great Yang, the Way of benevolent governance, desiring no harm.

The Son of Heaven is the heart of Heaven; the Empress is the heart of Earth. The heart governs and upholds correctness. Heaven covers all without exception, generates all without distinction of great or small—all receive the mandate to live, and thus it is Heaven. Heaven is the true essence of the ultimate Way, never deceiving people. All things should be cherished and loved; their intentions should accumulate sincerity and trust, always desiring to benefit and not harm, never betraying a single thing—thus it is Heaven.

The emperor and king are the children of Heaven and the leaders of humanity; their conduct should reflect this. The son should receive his father’s teachings, commands, and strict instructions, following them accordingly. Only then will his actions align with his father’s will and intentions, and he may become a good family. If he does not receive his father’s teachings, his family—great and small—will not be governed, and it will become impoverished. Wealth will scatter in all four directions, constantly suffering from inability to gather. Affairs will be chaotic, disasters will arise in succession, and great sorrow will follow—all faults lie here.

When the emperors and kings of antiquity were about to act, they first looked up to Heaven, receiving its teachings in their hearts before proceeding.

The conduct of the empress should rightly mirror that of the earth. The earth bears all without exception, gathering both great and small, encompassing all without distinction of good or evil, nurturing them all. The empress is the child of the earth, the heart of the earth. As the heart worries over all matters, the child should emulate her mother’s conduct—if her actions resemble her mother’s, she is a filial child.

The correspondence between Heaven and Earth and the empress is like that of echo and sound: if her deviation is slight, the consequences are slight; if great, the consequences are great. Even a hair’s breadth of misalignment will leave mother and child at odds in will and intent. In antiquity, when an empress was about to act, she first contemplated the Earth Deity, embracing all without exception in her nurturance. Nothing was beyond her forbearance, nothing lacked constancy; thus she found peace, aligning her heart with the earth’s.

If she errs, disasters will arise in succession, punishments will go unchecked, yin will prevail over yang, and the myriad things will fail to flourish—all faults lie here.

When these two—emperor and empress—govern rightly, the divine immortals appear, the true Dao emerges, the worthy and wise occupy their rightful places, and all good things gather in the realm.

Qi in its primordial state is yang and governs generation. Spontaneous transformation is yin and governs the nurturance of all things. Heaven is yang and governs generation; Earth is yin and governs nurturance. The sun and daylight are yang and govern generation; the moon, stars, and night are yin and govern nurturance. Spring and summer are yang and govern generation; autumn and winter are yin and govern nurturance. The celestial stems *jia*, *bing*, *wu*, *geng*, and *ren* are yang and govern generation; *yi*, *ding*, *ji*, *xin*, and *gui* are yin and govern nurturance. The earthly branches *zi*, *yin*, *chen*, *wu*, *shen*, and *xu* are yang and govern generation; *chou*, *mao*, *si*, *wei*, *you*, and *hai* are yin and govern nurturance. All nines are yang and govern generation; all sixes are yin and govern nurturance. Men are yang and govern generation; women are yin and govern the nurturance of all things. The male is yang and governs generation; the female is yin and governs nurturance. The ruler is yang and governs generation; the minister is yin and governs nurturance.

All things under Heaven consist of one yin and one yang, only then can they generate and nurture one another. If yang does not bestow generation, yin becomes empty and void, with nothing to nurture.
