If yin does not receive transformation, yang has nothing to bestow. Generation is governance; when yang qi governs alone, cut off and obstructed, it becomes Heaven’s great resentment. If yin does not receive transformation, failing to generate and bring forth, it becomes a grave fault.

Heaven’s resentment lies in yang’s reluctance to bestow, leaving nothing to generate, instead favoring destruction and harm to life. Earth’s fault lies in yin’s unwillingness to receive transformation, failing to bring forth and nurture growth, thereby faulting others and harming what should be nurtured. Heaven that does not send timely rain is a malevolent and inauspicious Heaven. Earth that does not nurture the myriad things is a malevolent and inauspicious Earth. A man who does not bestow generation severs Heaven’s governance. A woman who does not receive transformation severs Earth’s governance. The Dao of yin and yang, cut off and without posterity, is a great inauspiciousness—like Heaven and Earth suddenly destroyed, never to exist again.

Thus the sage values the essential patterns of Heaven. Heaven is the essence of all Dao. The worthy value the Dao, hence they follow the sage. The worthy enter the true Dao, hence they follow the immortal. Those who know how to become immortals must be true, hence they follow the true. Those who know the true must attain the divine. The divine share form and principle with Heaven above, hence Heaven is called divine, for it can command the divine.

The divine are the officers of August Heaven. The divine person is the foremost heart of August Heaven. The nature of Heaven and Earth is that the pure governs the turbid; the turbid cannot govern the pure. Radiant essence is the heart of the myriad things. Those who govern with clarity use their hearts to discern matters, employing pure brightness.

Now, what do the divine person, true person, immortal, Daoist, sage, worthy, commoner, and servant each resemble?

The divine person resembles Heaven, which moves and illuminates all without ignorance. The true person resembles Earth, which is upright, utterly sincere, and never deceitful. Heaven merely follows what people sow, never altering it. The immortal resembles the four seasons, which transform all things without fixed form, now flourishing, now declining. The Daoist resembles the five phases, which can divine fortune and misfortune, excelling in discerning safety and danger. The sage resembles yin and yang, which model themselves on Heaven and Earth to govern affairs, harmonizing the myriad things. The sage, too, should harmonize all things, fulfilling Heaven’s will and following yin and yang in action. The worthy resemble mountains and rivers, which convey qi and reach distant lands; the worthy, too, should enable the emperor to connect with the six directions. The common people resemble the myriad things, which grow without regard to high or low, all inhabited by people, hence they resemble the myriad things. Servants arise in degenerate ages, resembling the weak and submissive among grasses and trees, always dwelling in the lower currents, unable to rise. Servants, too, dwell below and cannot rise, hence they resemble grasses and trees.

Thus, if a servant is worthy, they may become a good person; if a good person studies diligently, they may become a worthy; if a worthy studies without cease, they may approach the sage; if a sage studies without cease, knowing the gateways of Heaven’s Dao, and enters the Dao without ceasing, they may accomplish the work of immortality and become an immortal. If an immortal does not cease in entering the true, they may become a true person; if a true person does not cease in entering the divine, they may become divine; if the divine do not cease, they may share form with August Heaven.

Thus the supreme divine person dwells in the Purple Palace of the North Pole, sharing form with the Heavenly Thearch, named the Heart-Mind Spirit of Heaven. If the divine do not cease, they may ascend beyond Heaven, receiving and transmitting qi, possessing voice yet no form, belonging to the realm above Heaven, attending to its affairs.

Those from the divine person downward all attend to matters within the six directions of Heaven and Earth, harmonizing all to prevent suffering.

I wish to hear: among the vast and boundless six directions between Heaven and Earth, what is most excellent? Among the thirty-six thousand realms between Heaven and Earth, longevity is the greatest excellence.

Thus, Heaven is foremost, Earth follows, then the divine person, the perfected person, the immortal, the Daoist, the sage, and the worthy. These eight all harmonize with the Heart-Mind of August Heaven, sharing its will and joining its power—all are Heavenly persons.

Heaven desires governance, and within its domain, each is appointed to their office. Thus, their thoughts and concerns ever align, for these are the people Heaven cherishes and nurtures. Heaven, in its greatness, covets longevity and eternal life. Immortals, too, covet longevity and life; those who covet life dare not transgress, each calculating for their own preservation.

Heaven’s laws manifest in celestial signs, which the sages of antiquity constantly emulated, never daring to deviate. Thus, they suppressed misfortune, severed cunning, and prevented treacherous ministers from acting—all by adhering to Heaven’s laws. To ensure yang qi daily flourishes, fire blazes brightly, and knows no decline, one must swiftly sever the dominance of metal qi and prevent its ascendancy. When metal qi is cut off, wood qi reigns, fire qi blazes brightly, and knows no decline.

What does this mean? The Heavenly Lord must abolish warfare. Warfare belongs to the class of metal; thus, it must be swiftly abolished. When emperors and kings bestow weapons upon feudal lords, they empower metal qi. When metal qi reigns, wood declines; when wood declines, fire dims; when fire dims, the omen of war arises. Fire symbolizes the ruler, capable of transforming the four seasons. Mars, as the harbinger of change, most faithfully reflects Heaven’s laws, not erring by even a fraction.

When the ruler governs his household, he should focus on cultivating the fields and managing livelihoods. Upon encountering these four circumstances, if he does not bestow benevolence and favor upon the people, leaving the common folk with no recourse against litigation and theft, what is to be done? When encountering the worthy, bestow upon them culture; the hungry, food; the cold, clothing.

Why bestow culture upon the worthy? Culture arises in the East and shines in the South. Thus, celestial patterns originate in the Northeast, and writing emerges from the Northeast’s symbolism. The tiger bears its markings in the *yin* position, the dragon in the *chen* position, ascending to Heaven. *Li* represents culture in the South; thus, the Three Luminaries embody culture. The sun rises in the East and reaches its zenith in the South. Heaven commands emperors and kings to model themselves upon these patterns.

Heaven has Three Sovereigns, Earth has Three Sovereigns, and humanity has Three Sovereigns. Heaven has Five Emperors, Earth has Five Emperors, and humanity has Five Emperors. Heaven has Three Kings, Earth has Three Kings, and humanity has Three Kings. Heaven has Five Hegemons, Earth has Five Hegemons, and humanity has Five Hegemons.

What does this mean? Heaven’s Three Sovereigns correspond to the Three Luminaries; Earth’s Three Sovereigns correspond to highlands, plains, and fields; humanity’s Three Sovereigns correspond to ruler, minister, and people. Heaven’s Five Emperors correspond to the Five Stars; Earth’s Five Emperors correspond to the Five Peaks; humanity’s Five Emperors correspond to the five viscera. Heaven’s Three Kings refer to the Three Luminaries, and its Five Hegemons to the Five Peaks—aligning with humanity and Earth.

Among Heaven’s Three Sovereigns, the most excellent is the sun, the middling the moon, and the lesser the stars. Among Earth’s Three Sovereigns, the most excellent are the Five Peaks, the middling the level lands, and the lesser the fields. Among humanity’s Three Sovereigns, the most excellent is the ruler, the middling the minister, and the lesser the people.

All people bear six great sins that cannot be absolved—some incur punishment in their own bodies, while others pass it to later generations. Yet, though one accumulates boundless Dao, if they refuse to teach others to seek life, their sin remains. Though one accumulates boundless virtue, if they refuse to teach others to guard virtue and nurture their nature with care, their sin remains. Though one amasses wealth by the millions, if they refuse to relieve the poor and aid the distressed, allowing people to die of hunger and cold, their sin remains. Though one knows the Dao, if they scorn it and refuse to study diligently to save themselves—or, having attained longevity within the celestial lineage of their ancestors, they instead treat it lightly and do not study, thus dying in vain—their sin remains. Though Heaven endows people with strength so they may clothe and feed themselves, if they refuse to labor and instead suffer hunger and cold, squandering their ancestors’ legacy and idling away their strength, their sin remains. If one forcibly seizes others’ property, making harmony their enemy, their sin remains. These are the six great sins. Heaven abhors them and they cannot be absolved.

As my departure approaches, I leave this one admonition to the six disciples: The Dao is vast, without above or below, without exterior or interior. Guard its harmonious qi, and you are a subject and child. Seek it near, and you grasp the great; seek it far, and you lose it. Thus, the ruler who excels in governance begins with the stirring within his own belly—truly contemplating the Dao, principle naturally unfolds. Near, it resides in the heart and chest; far, it pervades the Four Seas.

The ancients called this the essential Dao. When the sages of antiquity instructed emperors and kings, they deeply pondered and planned, closing their nine apertures, resting their four limbs, entering a state of primordial chaos—like a ring without end, like a child in the womb without duties—only then could they grasp its principle. My Dao takes this as its great essential, and Heaven treasures its transmission.

*Excerpts from the Tai Ping Jing, Ding Section, Scroll Four (conclusion)*
*Tai Ping Jing, Wu Section, Scroll Five*

Aligning the celestial omens with the stems and branches, the state of Chang’an is governed thereby. What you inquire is the profound connection between Heaven and Earth, the omen-texts that, once spoken, cannot be altered for ten thousand generations.

The Heavenly Lord suffers from frequent disasters and sorrows. August Heaven takes the four seasons as its limbs, Earth takes the five phases as its body. The limbs govern flourishing and decline, the body governs compass and square. These nine spirits flow together throughout the world, penetrating above and below, their transformations difficult to perceive. They are the world’s greatest treasures, the gates of all things, possessing inherent constancy. One must not recklessly transgress them: those who follow them enjoy enduring fortune; those who disrupt them bring discord between Heaven and Earth.

Heaven’s constant omen-law establishes the South as the ruler’s domain. The sun in the South is the ruler, fire in the South is the ruler, the Great Yang in the South is the ruler, the height of summer in the South is the ruler, the hearth among the Five Offerings in the South is the ruler, and the heart among the five viscera in the South is the ruler.

The ruler should wear red garments, for this aligns with the phase of fire. When the ruler encounters anomalies, they invariably correspond with yang, never with earth. The sun, being the brightest, leads all luminaries, so Heaven constantly uses the sun to divine the ruler’s virtue in its flourishing or decline.

The model for a ruler is to seek kinship with the benevolent, govern with those who possess a heart, and together with those who govern, always practice the Dao and cherish life. Thus, the East cherishes life, the South cherishes nurturance. Those without benevolence cannot govern together; those without clarity cannot be rulers or leaders. The East, associated with wood, embodies benevolence; the South, associated with fire, embodies clarity. The East governs the Dao, the South governs virtue; the Dao governs life, virtue governs nurturance. The East represents culture, where the dragon appears bearing it. The South represents refinement, hence it is the essence of culture and refinement.

The East is where lesser yang begins to arise, thus it emerges from the East. The South, as the great yang, embodies the ruler’s flourishing virtue, its brilliance illuminating the lesser yang’s domain—wood gives birth to fire. Lesser yin serves as minister, submitting in righteousness to the great yang. Thus, metal yields to fire, bending and breaking as desired; ministers must likewise submit in righteousness to assist the ruler’s desires. Hence, lesser yin is the minister. Great yin is the people, who flow ceaselessly like water. The people are tasked with governing life for the state and its lords.

Thus, water nurtures wood, and wood is the ruler’s domain. Heaven’s omen-law dictates that lesser yang fears lesser yin. Therefore, ministers, in reversing their roles, record the affairs of the state, its lords, and officials. Great yang fears great yin: when a state possesses virtue and its ruler and ministers are wise, the people follow; when a state lacks virtue, the people rebel. Thus, the foundation of governance lies in the people’s abundance, for many people bring wealth, few bring poverty.

Heaven’s omen-law divides into six parts. The southeast and above belong to Heaven, where all things ascend, creatures move, and people venture outward—all under Heaven’s domain. Thus, Heaven’s color is outwardly blue-green like wood, inwardly red like fire. The northwest belongs to Earth, where all things fall in autumn and winter, returning to soil, and people, like creatures, retreat into burrows by autumn and winter. Thus, Earth’s color is outwardly yellow-white like soil and metal, inwardly containing the black of water, symbolizing its northern movement.

The East and South hold honored positions, belonging to Heaven above and governing as rulers, teachers, and fathers. The northwest, belonging to Earth below, serves as ministers, the rear palace, and the people. The people are the rear palace of *jia*. *Jia* is Heaven, the fundamental position of kings, thus it is the Heart Star. The Heart Star is fire, belonging to the South. *Bing* is the chief of fire, chosen for its great brilliance—it is the ruler’s position. *Xin* is the rear palace of *bing*, and *jia* is the father of *bing*. Thus, *ji* is the palace of the great empress. *Xin* pairs with *bing*, and *bing* is the son of *jia*. Hence, *xin* is the palace of the lesser empress. *Bing* is the rightful son of *jia*, the ruler who receives the mandate.

*Geng* belongs to *yi*, the husband of the state’s feudal lords. *Ren* belongs to *ding*, the husband of the emperor’s younger sister. *Gui* belongs to *wu*, the in-laws of the state’s great empress. The ten celestial stems each have their affiliations, while Earth governs the twelve earthly branches—how is this so? Heaven’s law dictates that though yin and yang circulate, those that pair each have their own domains. Heaven’s law differs: it does not allow entire households to follow and remain together. *Jia* takes *yin* as its domain, *yi* takes *mao*, *bing* takes *wu*, *ding* takes *si*, *wu* takes *chen*, *ji* takes *wei*, *geng* takes *shen*, *xin* takes *you*, *ren* takes *zi*, and *gui* takes *chou*. Thus, the Dao of Heaven moves in reverse to govern, while the Dao of Earth remains still. Hence, there is division of land but no division of people.

Now, a state exists, so Heaven and Earth do not shift. Heaven completes one revolution in a day and night, its movement constant. Thus, the twelve branches each have their place and do not follow the stems in rotation. Wine is the sovereign of water, and water’s sovereignty should overcome fire. Fire is the ruler’s virtue; swiftly banish wine to preserve the fire’s power.

My Daoist method proceeds by regulating yang when going forth and regulating yin when entering; by regulating conduct when going forth and regulating spirit when entering; by regulating all texts when going forth and regulating all diagrams when entering; by dispelling disasters when going forth and rectifying the self when entering; by regulating the court’s learning when going forth and regulating the inner chamber when entering. In all matters, establish limits. Those who strive diligently in learning should each employ their talents, lest they lose the constant method. External learning, when pursued excessively, leads to superficiality, and one cannot restrain oneself. Internal learning, if not aligned with the correct path, veers into great error. Many scholars suffer from grave maladies yet remain unaware.

Those who favor external learning and possess great talent often fall into superficiality, causing the Dao to become greatly distorted and lose its true principles. They falsely claim it as the authentic Dao, deceiving one another in peril. Those who overindulge in internal learning often plunge into great error, believing they have attained it. Ancient and modern texts abound beyond measure. In learning, grasp the true essence and do not deviate from its root. For those who learn from a master’s oral instructions, do not violate their master’s words—this is the great essential.

The greatest harm in learning lies in aligning with external chapters and verses, which leads to superficiality, excessive ornamentation, and reckless speech. Those who delve into internal texts that align with diagrams and omens fail to deeply grasp their essential meaning and instead speak in error. In all matters governed by Heaven’s discourse, only when ten correspond with ten is it correct. When nine correspond, it is slightly erroneous; when eight correspond, it is slightly chaotic. Below this, it is unusable. Such misnomers disrupt celestial patterns, displease yin and yang, cause all things to contend, and bring great calamity upon the people.

The method of nurturing life lies in inwardly perceiving one’s form and countenance clearly—this is the way.

Externally perceiving the myriad things and their multitudinous essences—this is incorrect.

In all matters, one must constantly uphold the original text and seek the explanations of many worthies to stabilize it—this is correct. To amass numerous literary chapters and verses while forgetting the fundamental matter—this is incorrect.

The Celestial Master emerged with the qi of Great Peace, receiving the Dao and its virtue to revive the Supreme Sovereign. Favoring rulers who cherish the Dao, his thoughts extended downward even to the foolish and humble, penetrating the Six Directions and uniting with the Eight Extremities, encompassing all without exception.

The Dao is distinguished by nine degrees:
1. **Primordial Qi and Non-Action**: To think of the body as doing nothing, only contemplating its luminous purity, as if relinquishing qi and formless—this is the method.
2. **Serene Emptiness and Spontaneity**: To guard the form and embrace emptiness, naturally devoid of strangeness, with the body’s interior radiant and unobstructed like a king.
3. **Numerical Measures**: To accumulate essence and inwardly observe, counting from the hair down to the feet, distinguishing the five fingers, and enumerating every aspect of form and countenance, internal and external. Knowing its meaning and constantly dwelling on it without losing even a fraction—this is the lesser art of measurement.
4. **Spiritual Travel and Return**: To contemplate the spirits of the five viscera as they journey forth by day and return, witnessing their movements, conversing with them, and discerning good and ill fortune—this is the next degree.
5. **The Great Dao’s Spirits**: When the human spirit departs, it aligns with the four seasons and five phases, sharing the hues of green, red, yellow, and black with the visceral spirits. The spirits and officials of the five phases serve humanity, capable of subduing all malevolent forces.
6. **Stabbing Joy**: To stab the earth, inducing cleverness in people—this must not be employed frequently.
7. **Community Counsel**: The spirits of heaven and earth, the four seasons, altars of soil and grain, mountains and rivers, and sacrificial rites—these must not be treated recklessly.
8. **Vast Spirits**: These spirits are boundless, their Dao unattached; when the world’s refined qi descends, they cause people to speak recklessly, half resembling truth and half resembling deception.
9. **Ancestral Spirits**: These are purely apparitions of ghosts, devoid of true Dao.

The celestial spirits possess their own divine treasures, their radiant essence following the five phases in color and the four seasons’ qi in rise and decline, serving heaven, earth, the people, and the myriad things.

Between heaven and earth, at the juncture of yin and yang, none are untouched by the transformative power of virtue and born thereby. To uphold the Dao, accumulate goodness, and thoroughly harmonize with the spirits and qi of heaven and earth, the people, crawling creatures, the myriad things, and the qi of the four seasons and five phases—constantly interacting with them—is to know none who are not virtuous.

**First Rank: Great Compassion and Filial Piety**
Compassion and filial piety arise from inner reflection, thoughts emerging from the storehouse of the viscera, attainable without study—this is the art of spontaneity. Conduct aligns with the heart of heaven, intent harmonizes with earth. Above, it benefits the emperor and king; below, it leads the people to prosperity, fostering harmonious qi and serving as the foremost model for humanity. Its practice is as vivid as cinnabar and ink—thus, it is ranked first.

**Second Rank: Illuminating the Dao and Great Gentleness**
To clarify the Dao and its virtue, leading the hundred clans, studying and cherishing the Dao, amassing virtue, and preventing theft and banditry—this benefits the emperor’s transformative governance, embodying the truest auspiciousness.

**Third Rank: Filial Piety, Fraternal Respect, and the Beginning of Virtuous Transformation**
Those who begin to learn and desire goodness harbor hope in their hearts, turning from depravity toward rectitude, though their benevolent conduct has yet to fully transform.

**Fourth Rank: The Diligent Farmer’s Son**
The diligent farmer’s son rises at dawn and rests at dusk, unafraid of toil, accumulating day by day. His household thrives, sustaining his parents, securing the earth’s bounty, and following heaven’s Dao. He dares not act wrongly and benefits the county’s governance.

**Fifth Rank: The Greatly Unbenevolent Son and Lawless Youth**
The lawless, the unbenevolent sons—those who reject principle, curse heaven, strike the earth, and neglect their parents—inevitably wield weapons, terrorizing their villages. These frivolous youths disrupt heaven and earth’s transformative work, becoming grave harms. They must be captured through concerted effort, discarded into ditches, and denied burial.

**Sixth Rank: Discord at Home, Deceiving the Elderly and Favoring the Young, Sharing Food but Hoarding Wealth**
Such households are doomed to ruin. Kin turn against one another, unable to instruct, recklessly spreading rumors and evading responsibility. Abandoning roots for branches, their calamity is irredeemable.

**Seventh Rank: Repenting Wrongdoing and Abandoning Weapons**
Born in destitute villages, rarely witnessing or hearing of goodness, ignorant of right and wrong, their conduct offends heaven. Yet, thanks to a sagacious ruler, they are guided toward goodness. Though unlearned in youth, they repent in maturity. Let the virtuous and worthy, with pillars five feet high, swiftly expel them from the ranks. Those who study should examine this: one day, all the people may become good.

**Eighth Rank: Repenting Wrongdoing and Returning to Goodness**
Those whose studies fail and whose misfortunes multiply may yet, by the grace of a sagacious ruler who understands their plight, be allowed to repent and even become teachers of others.

**Ninth Rank: The Greatly Wicked, Deceitful, Greedy, and Corrupt**
These corpse-like officials, wicked and avaricious, deceive their superiors and harm their subordinates. Great flatterers, they bear human form but possess the hearts of ravenous beasts. They bring no benefit to heaven, earth, yin, or yang, and their deep-seated disasters warrant execution and annihilation.

**Tenth Rank: Correcting Wrongs and Returning to Rectitude**
To repent, reform conduct, and change one’s heart—though lacking goodness in youth and suffering repeated calamities—is to amend faults by evening if committed by morning, thereby earning the name of a good person.

These ten ranks are the methods of the ancient sages and worthies, delighting in people’s goodness and preventing mutual harm. Their aim is to allow each to complete their natural lifespan, return to the Dao, and sever the roots of misfortune, thereby witnessing the qi of Great Peace.

The divine all operate by established norms, their roots in the Great Correlation. The Great Correlation strikes the emperors and kings, thereby rectifying the movements of heaven. Its secondary root strikes the empresses and queens, thereby harmonizing the patterns of earth. Its middle root strikes the multitude of sages, thereby governing yin and yang. Its fine and subtle roots connect to the common people, thereby governing the myriad things. The great person who acts accordingly attains greatness; the middling person, middling results; the petty person, small gains—yet all may attain correctness.

When emperors and kings practice the Dao and virtue, their flourishing is vast and luminous; with little virtue, their light is dim. When empresses and queens practice the Dao and virtue, the moon shines with great brilliance; with little virtue, its light is faint. When the multitude of worthies practice the Dao and virtue, the stars and celestial cycles blaze with radiance; with little virtue, their glow is weak. When all four roots practice the Dao and virtue together, the world is at peace, auspicious signs appear, and great light extends far. Gazing afar at the celestial signs, wind and rain arrive in their proper seasons, the barbarians submit in sincerity, and disasters and harms dissolve of themselves.

Now, having received the Celestial Master’s writings on the Dao and virtue, they are entrusted to the reverent people, so that the reverent may return to a ruler of great benevolence and virtue, thereby pacifying the governance of the world and securing long-lasting peace for the self. The emperor is the first noble son of the August Heaven above; the empress is the first noble daughter of the Earth below. These most divine and sagely noble persons, by their office, ought to dwell within the hundredfold layers of the cosmos, yet instead they take on the cares of the world beyond ten thousand *li*, receiving the mandate of heaven to govern yin and yang, the six directions, and the eight quarters, upholding the supreme positions of heaven and earth. Entrusted by the divine spirits, they penetrate the utmost heights and depths, and all creatures that creep and crawl turn their hearts toward them.

Thus, they compose the *Wushang Lingbao Petition*, able to comprehend the will of heaven and illuminate the names of the officials versed in the stars and celestial cycles. As Grand Astrologers, they must not fail in their duties, alternating day and night to observe and await the flourishing or decline of celestial *qi*, the gains or losses of the Three Luminaries, rejoicing in receiving heaven’s commands and admonitions to secure their own peace. In the eleventh month, they cultivate the Yellow Bell, guiding the *qi* of the earth below to ascend and communicate, rejoicing in harmonizing with the intent of the Earth Queen to secure their own peace.

They construct the Hall of Light in the land of *bingwu* under the Great Yang, opening eight windows and four thoroughfares to delight in the free flow of the *qi* of the eight directions and four seasons, desiring to align with the auspiciousness of the eight winds and four seasons to secure their own peace. They open the four gates, rejoicing in receiving the world’s rare texts, extraordinary strategies, seldom-seen treasures, and the wise and wondrous arts that can bring long-lasting peace to the world and dispel calamities and anomalies.

In ancient times, the sages on the throne constantly sought out reclusive worthies and the meekly virtuous to share in governance. They wished to hear of the four seasons’ honored nobility, yet the kingly *qi* is the chief of the formless *qi*, the one to which all other *qi* strike and submit—these are the honored noble rulers. The kingly *qi* is heaven, the August One, the Emperor, the King, the Grand Year-Star, the Monthly Establishment, the Dipper’s Ridge, the Azure Dragon, the Great Virtue, the Flourishing Prosperity, the Emperor-King, the Supreme King, the Lord of Generation and Completion.

Thus, wherever the kingly *qi* resides, the myriad things submit to its rule; where it dwells, all things live and thrive as kings; where it turns away, all perish—this is due to the primordial *qi*. Therefore, when the kingly *qi* resides in yang, yang prevails; when it dwells in yin, yin prevails; when it resides in heaven, heaven prevails; when it dwells in earth, earth prevails. Wherever the kingly *qi* resides, all becomes kingly, receiving the mandate to govern and order.

Thus, the ancient sage-kings faced east in spring, south in summer, west in autumn, and north in winter, with the sixth month at the center. When the *qi* completes its circuit, they presented themselves to heaven, for the kingly *qi* is most honored in heaven. The month’s establishment is called "Breaking and Great Expenditure"; when the emperor’s *qi* clashes with it, it is named "Death and Extinction." The primordial *qi* establishes the positions, and the emperor’s *qi* is the first *qi*, majestic and not to be rashly opposed.

The position after the monthly establishment is called "Closure." Closure is when heaven seals off the yin *qi* of rest that follows, fearing that it may advance to become treacherous and crafty, encroaching upon the emperor’s established *qi*—thus, it is closed off behind. Opening is heaven’s law, which delights in no harm or injury. Therefore, opening what follows demonstrates the teaching of restful *qi*, for if there are those who act treacherously, it delights in opening the way for them to retreat. If they do not retreat, they will be seized; once seized, they will be interrogated, and guilt will be established. Once guilt is established, it cannot be removed, and death or peril follows.

Thus, the fifth position after is "Peril," which brings one near death. The sixth position after is "Breaking," where the Dipper’s handle breaks and death ensues—thus, the *Kui* star governs death, leading to peril. Therefore, the emperor’s *qi* arises from Lesser Yang and Greater Yang, ever guarding the establishment of the Dipper. The *qi* of death arises from Lesser Yin and Greater Yin, ever guarding the *Kui* of the Dipper.

Thus, the six positions following are where heaven constantly rests and empties, aligning with earth’s *qi* to govern closure, concealing treachery and villainy, dwelling together with evil spirits and beings—these must not be rashly opened or revealed. The ancients had worthies who cherished life, and all *qi* belonged to the front of the Dipper, moving in parallel with the celestial motions—thus, the days were auspicious and full of *qi*. All who are treacherous, crafty, yin-assassins, or evil and perverse resemble yin *qi* and belong to the rear of the Dipper—thus, the days are in decline, and their actions are inauspicious.

The primordial *qi* is vague and indistinct, naturally coalescing into one, called heaven. Dividing, it generates yin and forms earth, called the second. Thus, above is heaven and below is earth; yin and yang unite to generate humanity, called the third. The three powers together generate and nurture all things, called wealth. Wealth generates desire; desire generates perversity; perversity generates treachery; treachery generates craftiness; craftiness generates harm without end—then chaos and ruin follow. If ruin does not cease, it cannot be governed again, and thus it reaches its limit and returns to its root—this is called "inherited burden."

The Way of heaven is without intent: when it encounters the unworthy, chaos ensues; when it obtains the wise and enlightened, order is restored. In ancient times, when emperors and kings obtained the wise and enlightened, the Dao flourished. They dared not take the foolish and unworthy as close advisors. Swiftly transmit this text to a ruler of supreme virtue. Those who practice it with penetrating clarity will shine, and the three *qi* will appear and inquire of one another.

Those who divine with ten successes in ten are thorough in governance—this is the foremost clarity, fit for service to emperors and kings. Those who divine with nine successes in ten, with one *qi* disordered and ungoverned, may serve as feudal lords. Those who divine with eight successes in ten, with two *qi* disordered and ungoverned, may serve as common folk. Beyond this, it is called "disordering heaven’s upright Dao," and grievances will bind the spirits and numinous essences, lurking in concealment where governance cannot reach, unable to harmonize the *qi* of Great Peace.

If you seek the Dao, ponder the written texts; the method of seeking the Dao takes stillness as its root. Accumulate essence without cease, and it becomes the gateway to spirit. The five virtues harmonize and unite, revealing the hun and po souls. When the heart-spirit is illuminated, the great Dao unfolds. First discern safety and peril, observe the four neighbors. The host of spirits gathers like clouds; if this practice does not cease, you shall be a long-lived lord. The great Dao does not require toil—your form like dead ashes, guarding the hun-spirit. If the hun-spirit does not depart, you shall long endure. The cycle returns to its beginning, endless as a ring. To abandon the root and seek the branches brings trouble to the Dao; the multitude loses it and cannot be whole. Reflect on its meaning, do not lose the true words. Purity and stillness are the foundation, not the use of wealth. How can you not cherish the words of an enlightened teacher? Follow the teacher’s instructions, and you shall not die.

The foolish rebel against their teacher and dwell near ghosts; they do not attain the upright Dao but enter the gate of misfortune. They depart and do not return to spirit; their bones and flesh rot in the mire, called ancestors only in name. Their fate is extinguished, their ruin complete.

The arts of the common and foolish all arise from within, possessing their own laws, with depth as their root. When they encounter the spirit, they live, free from suffering and sorrow. The spirit detests strife and turmoil—calm the heart, settle the mind, and beware of sudden violence. With prolonged stillness, the myriad Dao emerge. Long endure without death, and you shall match heaven’s completion.

To practice this, you must harmonize and become one with the Dao. The worthy hold fast without wavering, and all matters are fulfilled. Cast aside worldly thoughts, unite with the spirit, ride clouds and mount dragons, sharing a chamber with the Thunder Duke. Your body transforms into spirit, your form like the Great One.

Ponder these written words carefully; be vigilant not to lose discipline.

The Dao of focused contemplation is perfected in seclusion. Do not seek honor or rank; let your resolve grow daily more refined. Open the obscured to radiant clarity, like the brightness of day. When you do not study, it is as if gazing into blackest night—east, west, south, north, lost within your chamber. The worthy and sagely tremble, their hearts alone quaking with fear.

If you firmly uphold the five precepts, you shall not die. Content with poverty, delighting in lowliness, you may endure long. To scorn lowliness and seek nobility obstructs the Dao. Covet no high office or heavy emolument; to forcibly pursue rank is to lose the Dao. Better to lie abed in long repose.

Without eating, you become luminous; the hundred evils depart, and calamity flees afar. Guard stillness without cease, and you shall not perish. With good fortune, you may live long and walk far, never daring to indulge or lose constancy. Seek without cease, and you shall be a king of the Dao. The arts of nurturing life differ in method; they do not hinder the people’s affairs.

When those above cherish life, the people’s lives are long. The worldly teachings place the Dao above, with benevolent kings. The sagely lord ponders the Dao, and its transformative influence flows downward, making the people pure and incorrupt. They shall know no calamity forever.

If the people do not die, it is due to the clarity of those above. When the ruler above lacks clarity, teachings go unheeded. Refusing the Dao, they instead favor warfare. Every household has a wicked son, and families perish. Wielding weapons, they waylay travelers by the roadside, seizing their goods in moments of vulnerability. The magistrates are not at peace, and bandits roam. Observe the people, and you may know whether those above are enlightened.

When the lord cherishes benevolence, those below seek long life. When those above lack benevolence, those below incline toward perversity, all meeting early death, knowing no joy in life.

When the foolish below cherish virtue, it is due to the ruler’s teachings. When the people cherish the Dao, their lord is enlightened. They all desire long life and to distance themselves from calamity, rejecting corruption and laying down weapons. They fold their hands and do nothing, casting aside misfortune. The sagely lord greatly prospers, and the people grow close. His kindness extends even to the foolish below—this is the mark of a true king. The Dao of heaven cherishes life to secure those above. When the foolish below do not contend, it is the blessing of those above. The world is most fortunate, and none do not turn toward the king.

When the people do not cherish the Dao, it is due to the obscurity of those above. Harboring treachery within, they outwardly display virtue, yet do not practice it, favoring warfare instead. Fathers and sons are separated, dwelling by the roadside. They cannot attain long life, and deaths accumulate. Households have impoverished sons like tigers and wolves. Those above lack virtue, and the calamity of war follows. The foolish below have a ruler whose transformative influence does not flow; the people’s many inclinations toward immortality reflect the emperor’s clarity. Heaven sees his governance, and kindness flows downward. Even the crawling and panting creatures are bathed in his light.

Heaven cherishes life and the Dao, thus it is called the "Heavenly Canon." Those who accumulate virtue are the "Earthly Canon." Earth cherishes nurturance, thus it is called the "Earthly Canon." Those who accumulate harmony and delight in giving are the "Human Canon." Harmonious *qi* flows and circulates; people possess wealth and circulate it, giving and receiving. Thus harmony is the "Human Canon."

In ancient times, those who sought learning all rectified their roots. It is like planting a tree: seek a good seed and place it in good soil, and its growth—root, trunk, branches, and leaves—shall all be good. The root is the master; the branches and fruit are the disciples. Thus, in ancient learning, all first reflected on the root before studying the Dao. Therefore, those who could practice it harmonized with the heart of heaven, and so it was auspicious.

If one plants a tree without choosing a good one, placing it in poor soil, how can its branches, leaves, flowers, and fruit be beautiful? This begins with aligning the body and rectifying the nature, directing the intent of the Dao to return to primordial *qi*, thereby settling the body. Reflect on the duties and practices of the ancient masters—how can one govern oneself? Plan with a settled mind, and you shall attain it yourself. First settle the body, then begin the practice, like an infant at play, without straining sinews or strength, using only good intent.

Ponder how the ancients alone attained longevity—through singular focus, how did they achieve it? Only by the utmost Dao, restraining perversity and removing treachery, like a spirit. Without strange occurrences, the root is rectified, and thus one gains heaven’s heart, does not betray earth’s intent, completes the four seasons, harmonizes the five phases. Descendants do not inherit burdens from one another; each embraces utmost virtue, no longer knowing perversity or evil.

Entering the chamber alone, one contemplates the fundamental needs of the scriptures and the Dao—what must be brought forth and what must be let go. The worthy first grasp its meaning, and those who follow after attain it as well, thus together entering the Dao, far removed from perversity.

Secluded in the chamber, one reflects and preserves, the five officials shifting in turn, aligning with the cycles of yin and yang—meng, zhong, and ji as brothers—moving in response to *qi*, in accord with the four seasons and the five phases. The transformations of heaven’s Dao become the constant norm.

To lose *qi* is to die; to possess *qi* is to live. All things follow this, and the human Dao stands supreme. Thus, the five officials arise in accordance with *qi*, and heaven’s Dao soars as the supreme power through *qi*.

The perfected person accumulates *qi* and gathers spirit illumination; thus, the Dao alone endures in its constant course, while the myriad people, losing *qi*, perish. The dead are base; the living are noble.

If you guard the Dao, you may long endure, transforming with *qi* as heaven does in its constancy. Do not hasten after fame and profit, and the Dao will proceed of itself. Heaven’s Dao constantly generates without loss; earth’s Dao sustains duality, presiding over death.

The sages and worthies of highest antiquity—those of superior attainment retired to the mountains, while lesser scholars perished like insects among the common folk.

The worthy, upon seeing these writings, ponder deeply upon these words, first embracing difficulty and then ease, thus keeping the body free from harm. By guarding virtue, one completes the great Dao in the body. After studying and passing through the nine chambers, one becomes a spirit person, whose thoughts are ever distinct from those of ordinary people, never ceasing day or night to contemplate earthly matters, but desiring to hear of heavenly affairs.

The mind then contemplates the duties of heaven above, and only afterward descends through the nine chambers, accumulating essence with utmost sincerity, naturally transforming and altering one’s form. This is the sage of the highest heavens, who no longer concerns himself with the affairs of the common world—this is clear.

My writings enable the lofty scholar to attain life without hindrance, while the lesser scholar is prevented from reckless actions and false words. My writings on the Dao exhaust the aspirations of humanity, allowing the worthy and the unworthy each to fulfill their capacities, so that even at death, there is nothing left to regret—each has fulfilled their heavenly mandate.

Those who desire longevity and lasting joy should contemplate and follow the true intent of the Dao. Those who do not seek lasting joy should attend to worldly affairs, content merely to preserve their bodies.

Examine your conduct and reflect upon yourself to know the methods of gain and loss. The wise and enlightened encompass heaven and earth, accumulating boundless scriptures, yet if they cannot prolong their lives and enhance their destiny, this is called emptiness, a Dao without substance.

The masters of esoteric arts, though they may study for a long time and exhaust themselves, though they may master the patterns of heaven and earth, comprehend the nature of all things, and amass a complete collection of texts, if they cannot serve their parents and honor their ruler, such knowledge is of no benefit.

Ponder deeply upon these words, and good and ill fortune may be known. By practicing this simplicity, one comes to understand gain and loss for oneself.

What in learning is most urgent? Thus, I set forth these two matters, clearly distinguishing the signs of a scholar’s loss and gain.

Since the closing of the age, there have been two urgent concerns; the rest may be known or not, as one wishes. What heaven, earth, and the sagely and enlightened deem most pressing to promote and greatly attain are longevity and filial piety.

Longevity is to share the same excellence as heaven and earth. Filial piety is to share the same power as heaven and earth. Thus, longevity is long life, sharing the same essence as heaven; filial piety is to submit below and comply with those above, sharing the same resonance as earth. These two matters accord with the intent of heaven and earth, and misfortune naturally departs.

Ponder deeply upon this intent—it is the principle of Great Peace, the essential key to long life. Yet those who desire to do good and seek to live are few.

Parents are the root of life. The ruler is the gateway to honor and esteem. The teacher is the source of wisdom, the inexhaustible vocation. These three are the gateways of virtue and the Dao.

Parents transmit the ancestral lineage of heaven and earth’s yin and yang. The teacher understands the intent of heaven and earth, resolving the knots of worldly affairs. The ruler, bearing the mandate of heaven and earth, complies with yin and yang, ever striving to grasp their intent, taking the governance of the Dao as his duty. Thus, these three are the gateways of nature and destiny.

Ponder deeply upon these words, and the myriad harms will be dispelled. Longevity and filial piety are what the divine spirits love. Those who lack longevity and filial piety are the targets of a hundred calamities.

This Dao is natural and requires no effort. To know its efficacy, observe how it constantly follows the good and evil of human intent. The mind’s intentions scheme within, and echoes respond without. To know this Dao, observe the correspondence of reflection and echo.

The mind and intent are the gateways of good and ill fortune. The rulers of Great Peace in antiquity governed by ensuring their minds and intentions were good, and thus their ministers were good. If their intentions were misguided, their ministers followed suit.

Mind and intent are the pivot and trigger of heaven and earth; they must not be recklessly disturbed, lest harmonious *qi* be thrown into chaos and disasters arise daily.

*Excerpt from the Fifth Scroll of the Abridged* Classic of Great Peace*, Wu Section*
*Excerpt from the Sixth Scroll of the Abridged* Classic of Great Peace*, Ji Section*

Now throughout the realm, mouths are sealed in fear, daring not to speak recklessly. Even the sun, moon, and stars in their celestial courses—intimate spirits of heaven’s constellations—stand in mutual awe. Thus when the sun rises, the stars flee and hide, not daring to appear, for they fear its majesty. Within the four borders, where a stern emperor reigns, heaven trembles and the earth quakes; though the capital may lie at a great distance, none dare speak in defiance of his edicts. If a province has a powerful governor, the entire province dares not speak. If a commandery has a formidable magistrate, the whole commandery dares not speak. If a county has a harsh magistrate, the entire county dares not speak. If a village post has a stern warden, even that single post’s jurisdiction dares not speak. This warden is but the lowest of officials—how much more so for those above him? All fear harm and seek only to absolve themselves, so that even if they harbor good intentions, they dare not express them to their superiors, and thus the Dao is severed.

Even within a single family, bound by blood and kindred, such fear prevails—how much more so between those of different generations? Since the middle ancient era, the Dao and virtue have been lost, and governance has relied instead on might and force, with coercion and threats. Those who do not comply later suffer grave harm, their descendants deeply afflicted. In the lower ancient era, this grew even worse: should one wish to submit a memorial or speak to the emperor, those who probed his intentions would kill them. If not harmed at once, they would be secretly entrusted to others for injury. Thus ministers and people all tied their tongues, sealing their mouths in silence; though they witnessed sorrow and injustice, they could not report it upward. This left the emperor’s wisdom and insight cut off, and heavenly omens multiplied—clear proof of the effect.

Now the people are born of their parents and receive life from heaven and earth, taking heaven and earth as their parents. When they witness calamities or auspicious signs, these are the words of heaven and earth, wishing to speak. Yet all fear harm and instruct one another, collectively turning their backs on the August Emperor and the Earthly Sovereign, suppressing their grievances before heaven and earth, so that words cannot pass, and heaven and earth remain long burdened with unspoken sorrow.

Though the emperor is the wellspring of divine and human, he dwells within a hundred layers, beyond ten thousand *li*. Within those hundred layers, those who wish to convey words are obstructed and coerced, unable to reach him. When words cannot pass, heaven and earth grow enraged, slaughtering all things and destroying the cosmos. In such a year of great misfortune, wisdom is severed, and the state faces grave peril. This crime cannot be named, and thus it must be eradicated.

Great calamities and strange omens are the great words of heaven and earth. Moderate calamities and omens are their moderate words. Minor calamities and omens are their minor words. This is like human affairs: great matters merit great speech, small matters small speech—nothing appears without cause, nor is it meant to deceive. When great auspicious signs appear, heaven and earth rejoice greatly; when moderate signs appear, they rejoice moderately; when minor signs appear, they rejoice slightly. The absence of calamity and auspice is equilibrium.

Thus when heaven intends to aid an emperor, it first endows him with intention. From ancient times to the present, when heaven intends to aid one, it invariably produces extraordinary texts and marvelous strategies that can be verified and governed. Those who follow them all meet with great fortune; when heaven does not intend to aid one, it severs these extraordinary texts and strategies, preventing them from being seen, or if seen, making them appear foolish so they are not understood or applied. When heaven intends to promote one’s conduct, it opens the heart to clarity and receptivity, allowing their use—this is the method of heaven’s aid, and it does not deceive.

Those who are about to prosper tend to favor goodness; those about to decline tend to favor evil. Those destined for fortune are easily guided; those destined for misfortune resist and defy others. Heaven constantly aids the good; the Dao longs to return to the virtuous. Heaven refuses to aid the wicked; the Dao refuses to entrust itself to fools.

Heaven’s talismans return essence as cinnabar script, inscribed into the belly. When one sees the script within, great fortune follows, and all evil departs. The Five Offices and Five Kings are the origins of the Dao, the ancestors of spirits. If one can carefully seal them, closing the gates, then outwardly dark but inwardly bright, how can one not see clearly? Guarding this over time, heavenly physicians descend, and all illnesses vanish, leading to longevity. Fools discard it; the wise treasure it as a priceless gem—this may be called the Dao of eternal existence. It uniquely honors the natural, with form and spirit mutually preserving each other. When these two embrace, any perverse thoughts become faults, and losing the natural, one cannot attain longevity.

The infant’s five essences return to preserve itself. The Heavenly Lord asked: Why is the realm so difficult to pacify? The divine officials of the Five Phases replied: Now the emperor dwells within a hundred layers, ten thousand *li* from the four borders. Those far away harbor many grievances, and good and evil cannot reach him. Extraordinary methods and marvelous strategies are severed, unable to reach the emperor. Ministers and people, though aggrieved, cannot plead or communicate. Over time, the four directions become obstructed, and the worthy and good hide in seclusion. The emperor cannot obtain marvelous strategies or extraordinary words to pacify the realm—the fault lies in the closure of the distant borders on all sides.

People dwell between heaven and earth; since the opening of the world, each person has but one life, never to be reborn. From the moment one has a name and is called human, humanity is the chief of all harmonious things, noble and honored, akin to heaven and earth. Yet upon death, one is eternally confined, never again to be called human or to rise and act. Thus it is mourned as a great injustice.

Heaven and earth’s laws: Heaven and earth are the parents of all things, and they fear that among them, some may weep in grievance, gazing upward to heaven and bowing to earth, lamenting their early demise. Thus heaven generates the true Dao and marvelous methods by which one may protect oneself and attain modest longevity. All living things grow old and perish, yet fools refuse to diligently study the true Dao and good methods that could grant eternal years, delaying death and aging. Instead, they each neglect themselves.

They scorn the true Dao and mock its marvelous methods, instead engaging in deceit and falsehood to disrupt the Way of Heaven. They deceive their superiors, hastening toward death, building tombs and preparing for the grave, arranging funerary pacts and mourning garments in advance—seeking death, they find it. What injustice is there in this?

When one’s years are spent and fate exhausted, it is like the sun rising only to set again. The ancient sage-kings, ever mindful of their own worth and fearing death, day and night sought rare knowledge and extraordinary methods, revered Daoists, and exhausted their wealth in pursuit. Their utmost sincerity moved the August Heaven, which responded with auspicious signs. Masters of Daoist arts aided them, and so many attained long life, some even transcending the world.

Now, heaven and earth regard humans as their children, and the emperor is the most honored of Heaven’s offspring. Yet they do not cherish the true Dao or its marvelous methods. Thus, with deep calculation and foresight, they know that the wealth of the world is not theirs to keep forever.

In ancient times, sages were wise and enlightened, and all worthy men emerged, gathering above as assistants. Thus, grievances were resolved. Heaven and earth have their principles—how much more so human relations? Emperors could govern with ease, free from worry, while the worthy fulfilled their loyalty, aiding their rulers in governance, together alleviating the great concerns of heaven and earth. The people thrived as a result—was this not good?

When great assemblies were held, it was difficult to question why heaven and earth collapsed, why the sun, moon, and stars were eclipsed, why people died violently, or why the twelve thousand states’ strategies and divine texts were revealed. Why did the Three Luminaries suffer eclipses? Heaven and earth openly praise and elevate, yet this is not called praising or elevating people—it is called mutual reciprocity. Such examples are numerous and cannot all be recorded, and none of these receive heavenly retribution.

Yet if others do not protect me, I alone secretly protect them—Heaven rewards such a person. If others do evil, I alone do good—Heaven rewards such a person. If others do not contribute to me, I alone take joy in contributing—Heaven rewards such a person. If others do not feed me, I alone take joy in feeding them—Heaven rewards such a person. If others practice teachings as empty falsehoods to deceive, I alone teach people to be sincerely good—Heaven rewards such a person. If others say heaven and earth are unknowing, I alone secretly revere and serve them—Heaven rewards such a person. If others secretly desire to deceive their rulers, I alone secretly protect and benefit them without daring to deceive—Heaven rewards such a person. If parents do not love me, I alone love and protect them—Heaven rewards such a person. Such examples are too many to record.

The true person reflects: the superior person seeks heavenly reward, the middling person seeks human reward, and the foolish do not give yet demand reward. The most virtuous receive heavenly reward and transcendence. The moderately virtuous receive human reward, and so are loved, benefited, and employed. The foolish, contributing nothing, yet demanding reward, are despised and punished by heaven, earth, and humanity.

Thus, the qi of the August Heaven descends to generate, the qi of the Earth ascends to nurture, the qi of the Five Phases unite in effort, and the qi of the four seasons harmonize. The Three Luminaries shine ever brighter, and the world unites as one. Heaven’s nature is to act, and it most honors, values, loves, and protects those who embody it. Once heaven’s nature is good, it generates all things without exception. Earth’s nature is to nurture all things without exception. Sages delight in ordering heaven and earth, and all things receive their beneficence.

The great and good, the divine immortals, assist heaven and earth in their work, never daring to neglect themselves. They align with the primordial qi and harmonize with the heart of Heaven, and so enjoy perpetual fortune without misfortune.

The ancient sages and worthies, through deep thought and foresight, understood the intent of the Way of Heaven: they devoted themselves to secretly practicing goodness and dared not do evil. They deeply observed the bright prohibitions of the August Heaven, yet below, people turned their backs and violated them. With shallow learning and inferior understanding, they further disbelieved in Heaven’s prohibitions—thus, their fates were difficult to change, and they perished early.

The desired lifespans are: Heaven’s longevity at one hundred twenty years, Earth’s at one hundred, humanity’s at eighty, hegemons’ at sixty, and the subordinate at fifty. The Three Norms begin in the east, the head of Heaven. The year and months culminate in the northeast, the pole of Heaven. Heaven’s longevity is the firmness of numbers; the northeast is the beginning of things. The great cycle of the year ends here, so one hundred twenty symbolizes Heaven.

Earth is yin, constantly receiving; the northwest is the extreme of yin. Yin brings death, yang brings life—thus, *hai* (the twelfth earthly branch) is the kernel, the end of yin in the northwest corner. The northwest is Earth’s controller of fate, so Earth’s longevity is one hundred years. Eighty and sixty mark yang’s cessation and yin’s rise, just as autumn begins. Autumn is the white qi, the White Tiger presiding—thus, the hegemonic lifespan. Fifty marks yang’s growth above and yin’s concealment below, yin and yang transforming each other—thus, the subordinate lifespan. Below this, all are called impermanent lifespans—truly a grievous entanglement!

Now, let me clarify one principle for you, which you must never forget if you wish to nurture yourself to the utmost and endure forever. To avoid misfortune and harm and attain long life, one must know how to cherish oneself, to value and befriend oneself, and thus nurture oneself—only then can misfortune and harm be averted.

To preserve the body for long, eat and drink in moderation, neither too much nor too little—this is cherishing and nurturing oneself. To close the gates and dwell within, not engaging in worldly affairs—this is cherishing and nurturing oneself. To read endlessly, content in poverty and lowliness, free from worry—this is cherishing and nurturing oneself. All that came before is not like this.

To speak of cherishing oneself is to speak of sincerity. Truly cherish and preserve yourself, reflect on your body—even with eyes closed, you still see yourself, never for a moment separated from it.

Reflecting in worry until one feels sated without eating—this is the mark of one who truly cherishes oneself. To speak of "valuing oneself" is to speak of cherishing the form of the body, its every part visible from head to toe. When such sincere love and care never cease, the face and eyes radiate light. If one cannot forget this day or night, making it a constant practice, the flesh may take flight and grow strong—this is the Way of self-love and self-care.

Now, therefore, let men and women, young and old, wise and foolish alike, all submit memorials to the throne, that the emperor may attain enlightenment and wisdom. The emperor is like the North Star, ever fixed in its place, while all other stars come to present their affairs. The greater stars lead, the middling follow, and the lesser come last; if even one star fails to appear, the flow of qi is cut off, and the celestial movements are harmed. For the stars are the essence and radiance of the people and all things. Thus, if even one person cannot reach the emperor, one star too cannot reach its place. Heaven’s qi then becomes disordered, and earth’s qi turns against it. Therefore, instruct all officials and commoners, great and small, to submit memorials together, to harmonize heaven’s qi, to stabilize the stars’ courses, to dispel celestial afflictions, and to relieve the emperor of the burden of inherited faults.

Thus, three messengers are dispatched to circulate the memorials, lest any fail to reach the throne. The chief officials record disasters and omens within the city walls; the road inspectors record those along the thoroughfares; and the rural officers record those in the four wilds. Each gathers reports of varying lengths, transmits them to one another, and competes to submit them first. If the chief officials grow enraged, heaven and earth engage in battle, and their discord manifests in the sun, moon, stars, and celestial cycles—sometimes eclipses occur, sometimes they do not, the fault lying in the struggle between yin and yang qi. Yin and yang contend for dominance, each seeking to overpower the other. Yet yin and yang were originally meant to benefit and assist each other, together generating harmonious qi; their conflict arises solely from this lack of harmony. If they were harmonized, no eclipses would occur. In the most virtuous ages of high antiquity, eclipses were unknown. By the middle ages, heaven and earth’s intent was gradually lost, yin and yang grew less loving toward one another, and thus their battles began.

If you doubt my words, let a virtuous ruler put my teachings into practice. If he fully grasps their meaning, the battles will cease; if he grasps half, they will diminish by half. When the emperor abundantly practices the Dao and virtue, the sun and moon do not eclipse, and the stars’ courses remain orderly. This is like old friends who, though long parted, rejoice greatly upon meeting and aid one another. But if they were never close and suddenly encounter each other, they will fight instead.

I ask: when drought strikes and all perish, when the people suffer and die of hunger and cold—this is the wrath of the Great Yang, the August Heaven. The six yang forces unite in resentment and thus bring harm. What does this mean? The six directions reach their limit, and their great net, long disordered by human malice, turns to killing. How does this harm people? It has no name. It simply strikes when the burden of inherited faults reaches its extreme, erupting in great fury, making no distinction between good and evil—those it encounters meet great misfortune. It is like a man seized by rage who, in his fury, attacks even the innocent. What wrong has the victim done? He merely encountered another’s rage. Thus, when the burden of inherited faults reaches its peak, it causes death and evil without distinction. The greatest calamity lies here.

I ask: the strategies of the twelve thousand states differ—where should they be aligned? Let each follow its own customs, but with what should they begin? With the Dipper’s handle pointing southeast, the fire qi arises. I wish to hear the essential meaning of this. Fire is yang. Its tally commands the heart of heaven; harmony governs bestowal, openness governs communication, and clarity governs order. Fire is the lord of the heart, and the spirit of harmony is the chief of transformation. All affairs that arise begin in the heart. The heart governs right action, leaning on benevolence and clarity, and is further endowed with divine radiance. Though the twelve thousand states’ strategies differ, when their memorials are unified in one document, the primordial qi will naturally follow and flow. The perfected ones will adhere to it; to act in accord brings fortune, to oppose it brings ruin. Heaven delights in issuing such texts, and thus I speak.

In ancient times, the fire phase was to bring Great Peace, yet the divine Way was not rectified. Why, then, does the Celestial Master now command that the fire phase alone rectify the divine Way? Because the fire qi is at its most flourishing, and when the qi of the Highest Sovereign arrives, the fire qi’s flourishing must rectify the divine Way. Why? Fire is the heart of heaven. The heart governs the spirit, and when the heart’s spirit is bright, the heavenly qi is harmonized. When the heavenly qi is unbalanced, the emperor is distressed, yet the people do not grasp its essentials. If you wish to know this, it is bitter to the ears.

Now, when wicked men occupy high positions, they disrupt the emperor’s governance. When the upright are denied office, heaven and earth lose their rectitude, and deviant qi prevails. When deviant qi is abundant, it harms the upright; when the upright are many, they suppress the deviant. These two forces are the natural arts of heaven and earth.

I ask: the Supreme Qi of the Utmost Cavern governs governance. Thus, the Celestial Master examines the sores, scabs, and worms that devour people—this alone verifies the matter. When worms devour people, the disaster is most severe, for it disrupts the proper order. Now that the August Qi of balance has arrived, such things should not occur. They are the responsibility of a virtuous ruler who seeks to understand the Dao in its fullness. Before instructing the people to transfer the names of all worm lords, great and small, that cause harm—such as the three worms of the abdomen that produce sores and scabs—let their names be transferred. There is no worm without a name, however minor. Worms that hide within and secretly consume people are like worthless ministers who lurk within and devour the people. They are deeply to be feared; if not feared, they will bring great harm. Heaven bestows human destiny, and it has its own standards and laws.

What Heaven and Earth reserve for themselves lasts thirty years—akin to the way Heaven and Earth, sun and moon, alternate in their cycles, with surplus days forming intercalary months. Thus is the private mandate established; those who surpass this term become immortals. The span of life allotted by Heaven is set at one hundred twenty years; by Earth, one hundred years; by man, eighty years. The lifespan of a hegemon is set at sixty years, and that of a commoner at fifty. Those who fall short of these measures—whether in death or life—suffer the calamities of inherited burdens. How can this be called unjust?

Each person is born with a celestial reckoning, governed by fixed laws, yet most fail to exhaust their allotted span. The accumulation of celestial reckoning is boundless; thus, those who do good receive an increase in their allotment, augmented by this surplus. To grasp the greater principle, consider a village of ten households, each with a thousand acres of land. If nine households commit evil and perish, the sole virtuous household inherits the fields of all nine—this is the meaning of such reward.

Do not expect yin and yang to protect people. If one fails to fulfill their allotted span yet hopes for celestial recompense, they will not receive it. If today you eat another’s food, then tomorrow they eat yours, this is not called consuming another’s food but “borrowed grain.” If today you drink another’s water, then tomorrow they drink yours, this is not called drinking another’s water but “borrowed broth.” If today you carry another’s burden, then tomorrow they carry yours, this is not called bearing another’s load but “borrowed luggage.” If today you lend another your strength, then tomorrow they repay you, this is not called aiding another but “exchanged labor.”

Now, when people praise and recommend someone, they rush to submit memorials; when villagers do so, they too rush to submit memorials; and when travelers do so, they likewise rush to submit them. If local officials hesitate to submit, they fear the people will do so; if the people hesitate, they fear the travelers will; and if the travelers hesitate, they fear the officials will. Thus, all are compelled to submit, and thereafter they vie to present matters.

When officials and commoners prove trustworthy, the emperor employs them without betrayal. Thus, officials and commoners delight in their service, and the emperor gains wisdom, fulfilling the royal will and securing his longevity. Officials and commoners, in turn, honor Heaven and Earth, remaining free of illness. When all four directions of Heaven and Earth benefit, long-lasting fortune is assured, establishing a model for ten thousand generations. This is entrusted to a ruler of supreme virtue, that the people may know the will of Heaven, enabling them to secure their own peace and wholeness, free from confusion.

The great compilation gathers and rectifies matters, examining the roots of Heaven and Earth to eliminate the terrors of Heaven, the faults of Earth, and the harms afflicting the state, thereby establishing the *Canon of the Utmost Extremity*. Furthermore, I inquired of the Heavenly Master’s writings, which collate and verify all texts from the opening of Heaven and Earth to the present—those of former worthies and sages, the *River Chart* and *Luo Book*, divine writings, and even the words of common folk, servants, and distant barbarians. All receive extraordinary words and unique strategies, unified into a single discourse to illuminate the Dao of Heaven. Was this not an immense labor?

Yet because distant matters often remain obscure, each seeks the abode of Great Peace within their own domain, preparing in their assigned villages and towns. Those too distant to deliver their words in person may establish stations along the roads, where they deposit extraordinary words, virtuous strategies, and rare methods. These are then gathered and presented to the ruler of virtue, allowing the assembled worthies to examine and classify them, selecting the finest and most upright to discard falsehoods and form the *Canon of the Utmost Extremity*, named the *Celestial Canon of Utmost Governance*.

Thus, the ailments of Heaven and Earth will be entirely dispelled; the governance of the emperor will achieve great stability; and the accumulated disasters of inherited burdens across ten thousand generations will be driven away. Thereafter, the myriad beings and spirits will transform in ways beyond description, and no longer will they ascend to report human evils to Heaven above.

Therefore, the decree to collate and verify these texts is Heaven’s command for me to speak below. Though laborious, how could I not exert myself to the utmost? If every year, from all under Heaven, ten or so writings and individual testimonies are gathered, the doubts of the world will resolve themselves—without undue burden. Each remains in their place, speaking and transmitting their words upward. This is how the world’s voices are collected and shared, communicating the intent of Heaven and Earth, circulating the qi of Heaven and Earth, eliminating the emperor’s disasters, and benefiting all people and beings. When each attains their rightful place, Heaven and Earth will rejoice as one, their ailments dispelled. In their joy, they will protect the emperor, allowing him to govern effortlessly and wander at leisure.

I wish to know why Heaven and Earth, at this time, command the people of the world to gather words and strategies, along with the writings of ancient and modern divine sages, to form the *Canon of the Utmost Extremity*.

The reason is that Heaven and Earth suffer from grave illnesses, constantly afflicted by chaos, and have never achieved proper governance. Thus, they instruct people to gather and collectively produce correct words and extraordinary strategies to cure these ailments. This is why they command a great assembly of voices and matters.

I wish to know why, when Heaven and Earth are in chaos and afflicted, they do not simply bring forth more good sages.

To repeatedly produce later sages would be of no benefit. The Heavenly Master said: The conduct of ancient sages varied in excellence, each excelling in one domain, all speaking the words of Heaven and Earth yet differing in expression. Thus, the sages who appeared before and after pursued distinct paths. All delighted in fulfilling the will of Heaven and Earth, eliminating evil and promoting good, yet their words were not entirely alike, though broadly similar. Therefore, even the assembled sages could not fully comprehend the intent of Heaven and Earth. Thus, Heaven and Earth remain afflicted by grave illnesses, none of which are dispelled. For this reason, I have been sent to convey this message to the Perfected One.

The Perfected One I address is one among the gods of Heaven who delights in goodness and seeks to align with the will of Heaven—unique in his enduring truth. The reason for collating the divine writings of the high, middle, and low antiquity is this: what the divine writings of high antiquity did not address, those of middle antiquity did; what the divine writings of middle antiquity did not address, those of low antiquity did.

Thus, by categorizing and aligning them to complement one another, a single discourse of goodness is completed—hence their compilation, whereby the intent of Heaven and Earth may be observed. What the sages of high antiquity missed, those of middle antiquity grasped; what the sages of middle antiquity missed, those of low antiquity grasped; what the sages of low antiquity missed, those of high antiquity grasped. By categorizing and aligning them, and thereby complementing one another, a single discourse of sagely goodness is completed.

The highest sages may have missed something, which the middle sages grasped; the middle sages may have missed something, which the lesser sages grasped. Again, by categorizing and aligning them, and thereby complementing one another, a single discourse of sagely goodness is completed. The greatest worthies may have missed something, which the middle worthies grasped; the middle worthies may have missed something, which the lesser worthies grasped. By categorizing and aligning them, a single discourse of worthy goodness is completed. Emperors and kings may have missed something, which their ministers and sons grasped; their ministers and sons may have missed something, which the common people grasped. By categorizing and aligning them, and thereby complementing one another, a single discourse of goodness is completed. The eldest may have missed something, which the able-bodied grasped; the able-bodied may have missed something, which the young grasped. By categorizing and complementing one another, a single discourse of goodness is completed. Men may have missed something, which women grasped; women may have missed something, which servants, slaves, and barbarians grasped. By categorizing and aligning them, and thereby complementing one another, a single discourse of goodness is completed. The writings of high antiquity may have missed something, which those of middle antiquity grasped; the writings of middle antiquity may have missed something, which those of low antiquity grasped. By categorizing and aligning them, and thereby complementing one another, a single discourse of goodness is completed. The people of high antiquity may have missed something, which those of middle antiquity grasped; the people of middle antiquity may have missed something, which those of low antiquity grasped. By categorizing and aligning them, and thereby complementing one another, a single discourse of goodness is completed.

Some may have missed something above, yet grasped it below; some may have missed something below, yet grasped it above; some may have missed something above and below, yet grasped it in the middle; some may have missed something in the middle, yet grasped it above and below. The divine writings of the celestial gods may have missed something, yet the sages grasped it; the sages may have missed something, yet the worthies grasped it; the worthies may have missed something, yet the common people grasped it; the common people may have missed something, yet the barbarians grasped it. Some may have missed something internally, yet grasped it externally; some may have missed something externally, yet grasped it internally. There are those who grasp it, and those who miss it. Thus, from above and below, within and without, the noble and the humble, the near and the distant—all take their essential words, compiling their strengths and shortcomings, categorizing and aligning them, and thereby complementing one another, then it shall be complete. Thereafter, the words and discourses of the writings shall be fully communicated.

Heaven and Earth generate all things, the people, the sages and worthies, the crawling creatures and the myriad beings—each has its strengths and shortcomings, each has its insufficiencies, each has its losses. Thus, their actions differ, though all broadly seek to align with the intent of Heaven and Earth and thereby secure their own peace. Therefore, today Heaven has sent me down to assist the ruler of supreme virtue in further examining the teachings of the writings, and I have assembled them all. The divine writings and sagely discourses, extending even to the common people, servants, slaves, and barbarians—by categorizing and aligning them, combining their words and discourses, the good shall be made into a comprehensive scripture, named *The Writings of the Supreme Heaven’s Utmost Governance*.
