Thereafter, the grave illnesses of Heaven and Earth shall all be dispelled.

I ask: by assembling these categories to align with one another—
Indeed, rectifying their words for goodness brings fortune; failing to rectify their words for goodness brings misfortune. Thereafter, the qi of the Great Peace and the Supreme Sovereign shall swiftly arrive.

People afflicted by illness all wish to swiftly recover and become well; the illnesses of Heaven and Earth likewise wish to swiftly recover and become well. Now, heterodox writings confuse the Daoist scriptures; when the Daoist scriptures are confused, the celestial patterns and earthly principles are disordered. When the celestial patterns and earthly principles are disordered, Heaven and Earth fall ill. Thus, the Three Luminaries, winds and rains, the four seasons, and the Five Agents engage in constant strife, and the years turn inauspicious. The emperor and king grow anxious and distressed; the officials govern in chaos; the people suffer from hunger and cold—all this is the affliction of heterodox writings. When heterodox writings, heterodox words, and misleading discourses are used to govern the state, disorder arises daily. Thereupon, ministers distort the law and act recklessly; the people are impoverished and exhausted, together defiling the principles of Heaven and Earth. The celestial officials grow furious, weeping and crying out in grievance without end.

When heterodox words, heterodox writings, and misleading discourses are used to govern the household, father and son, husband and wife fall into disorder, growing mutually resentful and constantly quarreling without cease, thus becoming an inauspicious household. Only upright words, upright writings, and upright discourses are the root of rectifying Heaven and Earth, the treasures that pacify the household, the state, the sacred vessels, and the parents—and the mandate received by all people and the myriad beings under Heaven. Thus, one must strive to rectify them.

Therefore, in my practice of the Dao, I wholly uphold the fundamental precepts and the mean, discarding the superficial. Heaven upholds the fundamental, so I uphold the fundamental; Heaven preaches the mean, so I preach the mean; Heaven discards the superficial, so I discard the superficial. In my writings, I am of one body with Heaven and Earth, of one heart and one intent, of one direction and one principle, of one liking and one disliking, of one Dao and one path. Thus, when the virtuous ruler applies them, there shall be no error. For ten thousand times ten thousand years, they shall not be abandoned—only growing ever more manifest, with no time of obscurity; only growing ever more ordered, with no time of chaos; only growing ever more good, with no time of evil. Thus, it is called *The Utmost and Upright Dao of Heaven*, which embraces the heart of Heaven and Earth. Those who obtain its highest secrets may attain longevity; those who obtain its middle secrets may become the state’s assistants; those who obtain its lowest secrets may always secure their own peace.

I ask: why is yang alone honored and noble, while yin alone is deemed lowly and base?
The divine person says: Yang is alone honored and noble because it upholds the fundamental, ever full and replete with substance. Yin is alone deemed lowly and base because it is empty and devoid of substance—thus, it is despised and held in contempt. Now, yin and yang, male and female, are the very origin from which the primordial qi first arises—the gateway of yin and yang.

The place where humans receive their mandate and life is their root. Thus, when a man receives his mandate, he is full and overflowing, with an abundance below and to his left and right—one solid essence remains. Those above are full and overflowing, ever bestowing upon the lower yin and accumulating surplus. This bestowal is the movement of Great Yang; is there anything it does not generate? Is there anything it cannot accomplish? The accumulation below corresponds to Great Yin and Earth, with patterns and veins aligning with the fields’ divisions. The solid essence on the left corresponds to humanity, while that on the right corresponds to the myriad things. This solidity—this core reality—is benevolence and the love of bestowing, which is why yang is honored as noble. Women are deemed lowly and base because the place where they receive their mandate is empty and void, without fullness or surplus, and thus without solid essence—hence their lowliness.

Thus, the Way of Heaven values the root and guards the origin. One must return to the root and guard the primordial, rightly upholding the examined patterns to dispel confusion. Only then can Heaven endure and Earth last, the state be at peace and the people secure—all because the solid yang delights in bestowing. Yang is Heaven, the ruler; yin is Earth, the minister. Therefore, one reveres yang’s bestowal and thereby nourishes it.

I ask the divine person: how many states are there in the world?
There are eighty-one domains in the central region, and beyond them, another encircling expanse—altogether, the world holds ten thousand states. Farther still, beyond the ordered caverns of the void, the three regions together comprise twelve thousand states, all receiving the teachings of Great Peace. In the first year of Great Peace, people rejoice and act in goodness. In the second year, the earth brings forth great joy. In the third year, grace and favor thoroughly permeate the world. In the fourth year, the winds and qi flow in harmony. In the fifth year, spirits do not wage war, and malevolent forces submit and vanish. In the sixth year, the six norms are fully established. In the seventh year, the Three Luminaries grow brighter. In the eighth year, grace reaches all eight directions. In the ninth year, yin and yang are both content. In the tenth year, the myriad things each attain their proper place. This completes the lesser cycle, and when things combine thrice, Heaven, Earth, and humanity are complete—thus, in thirty years, Great Peace is achieved.

Now, the qi of the Supreme Sovereign emerges, and the true Dao arrives, governing for ten years—this is Lesser Great Peace. If one diligently practices the true Dao for twenty years, Middle Great Peace is attained, wherein emperors and kings below, along with all officials and commoners, follow the true Dao and dispel deceit and falsehood.

The divine person speaks to the perfected one: In ancient times, when first learning the Dao, the spirit roams and guards softness to preserve itself. Accumulating virtue without cease, the Dao leads to immortality—riding clouds and driving dragons through the gates of Heaven, following the celestial rotations like a cycle. The perfected one, through singular devotion, attains longevity, their life linked to Heaven. The Dao of yang accumulates through focused devotion, and daily, singular sincerity brings it to fruition. Without contending for glory or rank, one may yet hold high office. Serving teachers with filial piety, the Dao naturally comes. The spirits recognize goodness, and people speak with them.

The teacher who opens one’s understanding is the beginning of the Dao. The ruler, father, and teacher are the gates of destiny for the world. Revering and serving these three, the Dao unfolds in great measure. Failing to serve them, one’s chamber is closed without a door—blessings and virtue flee, while misfortune and chaos take pity. Examine these matters carefully, and do not lose the words of this text.

Parents give life, while teachers instruct in relationships. Serving them with devotion—can one not be cautious? The noblest in the world abandon office to become immortals. Immortality has no end, and life connects to Heaven. Local officials govern the people, while immortal officials serve as celestial officers—what business do they have with the mundane? Their affairs differ. Local officials govern the people and the myriad spirits; the world’s affairs each have their ruler. Strive to think of goodness, and your body may remain whole. Thus departing, you do not betray your ancestors.

My illustrated texts are now exhausted, and nothing more can be set forth. Exert yourself in study and carefully inquire into these writings.

The divine person is about to depart and thus admonishes the perfected one: Be cautious, be cautious! Do not transmit this recklessly. To one unworthy, do not reveal it. Hide it deep in the abyss, in the darkness between the unseen. The Dao does not drink blood, nor does it speak of essential texts. What is external and internal is already complete—nothing more can be said.

Here, the divine person is depicted in feathered robes, ascending to Heaven in a carriage drawn by nine dragons, accompanied by lesser perfected ones on simurghs and cranes, with colorful clouds gathering before them, as if bidding farewell.

On the western wall is an illustration: The ancient divine and perfected ones warned later learners through images of evil—do not act as hidden thieves, do not dislike following proper affairs, and do not indulge in jealousy, which brings death and misfortune. The Way of Heaven cannot be forcibly seized; those who seize it will bring about war, loss of authority, death, and the ruin of their lineage. Stealing divine texts will lead to defeat; seeking profit will instead bring harm—this is the resonance of Heaven and Earth’s nature, the meeting of the spontaneous. Examine joy to endure long; be cautious, be cautious! Do not delight in harm. Goodness arises naturally, while evil self-destructs. Observe these two images and ponder their benefits and harms.

All things under Heaven follow their kind. Even in the space of a hair, there is no error. Yet people are not themselves refined and thus remain ignorant. Once the name of guilt is attached, nothing can be done. Failing to guard the root, one’s death is followed by lingering transgressions. Acting wickedly within, refined qi summon external forces. Thus, ahead lies harm and imprisonment, while behind lurk malevolent spirits, all hastening to fight. Regret comes too late, and one forgets oneself.

Therefore, these images are drawn to warn later worthies as a great caution. Fools do not believe in the Dao and neglect affairs as if indifferent. Yet when they speak, they do not err by even a fraction. Thus, those who guard softness attain longevity, while those who love strife perish. Things follow their kind and cannot return—regret is useless, and spirits become attached.

Seeing the warning and awakening, one may yet return in time. If no harm has been done above, one may still become a good person. The good ascend, while the wicked descend. The Way of Heaven is impartial, and the spontaneous is never lost. Open and unobstructed, it aligns with the heart of Heaven and the will of Earth, transforming Heaven and Earth’s calamities, smoothing their discourse, allowing people to dwell in their places and the myriad things to remain unharmed.

Thus, Heaven sends forth written scriptures, enabling communication across ten thousand myriad leagues, conveying its words to enlighten the virtuous, discern the wicked, and resolve grievances and entanglements. Therefore, the emperor-kings dwell within a hundredfold seclusion, attaining long-lasting peace, their wisdom and clarity reaching distant lands.

Since the Highest Antiquity and Middle Antiquity, many have turned their backs on Heaven and Earth, jointly deceiving their superiors. Hence, disasters and calamities arise daily, and the dead cannot be numbered. The emperor-kings, long distressed, cannot restrain their subordinates from craft and deceit. Thus, Heaven dispatches the three Daoist scriptures to circulate their qi, bringing joy in knowing gains and losses, harmonizing above and below. Admonitions extend to the humble and distant, preventing grievances and entanglements, aligning with the heart of August Heaven. Delighting in the removal of disasters, they prevent Heaven’s wrath.

In the Lower Antiquity, the hearts of people are perverse and obscured, unlike the Three Sovereigns of the Highest Antiquity, whose hearts were simple and sincere, their intentions single-minded. Each delighted in aligning with the heart of Heaven, loyal and trustworthy, never deceiving their superiors—thus, no scriptures were needed. In the Lower Antiquity, petty men are foolish and deluded, distorting words with falsehood, deceiving Heaven and Earth, and hoodwinking emperor-kings. Therefore, Heaven and Earth are often enraged, sending down disasters. When Heaven and Earth’s afflictions are removed, the emperor-kings are secure and long-lived, the people dwell in peace, the myriad things fulfill their heavenly years, free from resentment. Yin and yang proceed in harmony, the host of spirits rejoice greatly, filled with joy—this is the essential Dao.

If a son is unfilial, he cannot exert himself to nourish his parents. If a disciple is disobedient, he cannot fully devote himself to following the Dao of his enlightened teacher.

A minister who is disloyal cannot fully devote himself to reverently serving his lord. For these three conducts—failing in filial piety, loyalty, or obedience—the guilt cannot be absolved. Heaven detests them, ghosts and spirits harm them, and all people despise them. Even in death, their blame lingers in the underworld, branded as those whose three conducts were unruly and unvirtuous. Each month’s final bright dawn, they are summoned to face Heaven, which governs the rectification of yin and yang. The spirits and officials of high and low ranks grieve for their souls, tormented until annihilation.

Heaven sets fifteen days as a minor reckoning, thus the moon wanes after the fifteenth day. A month serves as a middle reckoning, and a year as a great reckoning. The myriad spirits and essences between Heaven and Earth jointly assist Heaven in nurturing the twelve thousand beings, and thus all spirits and essences receive their allotted sustenance. This is like worthy ministers aiding the emperor-king in nurturing all people and things, so that all receive their due.

Therefore, Heaven establishes the law: all spirits report in minor audience on the fifteenth day of the month, in middle audience once a month, and in great audience once a year. Those with great merit are promoted and elevated; those without merit are demoted or punished. Those who disrupt governance are the spirits of perversity and evil.

If one lives as a filial son, a loyal minister, and an obedient disciple, never departing from these virtues, then after death, one’s soul, spirit, and essence will not face judgment. For the two reckonings: those who study my Daoist scriptures, aligning them with past and present, categorizing them by kind, and grasping their essential meaning—even the most worthy and enlightened rejoice uncontrollably, unable to restrain themselves from goodness. If they dare enter the thatched chamber, steadfastly guarding the Way without fail, they will surely transcend the world. Their aspiration merges profoundly with the numinous, and they no longer seek praise in worldly affairs. Their goodness pervades Heaven and Earth, and their spirit aids Heaven and Earth, returning to assist the emperor-king in transforming evil. Their benevolence extends even to the smallest blades of grass, and none fail to receive its transformative virtue.

Thus, in antiquity, the worthy and enlightened who found a teacher and could aid the emperor-king in achieving Great Peace were all such people. The moderately worthy, diligently studying my scriptures, aligning them with ancient and modern Daoist texts, categorizing them by kind, and studying them earnestly—those among them of sufficient talent may ascend to become good ministers and virtuous officials, aiding the virtuous ruler in transforming evil. Their benevolence reaches even the smallest blades of grass. Yin and yang harmonize, and warfare ceases. The emperor-king enjoys long tranquility without trouble, while all ministers below teach and strive together, all obedient and virtuous, loyal and trustworthy. Governance proceeds without punishment, and evil cannot prevail.

When the people collectively study my Daoist scriptures, high and low unite in shared purpose, acting as one. No one remains who knows how to commit wickedness. They collate and categorize ancient and modern Daoist texts, linking them by kind, making them the learning of the age, passed down from father to son without end. When the three grades—superior, middling, and common—all practice this, the malevolent qi of Heaven and Earth is entirely dispelled, and no further calamities of karmic inheritance arise. Goodness harmonizes yin and yang, the qi of Heaven and Earth aligns, and auspicious signs emerge, roaming the emperor’s capital. This is the proof of the joy and delight of the August Heaven and Earth.

Therefore, those who study my texts should examine them with utmost care. For the three reckonings: those who attain the Dao will surely encounter spirits who empower them. The most worthy and enlightened govern ten out of ten matters perfectly and may serve as the emperor’s ministers, driving away perversity and eliminating evil. Some may, after a long time, enter the chamber and transcend the world, no longer seeking praise in worldly affairs. Thus, only by guarding the One can one fully know good and evil, merits and faults; only then can one guard the Dao. By entering the chamber and refining one’s thoughts, one can then guard the spirit—this is the third stage.

The worthy collate and verify ancient and modern divine scriptures. The moderately worthy guard the One and enter the Dao, eventually witnessing the spirits themselves. They govern nine out of ten matters perfectly and may serve as great ministers to kings and lords, driving away perversity and eliminating evil. With time, they may hope to enter the chamber. The lesser worthy guard the One, enter the Dao, and study the scriptures, sometimes witnessing the spirits. They govern eight out of ten matters perfectly and may serve the people in driving away perversity and eliminating evil. They, too, collate and verify ancient and modern Daoist texts, proving the Way to themselves, so that even the foolish come to understand and believe in the Dao.

When the great worthy, the middling worthy, and the common people all guard the divine Dao and practice it, the spirits of Heaven and Earth and the four seasons all assist them, and perversity naturally vanishes. Thus, the spirits of Heaven above, Earth below, the four directions, the six relations, and the six kinships all rejoice. Heaven promotes goodness and aids people in auspiciousness.

My Dao governs Heaven and Earth, pacifies the emperor-king, and gives life to what Heaven and Earth love—thus, one must love the true Dao and true virtue. Heaven is the truth of the Dao, its guiding principle, its faithfulness, and the course by which it moves. Earth is the chief of virtue, its guiding thread, and the foundation upon which it rests. Thus, it is the mother of the myriad things, enduring humiliation and dwelling below, never boasting of its toil.

As the Virtuous Lord, I teach and transform the ignorant, taking these two matters of Heaven and Earth as my foundation. Thus, I always follow the laws of Heaven and Earth, never straying from their gate and threshold. My scriptures are the words of Heaven and Earth, deeply and uniquely resonant with the gods and spirits, like the exterior and interior of a single body.

All names under Heaven today are categorized by kind, so one may know their proper affiliation. Those who embody the Five Surnames in abundance resemble yang and are benevolent; those who embody the Six Passions in abundance resemble yin and are greedy. Those who receive more yang bestowal become male; those who receive more yin bestowal become female. Those who receive more qi of prosperity and dominance are noble and single-minded; those who receive more qi of decline, decay, and imprisonment suffer frequent illness, die young, and live in extreme poverty.

Thus, all who are born embody the qi of the Five Phases they resemble. Their fate is determined by the Six Jia and Five Calendars, categorized by kind according to the ancients—never erring even once.

The sages of antiquity delved deeply into the origins of all matters, understanding human nature through this. Do the Perfected Ones comprehend this? Gazing upward to emulate the heavens in conduct, one may act in accordance with celestial patterns; looking downward to emulate the earth in conduct, one transforms through the earth’s virtue and power. Reflecting that heaven and earth, as father and mother, gave me life and growth, they do not wish me to delight in evil—thus, I examine my heart before acting. The heart is the most revered spirit concealed within. The heart is the sacred, pure yang fire. When this fire moves, it ascends, sharing the same radiance as heaven. Thus, the sun, sovereign of fire, governs all under heaven with impartial illumination. Therefore, when a person embodies utmost sincerity, the pain of the heart’s rectitude ascends as the sacred spirit, rising to the sun and moon, and further ascending to heaven. Thus, utmost sincerity within is the numinous spirit—how can one not be cautious?

Heaven acts through the utmost Dao; earth acts through the utmost virtue. The utmost virtue is the foundation of the household, jointly nurturing the myriad things without concealment or partiality. The sages of antiquity emulated heaven and earth in their conduct, employing the utmost Dao and essential virtue to instruct the foolish, guiding them to prudence and goodness, making governance effortless. Yet in this age, such ways are often obstructed and severed, so the foolish collectively engage in cunning and deceit, losing the Dao of heaven. Unaware of their own wrongdoing, they fail to practice the true Dao and benevolent virtue, thus many incur heavenly punishment, meeting deaths that remain unabsolved.

Now, the Celestial Master broadly opens the path of the heavenly Dao, meticulously collating the texts of ancient Daoist scriptures to establish the true essential and secret Dao. The true Dao abounds in goodness; its writings enter the divine, enabling one to perceive spirits and govern alongside them. When the spirit enters the divine, it is the true Dao. Many attain this in secluded chambers; some are enabled to transcend within their rooms and depart, while others enter and exit without yet being able to leave. Some merely perceive the spirits but remain bound through the ages. Those who conduct themselves as disciples of the Dao and study to attain high office must resolve their intentions.

For all people, focused inquiry is key. Entering the gate of learning today, one must concentrate the mind, constantly desiring to benefit and cherish others without uttering falsehoods. Those who study in youth yet persist in ignorance into old age do not delight in attaining office. Yet those who diligently study, striving to comprehend the classics and the Dao, ceaselessly accumulating goodness—whose conduct and learning establish their reputation, whose mastery of the classics and Dao deepens their understanding of the origins of ancient and modern calamities—bring benefit to superiors and advantage to inferiors. Their accumulated goodness cannot be concealed, and their names resound in all directions. Enlightened rulers favor them, summoning and appointing them, while all praise, "Excellent is this person!" Those who rejoice in their virtue are those who study the Dao and transcend the world.

I further expound the Dao to disciples: those who do not transcend, though they enter the gate of learning today, take no delight in pondering the true Dao or its benevolent teachings. Instead, they seek vast knowledge and broad observation, aspiring to exhaust the ways of the sages. Yet they do not desire to practice goodness, preferring instead the superficial embellishments of rhetoric that enable deception. Even after entering the classics and the Dao, their minds remain unfocused, constantly indulging in falsehoods and verbal disputes, making harm to others their vocation. They disrespect superiors and fail to cherish inferiors. Their mastery of the classics and Dao remains hollow, unfit to serve as worthy ministers to emperors and kings, instead becoming leaders of disorder. Relying on others’ wealth to advance themselves, they seek high office to elevate their reputation, then embezzle public resources for private gain, betraying superiors to benefit subordinates. Such are the disruptors who undermine proper governance, the scourges of heaven and earth, the traitors to the state. They are tigers and wolves among the people, wicked children to their parents. Heaven and earth detest them; ghosts and spirits abhor them. Thus, their crimes warrant execution by the emperor to align with the will of heaven, to eliminate the great harm to the people—these are the deceitful who attain office.

Some, though their minds lack sincerity and substance, harboring no true steadfastness, instead constantly scheme to obtain office. Office is the celestial constellation’s domain, bestowed upon the virtuous and rewarding the meritorious—not recklessly given to the undeserving. The undeserving are disregarded by heaven and earth, unloved by spirits and deities. The foolish, unable to deeply recognize their own faults, persist in vainly desiring celestial office. Malevolent spirits and entities then enter their hearts, compelling them to utter falsehoods and perverse speech, which they cannot restrain. Thus, some perish through perverse words—this is the meaning. Not only does misapprehending the Dao bring misfortune, but the Perfected Ones must strive in the art of self-transcendence.

The sages and worthies of antiquity observed the luminous laws of heaven and thus practiced the Dao and upheld virtue. Heaven is singularly focused, moving day and night in the Dao without speech, thus enduring in fortune. Earth moves day and night in the Dao without speech, nurturing the myriad things, thus enduring in singular fortune. The four seasons move day and night in the Dao without ceasing, thus perpetually flourishing and reigning without end. The Three Luminaries alone follow the true Dao without speech, thus perpetually radiant, moving in accord with heaven. The Five Phases alone follow the true Dao without speech, thus enduring with heaven and earth. All under heaven who practice the Dao emulate these—innumerable are the examples. Constantly cherishing and benefiting others, refraining from reckless speech, the Dao may be attained. Those who lightly dismiss my words are harmed by the Dao.

I speak as the discourse of heaven to admonish the virtuous ruler. When a virtuous ruler arises in heaven, they must love the Dao, and the myriad people will emulate their ruler, all taking this text as a warning. Thus, heaven’s emulation and law are most exalted, without superior; in reversal, most humble, without inferior. Its greatness has no exterior; in reversal, its smallness has no interior. It encompasses and nurtures the myriad things, bestowing benefit and blessing upon the good and evil, great and small alike, endowing them with primordial qi to give life, ultimately without harm or injury. Thus, it is most fittingly called the divine, the supreme ruler of heaven.

Now the qi of the Supreme Sovereign arrives, and the virtuous ruler governs, emulating this as their model. Thus, my Dao rises and falls, sinks and floats, desiring that the multitude of worthies deliberate upon it together.

The earthly gate of the southeast holds the waters of heaven and earth, which do not resist even the smallest currents—good and evil, great and small all return to it. Do you, Perfected One, comprehend this?

Among the myriad scrolls of texts, only those that can extend a person’s years and augment their lifespan are true scriptures; the rest are not. Among the texts filling a chamber, only those that can secure the heart of heaven and bring about equitable governance are true scriptures; the rest are not. Among the ministers filling the court, only those who delight in their ruler and assist them in achieving Great Peace are the true ministers and worthy officials of the emperor; the rest are merely functionaries. Among the children a person bears, only those whose parents constantly enjoy their joy and suffer neither hunger nor cold are filial and virtuous; the rest are but numbers to be filled. Among the accumulated prescriptions and heavy carts of remedies, only those that can all extend years are true formulas; the rest are not.

The world abounds with such examples, too numerous to name or foretell. Perfected One, deeply ponder their meaning. My scripture, by inferring from one to ten thousand, suffices to illuminate the Dao of the world. Thus, I charge you, Perfected One, to transmit the Dao to the virtuous ruler, to examine and distinguish all common texts and the words of those who claim sagely writings, clearly demonstrating them to the multitude of worthies, so that all may together awaken and dispel delusion.

Once all common texts are examined and distinguished, the days of calamity will depart. For perverse texts and perverse words are the masters of treacherous disasters. True texts and true words are the officials who subdue treacherous evil. With true texts and true words, and with officials who rectify treachery, falsehoods will have no master and thus no place to abide. Perverse words as masters of treachery are like thieves who have a place to lodge; once the master perishes, thieves have no means to return and rest.

In practicing the model of the Dao of heaven, by inferring from one to ten thousand, the ten thousand cannot all be written. Excessive texts bewilder people; it is better to raise one guiding principle, so that the myriad strands arrange themselves and unfold. Thus, the clamor of ten thousand people is not equal to one emperor. The countless stars, myriad as they are, are not equal to the brightness of a single sun. The words of those who strive to support heaven and all below are not equal to one worthy and good person in the state. The Dao of heaven is vast and boundless, without limit, yet it is not equal to the primordial qi holding the guiding principle of heaven’s mandate.

If the worthy and virtuous ruler ponders my words, their lifespan will naturally lengthen. If later generations together ponder my words, fathers will be kind and sons filial, and this will daily expand and become clearer. Great and small will vie in doing good, and there will be no more violence. No longer will there be perverse texts or flatterers lurking in the state. Disasters and anomalies will be entirely eradicated, and the Three Luminaries will shine brightly. This is the natural art, which the Celestial Masters together purify.

In practicing the Dao thus, what harm could there be? Proceeding in this way as a model is the very movement of heaven. To record and preserve these writings is to contemplate the divine clarity of heaven and earth. The texts that verify this resonate with heaven and earth, forming a covenant of trust. Worthy rulers and the virtuous should together deliberate upon these words; those who practice them will daily flourish, aligning with the times to form a court that fulfills the desires of heaven and earth—thus, how auspicious!

I, on behalf of the virtuous ruler of Great Peace, establish these models and measures, without limiting them to one person. When the qi of Great Peace arrives, if even one person remains aggrieved, unable to attain their desire, then the qi of the Supreme Sovereign and Great Peace cannot arrive together. Thus, heaven instructs me to broadly open the path, allowing each to freely choose what they may do.

Those of wisdom and brightness who desire to live joyfully may study my scriptures, ponder their meaning, enter the chamber, and accomplish the Dao—they may attain life. Those of gentle virtue who desire to assist the emperor in governance may emulate my scriptures in their actions—they may bring about Great Peace. Those who desire to manage their households and engage in commerce may ponder my scriptures—they may complete their natural lifespan, each attaining their wishes without great grievance.

Thus, when the virtuous ruler governs, the qi of Great Peace arrives. The reason for this is that there are no aggrieved persons in the world; each attains what they desire. The worthy and enlightened virtuous ruler does not seize what others desire and must win the hearts of the world, desiring to comply with heaven’s will and return to it. The movement of heaven does not seize what people desire; the movement of earth does not seize what people desire. The enlightened ruler emulates this and thus achieves Great Peace.

Heaven and earth, most divine, do not seize what others desire—how much less should humans? The divine persons of high antiquity admonished their disciples and later learners to cultivate good and model virtue, secretly aiding and benefiting people to ensure constant auspiciousness, their merit multiplied. Overt goodness is met with human responses and resolves. Covert goodness is known by heaven, earth, and all spirits, thus their merit is multiplied.

Those who accumulate virtue are beloved by the wealthy, and their goodness naturally comes to them. What people praise, ghosts and spirits also praise, thereby aiding and assisting them. Those who love the Dao attain long life, sharing the concerns of yin and yang, following the movement of the August Spirit, the nature of heaven and earth, and attaining the principle of the Dao—thus, heaven protects them. Those who lose this disrupt heaven and do not love good people.

Seeking goodness through goodness is nothing strange. Learning through benevolence is the beginning of the Dao; attaining it through virtue is the harmony of the Dao; attaining it through the Dao is the highest. I originally studied little but did not cease, concentrating my spirit and reflecting upon it, tears often falling. Through long accumulation, I received the great grace of August Heaven, and today I fortunately encountered the divine persons of heaven in the wilderness.

At the beginning of my studies, I was deficient, pondering and inquiring about trivial matters and superficial embellishments. Originally seeking the method of guarding the One and nurturing nature, I composed three hundred verses, only to see the Celestial Master expound without limit. Thus, I dared to ask: Can the tranquility of the body be attained and long life preserved?

You come to study and inquire on behalf of heaven; I suspect heaven has bestowed this upon you. I wish to hear the essential meaning—by what is this made clear?

Now should a virtuous ruler obtain this scripture, comprehend it in heart, and practice it—discussing it with all worthy ministers to transform the common people—then surely a resonant response shall arise, which is its clear proof.

My Dao is perfected through precepts, not through false words or deeds. This is the decisive principle.

I have long embraced this Dao, yet found none with whom to speak. Heaven’s grievances have knotted severely, and afflictions transform without cease. In this stifled impasse, how could the Celestial Master go forth and transmit it?

It is said: The position is not fitting. My office resides in heaven; the Perfected One’s office resides on earth. Those on earth bring forth the myriad things, thus heaven’s creations are nurtured upon the earth. Therefore, I transmit the Dao to the Perfected One. The earth gives birth to rulers, common folk, and the twelve thousand beings—all receive yang’s bestowal, emerging from within yin. Thus, you may transmit it to humankind.

You doubt the sincerity of my words. Though heaven issues its decrees, it does not speak directly to mortals—yet our intentions are one. This scripture bears heaven’s mandate, its clarity like cinnabar and ink.

This is the origin of heaven’s numbering. Thus, before heaven and earth divided, accumulated qi congealed as one, then split into two, forming husband and wife. Heaven’s bestowal descends to earth, conceiving in the dark mystery, named as *jiazi*. Its roots spread in the northeast, in *chou* and *yin*. It first appears in *mao*, completing the southeast in *chen* and *si*. Its branches hang in the south, nurtured at *wu*. Turning old in the southwest, in *wei* and *shen*. Maturing in the west, the sun sets in *you*. Fully concealed in the northwest, in *xu* and *hai*.

Thus, numbering begins at one and ends at ten, for this is the origin of the five thousand and the root of the five phases. Multiply one by ten, and a hundred is complete. Therefore, heaven generates within, and thus all things reach their end herein. The Dipper is established in *chen* and broken in *xu*. *Established* means to stand—thus all things desire to reach full growth. *Broken* means to decay—all things perish completely in *xu*.

Numbering the eight directions of heaven and earth, ten completes the cycle. Yin and yang establish and break, thus this pattern recurs, following the Dipper’s pointer to illuminate affairs. This scripture is for dispelling harmful qi, thus it is said: “Model heaven as the standard.”

*End of Tai ping jing chao, Ji Section, Scroll Six*
*Tai ping jing chao, Geng Section, Scroll Seven*

The *Admonition on the Diagram of the Void and Spontaneous Dao’s Necessary Fulfillment*

The void is inwardly replete yet outwardly empty—being as if non-being. Reverse the womb and embryo to dwell with the Dao. Preserve only the heart, suspending dragon-like contemplation. Thus it becomes the spirit-chamber, gathering the Dao in emptiness. Roam only with qi, hence the void. In qi and spirit, all else is eliminated. With the heart as master, one attains freedom from deviation. Examine its meaning closely, never forgetting the true scripture. Attain this, and you transcend the world, roaming long within it. Why not refine your essence, only to remain with fools? Once misfortune arrives, great disaster befalls. Abandon true simplicity, and you revert to dust and ash. The wise heed the scripture’s admonition.

Non-action is non-action that accomplishes all, linking with the Dao. It emerges before infancy, enters the seamless, and reaches the Great Beginning, then returns. At heaven and earth’s inception, yin and yang had their source. Enter the art of non-action, and the body may be preserved whole. To depart from root and branch is the Dao’s affliction. To leave the Great Beginning is to forfeit wholeness. The farther one strays from life, the nearer to death’s gate. Indulging in vulgar learning harms the soul and spirit. Clinging to duality while forgetting the One loses their mutual resonance. Can one not be admonished? This is the Dao’s origin.

You, who guard the One exclusively, are the wellspring of benevolence and wisdom. Heaven’s Dao moves as One, thus it remains complete. Earth’s Dao moves as Two, and neighbors with ghosts. Truly know non-action, and you align with the Dao’s utmost spirit. Reflect deeply on this matter—the perfected ones preceded you. Seal your golden gate, allowing nothing to depart. In silence without sound, the spirit endures, and qi is perfected. The gate of immortal Dao is thus attained. How effortless! The Great Dao is no longer burdensome. Heaven’s Dao, impartial, returns to the benevolent and wise.

The law of spontaneity links with the Dao. Guard it, and fortune follows; lose it, and calamity arises. All things arise self-complete, one root with myriad branches, none without spirit. Ponder its meaning, and the Dao reveals itself. Together they emerge from primal chaos through the wondrous gate, neither increasing nor diminishing, preserving spontaneity.

All things born possess spirit, and of the eighteen hundred breaths, humans are supreme. Thus one may avoid death and attain long-lasting transcendence. Those who perish early lose spontaneity—even birds and beasts endure, let alone humans. Fools despise the Dao, sinking to earth’s depths. The benevolent and wise esteem the Dao, ascending heaven’s gate. The spirit-Dao does not die; ghosts and spirits meet their end.

Should you pursue this, it is like a ring without end. Beware of entering the realm of being, lest you invite harm. Neither act recklessly nor abandon restraint, lest you hasten death. Heaven and earth’s nature uniquely honors spontaneity. Each follows its course—none dare oppose it.

The Dao flourishes through non-action, the void and spontaneity. The lofty delight in it; the base disregard it. Study diligently and know your teacher—no words are forbidden. With a teacher, the Dao is clear; without one, transmission is difficult. Learning without a master’s instruction, the noble remain silent. Reckless action brings chaos; self-mutilation invites misfortune.

When the Dao is fully prepared, spontaneity is achieved. The three Daoist scriptures are all derived from collective deliberation, taken as heaven’s trust, and their resonance brings swift efficacy. To rectify the spirit and numinous, the decision rests with the illumination of ten thousand people, taken as heaven’s trust. To correct ordinary texts, the decision rests with collation, taken as heaven’s trust.

Those who wish to know the truth of this scripture may verify it through swift insight. Practice it, and it will resonate with heaven. The good will flourish daily; the evil will diminish, taken as heaven’s trust. To appoint worthy individuals, the decision rests with nine people. To discern who has entered the chamber and who has not, the decision rests with absolute clarity—no concealment or obstruction, taken as heaven’s trust.

To know if one’s body has attained the Dao and become deathless, the decision rests with the body’s transformation into spirit, thus transcending the world, taken as heaven’s trust. To thoroughly understand the meaning of this scripture, read it from beginning to end, then reflect inwardly. The heart will comprehend fully, and doubt will vanish. Once its meaning is grasped, it cannot be abandoned.

To test the efficacy of this scripture and distinguish truth from falsehood, apply it to govern toward Great Peace, taken as heaven’s trust. To know whether longevity is attainable, the decision rests with the era after Great Peace. If Great Peace has not yet come, prior generations’ disasters will cause harm, making efficacy difficult, taken as heaven’s trust.

For the Grand Yang to know Great Peace, the decision rests with the severing of metal. For water and fire to suppress and eliminate treacherous ministers and malevolent forces, the decision rests with the severing of metal and the decline of market wine. To see the great flourishing of heaven’s Dao, the decision rests with collating all texts and consulting with ordinary people.

To obtain efficacious medicine, collate all medical texts and test them. To hasten Great Peace, reveal all true texts and eliminate false ones. To delight in humanity and cease harming women, the decision rests with each residing in their place, providing according to their ability, ensuring parents are not burdened with sorrow or rebellion.

To eliminate illness and widely open the Dao, the decision rests with swallowing the cinnabar script’s characters. To know the method of compiling and practicing the scriptures, follow the text and emphasize its admonitions. Restrain yourself well, practice for a day, and a hundred harms will vanish from the heart. In an instant, all will be rectified, taken as heaven’s trust.

May I ask: what is the name of auspicious omens? Why do you persist in folly?

Would the Heavenly Master not abandon me and grant me but a single word of instruction?

As for auspicious omens: they are purity, stillness, rectitude, and singular devotion—where the heart aligns with heaven and earth, never transgressing the seasons’ decrees.

May I ask: by what means can one know this purity, stillness, rectitude, and singular devotion?

Excellent is your question. The nature of heaven and earth, from ancient times to the present, is such that the good bring forth goodness, the wicked bring forth wickedness, the upright bring forth uprightness, and the perverse bring forth perversity. This is the natural principle—nothing strange in it.

Thus, when the human heart is upright, pure, and still, and sincerity moves heaven, without any ill intent, auspicious responses and good omens converge, and so auspicious omens arise. Those who employ deceitful and false hearts in all matters of perversity receive no good response—this is the great and luminous proof of heaven and earth. Do you understand?

Good and evil each have their responses. Those who fail to harmonize bring about disharmony—this is the clear evidence of heaven.

Excellent. May I ask: when people do good—supreme filial children, supreme loyal ministers, supreme obedient disciples—what should they hold in highest regard toward their lord, father, and teacher? It is to present rare treasures, texts seldom seen, and thereby attain the highest.

Loyal ministers, filial children, and obedient disciples should always delight in such deeds. Why then do they not present what is commonly known, but instead present what is rare?

What is commonly known, the superior already possesses—why present it again?

This foolish student does not grasp the meaning.

I shall soon make it clear to you.

What the world deems rare and precious—things never before seen and yet of great worth—when presented to one’s lord, this is the act of a supremely loyal minister. Rare and excellent food never before seen, when presented to one’s parents, this is the act of a supremely filial child. Teachings never before heard, when presented to one’s teacher, this is the act of a supremely good disciple. Do you understand?

I would hear of presenting what is already held in common.

What the superior already possesses, yet is presented again—why?

Because all things respond accordingly, such repeated presentation does not remove the fault. Why is it so weighty?

You should not fail to understand: what people already possess in common, to present it again is wearisome—why present it once more?

From ancient times to the present, the great sages’ determination in all matters has been to discard the common and select the rare, thereby aligning with the will of heaven and earth. This is what is meant.

Heaven has two hands, and by them all things are accomplished. If one hand is afflicted with perversity and evil, nothing can be achieved. Heaven greatly resents this; earth regards it as taboo. The world falls into chaos and accomplishes nothing, all due to one hand’s perversity failing to join in effort.

In all matters, if not properly ordered, the six directions will not attain Great Peace—this too arises from the two hands, when one is afflicted with perversity and fails to join in effort. The fortune or misfortune, safety or peril that ensue all stem from these two hands.

Perfected One, do you truly comprehend this deeply?

Were it not for the Heavenly Master revealing its essential meaning, how could one come to know it? Those who know it remain in eternal darkness and confusion, with no way to attain understanding.

The teacher is the root of all instruction in heaven and earth’s myriad affairs—though difficult, how could one refrain from speaking of it?

Excellent indeed are the Perfected One’s inquiries.

In essence, it is but □□. Be seated, and I shall explain its meaning fully for all Perfected Ones.

Let the world model itself upon this and act accordingly, and no more inauspicious or chaotic affairs will arise. The gods of heaven summon and inscribe the two hands as a crucial record. When a nation practices this, it endures long; when ordinary people practice it, they enjoy lasting wealth and peace.

The essential Dao is about to emerge, near at hand within the body of every person. Now I shall distinguish and explain it for the Perfected Ones.

Heaven and earth are the two hands that create and bring forth all things. The four seasons are the two hands that transmit and nourish all beings. Husband and wife are the two hands that transmit and continue the yin and yang of heaven and earth. Teacher and disciple are the two hands that transmit and communicate all matters of texts, the Dao, and virtue. Ruler and minister are the two hands that transmit and govern all matters concerning the people and the myriad things.

These six matters merely lift the guiding principles and reveal their beginnings—there is no end to what could be written. All things that require mutual support to be accomplished are the two hands. In heaven, this is called "overlapping compasses and repeated squares"—all things that correspond to one another.

If one hand is perverse and unequal, nothing is accomplished. In heaven, this is called "the governance of great chaos." In the six directions and eight distant regions, it is called "widows and widowers, severed lineages," and the days grow ever more degenerate. Nothing is accomplished because the two hands do not join in effort.

May I ask: why in heaven are they called the two hands?

The two hands signify their equal and joint effort, with no advance or retreat—only then can things be accomplished. If the two hands do not join in effort, nothing can be achieved.

Thus, in all matters, one must model them upon these two hands, each finding the right person to join in effort and unite in heart. Only then can this model bring peace, and the qi of Great Peace will immediately arrive. Without modeling upon these two hands, even after ten thousand myriad years, the qi of the Supreme Sovereign’s Great Peace cannot emerge.

The qi of Great Peace constantly desires to emerge, like heaven itself. Yet because the two hands have long failed to harmonize and govern, it remains blocked and unable to flow forth, pent up and resentful—all due to the two hands’ disharmony.

If the two hands are balanced and harmonious, the qi of the Supreme Sovereign’s Great Peace emerges, arriving one after another without delay.

Excellent.

Thus, if heaven and earth do not join in effort, the myriad things have no way to emerge. If the four seasons do not join in effort, all beings have no way to grow. If the five phases do not join in effort, all things have no way to be completed. If ruler and minister do not join in effort, all affairs have no way to be governed. If husband and wife do not join in effort, descendants have no way to flourish, and the family way has no way to be established. If teacher and disciple do not join in effort, no knotted affairs can be untangled, the Dao and virtue have no way to flourish, the mists of ignorance have no way to disperse, and the great transformation of the six directions and eight distant regions has no way to proceed.

Therefore, all must join in effort, just as the two hands—only then can things flow smoothly. Without modeling upon the two hands, misfortune arises, and though one may seek remedies, it is of no benefit—nothing can be accomplished.

Yet mere emptiness and prolonged sorrow bring only daily misfortune. Thus, in all matters resembling these two hands, selection and appointment must secure the right person. To fail in this is called "half-dead" by the gods above—how can one succeed or accomplish anything by acting with but a single hand? In all doubtful matters, ponder deeply this principle.

With a heart of sincerity—born of fire—return it to fire. In governing, model yourself thus, and you shall prolong your years and increase your allotted span, never failing even once. I do not deceive you. This is shown to the virtuous lord, to all people, and to the wise, each to reflect upon its meaning, that none dare transgress it. To employ it is called enriching and nurturing oneself; to neglect it is called bringing sorrow and suffering upon oneself. How wondrous!

The Dao I transmit conveys the will of Heaven. It may only advance, never retreat; only follow, never oppose. To follow is to fully attain Heaven’s favor; to oppose is to invite disorder and calamity. When human intent turns west while Heaven’s intent turns east, it is called discord with Heaven’s will. Let this be a warning to those who would understand.

Now, when common people recommend scholars to present to the emperor, entrusting them to the state, securing the right person brings great fortune, while failing to do so brings great misfortune. What can be achieved with the right person? What ruin follows without them? All perfected ones must be precise and forthright in this.

Thus, securing the right person brings four blessings, while failing to do so brings four calamities. With the right person, Heaven and Earth, the six directions and eight distant regions are at peace; without them, they are not.

Would you hear the essential meaning? When the recommended scholar is the right person, the ruler above is well-governed, affairs succeed, and constant peace prevails—daily benefiting the ruler: this is the first great blessing. The recommended person is capable and can be entrusted with office: the second blessing. Having become capable, they illuminate the Way of their teacher, extending grace to them: the third blessing. The recommended person proves trustworthy in their duties, further earning the ruler’s trust and employment: the fourth blessing. Joining in effort and with a single heart, their deeds daily succeed, monthly grow more illustrious, and yearly flourish ever more. Heaven and Earth rejoice, good omens appear in full, evil things withdraw, and the gods delight. Holding fast without fail, one may ascend to transcend the world, attain equitable governance in the middle realm, or below, preserve wholeness and complete one’s natural lifespan. Such is the goodness of recommending the right person.

In Heaven above, this is called the Talisman of Continuing Life. Why is it named the Talisman of Continuing Life? Because recommending the right person transforms danger into safety, chaos into order, failure into success, misfortune into fortune, and death into life. Above, one may transcend the world; in the middle, attain governance and peace; below, complete one’s natural lifespan and preserve one’s body.

Yet if the recommended scholar is not the right person, they bring no benefit to the emperor or the state, plunging governance into disorder. The emperor suffers in every way, Heaven and Earth are displeased, and thieves, bandits, and myriad disasters arise: this is the first great calamity. The recommended person cannot govern their office, deceit and falsehood daily increase, and long-standing unrest ensues. They cannot preserve their natural lifespan, may be harmed by Heaven and Earth’s spirits, or murdered by others, bringing disgrace to their parents and spreading evil to their wives, children, and descendants—known as a wicked person for their faults: this is the second great calamity. Their wickedness leads to the abandonment of their learning, defiling the sacred work of former sages and bringing disaster to their teacher: the third great calamity. Moreover, the recommender is untrustworthy, deceiving their ruler, presenting the wrong person, disrupting Heaven’s order, and defiling the constellations. Heaven detests them, Earth resents them, the ruler despises them, and sages condemn them—called a great deceiver and liar of the age. For this, they shall be punished: if not by Heaven, Earth, and the spirits, then by people. Their ancestors are disgraced, and disaster befalls their wives and children: this is the fourth great calamity.

To commit these four great calamities by recommending the wrong person brings sorrow to the emperor. Harmful qi stirs and cannot be restrained; disorder spreads without end, each fault compounding the last. Heaven and Earth grow furious, ministers contend, the six directions are displeased, the eight distant regions fall into discord, and eternal disorder ensues. In Heaven above, this is called the Talisman of Diminished Years and Shortened Life. Why is it named the Talisman of Shortened Life? Because order reverts to disorder, long years become few, and all undertakings meet misfortune, bringing no benefit to oneself. Heaven and Earth are displeased, deducting from one’s allotted span and diminishing one’s years—thus, it is called the Talisman of Shortened Life in Heaven above.

Excellent indeed! This celestial text is shown to the virtuous lord, to all people and the wise, extending even to the common folk.

When one in high position seeks worthy officers, one must be meticulous; when one in low position recommends them, one must be loyal. If later generations transmit and recite this text, treasuring it in their hearts, yet hastily appoint officers without adhering to its principles, Heaven and Earth will no longer be pleased. To know the Way yet deliberately violate it—how severe will the punishment be! Take heed.

This celestial text resolves the Six Extremities, gathering the great assembly of Heaven above. In the eighth month, the books are reviewed, mirroring the laws of Heaven and Earth to eliminate disasters and harms. Only the Dao of highest antiquity, wherein one cultivates the self and rectifies one’s conduct, dares not transgress what the divine spirits have transgressed, yet dares to seek life and plead for survival from the Heavenly Lord. One dares not act wantonly, fearing imperfection. Daily, one contemplates the vitality of life, becoming one with the divine spirits, manifesting their kind. Desiring to receive words of utmost loyalty and integrity, one clarifies right and wrong with the spirits governing all departments, then dares to trust in the principles of justice and injustice—how could there be a moment’s forgetfulness?

Above, there are those who observe humanity, fully discerning right and wrong. What can be concealed? What can be disbelieved? Thus, one attains self-governance, seeking and reflecting on the root. Never has there been the slightest boundary of unvirtuous conduct. One merely cherishes being human, relying on and revering the primordial qi, enabling all creeping and moving creatures to avoid witnessing calamities and anomalies.

Yet people betray trust in their sworn words, neither party believing the other, hence the lack of peace. Within the harmony of Heaven and Earth, above and below each maintain their trust, but people fail to grasp its essence. Humans consume the qi of the Five Constants, receiving and relying on nothing they do not partake of, yet losing goodness and following evil, their lives incomplete—why is this so? Thus, the Heavenly Lord declares that there is always good and evil, and those who ought to uphold justice. Therefore, errors and evils clarify the intent of Heaven and Earth, the Four Seasons, and the Five Phases, enabling understanding that the completion of life is paramount, extending one’s years and lifespan. People attain the Dao of life and completion, adhering to its prohibitions without negligence.

From this, it is clear that Heaven knows the foolish are shallow, lacking any intent of requital. To oppose Heaven’s actions is to contradict its works, amplifying human misdeeds—reversing the proper order to condemn the living and favor the wicked. Thus, the sage understands the convergence of yin and yang, the worthy govern right and wrong, resolving what is unknown, enabling each to fulfill their duty without resentment. The good naturally enjoy long life; the evil naturally suffer short lives—what is there to doubt or resent?

The virtuous inscribe the writings of goodness, not losing their pattern, their constancy, or their appropriateness—this is called supreme virtue. Nothing is left unaccomplished, nothing unachieved. They do not lose their clarity, their substance, the generation and completion of yin and yang, the ingress and egress of the life-generating qi governed by the Four Seasons, the completion of the Five Phases, the celestial bodies of sun, moon, and stars, their measurements, the timing of fortune and misfortune, the transformations of calamities and anomalies, the records of floods and droughts, or the length of human life—nor do they lose the intent of the thickness or thinness bestowed by the constellations. This is what the supremely virtuous ought to practice.

Thus, the virtuous person illuminates all, sees all, harmonizing above, below, and the center, each according with its proper place. Following their virtue, none lose their rightful name—this is called aligning with constancy. The writings of long life bestow glory upon all things: rocks split and sprout, branches hang and leaves spread to serve as clothing, mist, dew, snow, frost, and timely rain serve as drink and food. Growth and completion occur naturally, covering and bearing blossoms and fruit, providing for the people and the earth’s longevity. Named the "water mother" and called "melon" by the people, in the height of summer it serves as water and broth, relied upon by all under Heaven, consumed by all.

Such is the virtuous person who inherits Heaven’s mandate, completes Heaven’s form, and looks to Earth to provide for the people’s sustenance. Practicing reflection and bestowing generosity, none are left without virtue to satiate themselves—this is Heaven’s grace. What Heaven bestows to generate life is vast. To disobey its mandate and speak of spontaneity is to rebel.

Thus, the virtuous person, understanding Heaven’s intent, teaches the people to establish laws without losing Heaven’s favor, nurturing and raising them to maturity, enabling them to become human, to comprehend patterns and principles, to cultivate virtue and achieve completion, and to ascend to the ranks of Heaven’s officers. In Heaven’s affairs, merits and labors are differentiated.

The virtuous person, presiding over Earth’s affairs, commands the people to rely on and revere, deeply witnessing grace and bestowal, yet unable to requite it in due time. When the virtuous act on Heaven’s behalf, moving qi above, below, and at the center, those who do not receive their proper place scorn Heaven’s works. This is precisely what provokes Heaven’s unceasing wrath, causing the divine spirits to cease loving humanity, encroaching upon and seizing their years and lifespan. People then resent and blame Heaven, so the divine texts are sent down to prevent transgressions.

When one receives great kindness, even a single contrary thought or effort to do good is sufficient. Yet if one remains long in doubt and suspicion, clinging to past grievances, one harms oneself, living in constant dread, unaware of the cause. Heaven endows humans with knowledge of good and evil, and those who practice goodness with sincerity—Heaven does not wish people to have an evil reputation. Thus, desiring to cling to life and abhor death, one dares not violate prohibitions, as if they were harmful to oneself.

Therefore, following the qi of Heaven and communicating with the words of the enlightened, one speaks of the body’s comings and goings, understanding human sentiments. Seeing unvirtuous conduct, one retreats and self-reproaches, fearing that one’s name may be sullied in the celestial records. As one’s intentions at the time are applied to others, one dares not face them directly to explain complexities, but accepts the reproach for one’s actions. Striving to reflect, one considers the progress of one’s merits from birth, resolving the inherited burdens of one’s ancestors. When these burdens are removed and resolved, and transgressions exhausted, one may ascend.

To alternate between good and evil is to toy with one’s fate. Moreover, the good ought to endure temporary hardship, applying effort without negligence, and later receive blessings. When life speaks of enduring trials, accepting admonitions, and retiring to a tranquil place to reflect on one’s faults and self-reproach—these thoughts arise from within, and the celestial spirits know them. Do not grow weary. To foresee the Heavenly Lord’s intentions and actions is to be the foremost person, worthy to stand at the Heavenly Lord’s left side.

Those with meritorious deeds receive rewards, yet in humility dare not advance to accept greater benefits, instead exhausting their sinews and strength, applying their minds with utmost care for the great Dao. Thus, the Heavenly Lord values them anew, personally admonishing and instructing them—this is the blessing of life. To govern many with an impartial heart is sufficient in itself. To say, "I dare not," is to aspire to stand at the Heavenly Lord’s left side, merely to live on.

Only think of loyalty and filial piety, following principle to fulfill one’s duty. Dare not accept heavy rewards, fearing one’s lack of merit. Upon hearing of another’s transgressions, aid them in repentance. Examine and restrain one’s conduct, preventing violations, and contemplate the Heavenly Lord’s will. Knowing goodness, act with goodness; knowing trustworthiness, act with trustworthiness; knowing loyalty, act with loyalty; knowing compliance, act with compliance; knowing filial piety, act with filial piety—thus, evil deeds shall no longer advance. No transgression, great or small, escapes the Heavenly Lord’s knowledge. The register of good and ill is thinly inscribed, and each year, month, and day, accounts are tallied before and after. Years are deducted, lifespan reduced; if evil persists unceasingly, one faces the Ghost Gate. The Earth Spirit summons and interrogates, comparing their deeds and words for consistency. After painful reflection upon principle, only then do they submit. Their name is sent to the celestial bureaus, and when their allotted tally is exhausted, they are cast into the ranks of the Great Transgressors, drifting through later generations—such is the consequence of evil.

One desires to gain advantage from others, yet others do not wish to advantage them. Good advantage brings life; evil advantage is short-lived, for goodness does not long abide upon the earth. Thus, Heaven and Earth’s advantages are not evenly distributed. Heaven causes one to act with goodness, bestowing life, yet one turns to evil—how can the spirits and gods not afflict them with suffering? Whom can they blame? This text thus first advances goodness and retreats from evil—an ancient and enduring scripture.

Life’s mandate lies close within your own body—why knock upon your heart and cry out to Heaven? If your body does not purify itself, whom shall you purify? If your body does not cherish itself, whom shall you cherish? If your body does not perfect itself, whom shall you perfect? If your body does not reflect upon itself, whom shall you reflect upon? If your body does not reproach itself, whom shall you reproach? Ponder these words: do not resent the spirits and gods. For evil, you alone bear the burden, not others—do you understand this?

Act in accordance with what has been said, and let it never depart from your heart. Departure from it is ruin, irreparable, and you shall share the ranks of ghosts—how then shall you live? To reflect upon life is to attain life. How can one, dwelling between Heaven and Earth, forget the grace of Heaven and Earth? What manner of being is this? If you desire Heaven’s recompense, you must reproach yourself with sincerity and sorrow, weeping as you act, saying, "I, favored by grace, am made human, distinct from the myriad things. Heaven has granted me distinction—speech, perception of beauty and ugliness, knowledge of good and evil, right and wrong. I must be meticulous in my conduct." To speak words contrary to Heaven’s decree, refusing compliance, is to be a person of great treason and impiety—how could Heaven long abide with such a one?

If the admonitions received remain unclear, retire to a quiet place to reflect, reproaching yourself for the burdens you bear, and offering thanks to the spirits of Heaven and Earth, the four seasons, the Five Phases, and all the divine departments. The Heavenly Lord listens keenly, bidding you to ponder within. The people of antiquity all possessed wisdom and foresight, dared not transgress prohibitions, and regulated themselves with rectitude, fearing any lapse. At every movement, they acted in accordance with the mandate, lest they lose their years and lifespan. For this reason, they dared not slacken even slightly. For every transgression, there was punishment, and thus they examined and cherished themselves, revering prohibitions and daring not act contrary to the will. When reproached and questioned, their hearts trembled with fear, their qi dispirited and lost, bearing the displeasure of Heaven. Even the slightest misalignment was deemed unworthy, and the text’s complexity often led to thorough investigation and verification. Their words and trustworthiness could be named as honor, and throughout life, they yearned and aspired, aligning with Heaven and Earth, the four seasons, and the Five Phases, bearing the mandate together, daring not commit even the smallest error.

Truly, with the heart, one seeks advancement and searches for life. Only the great spirits review and approve one’s words, allowing one to witness the Four Seasons and Five Phases in their generation and transformation, and to see the difficulty of repaying the sun and moon. One fears being cast aside midway. Those who rightly cultivate the Dao dare not distance themselves, for the Way of the ancient sages arose naturally. Knowing the principles of Heaven above, all their actions are foreknown. Even the faintest sound and echo are understood, and their form and countenance are self-evident. Their hearts are luminous, their intentions clear. They know the matters to be saved, the meetings of fortune and misfortune—all is distinctly apparent. Within, their hearts rejoice, for they know they have received Heaven’s blessing. Witnessing the events of their past conduct, they are all the more vigilant and steadfast.

Reflecting that they have been favored and honored, the great spirits repeatedly admonish and instruct them, ensuring they do not falter. Gazing to the four horizons, above and below all is open and unobstructed. Within their hearts, they rejoice anew, gaining extended years and hearing what was previously unknown—all through the transforming power of the Heavenly Lord and the great spirits. The great spirits declare: "All the spirits know this. Those whose lives are extended have their fate recorded in the true registers. Before birth, their years, months, days, and hours are inscribed in the Bureau of Longevity. When the appointed time arrives, their names ascend, and their deeds are proclaimed, governed by the Perfected of the Northern Culmen. Their bones are transformed, their bodies become light and lustrous. At the appointed hour, they receive the elixir, refining their essence and brilliance. Wherever they manifest, all is accomplished. They emerge from the profound and enter the obscure—what is not accessible to them?"

Only those of antiquity who attained the Dao followed this method. Before birth, their names were recorded in the registers of longevity. When the year, month, day, and hour of their ascension arrive, their names are transmitted to the Central Culmen. The Central Culmen is also called Kunlun, where the governing spirits record their names without omission. They are made to move their limbs, bending and stretching, turning and complying, repeatedly admonished. Following their master through trials, they are given the elixir to drink. Their joints open and are refined. Though not immediately apparent, over time, one knows whether they are firm or not, demonstrating their unyielding resolve.

Craving life and detesting death, they contemplate the affairs of Heaven above. Repeatedly, they are sent to verify the allotted years, to know the prohibitions they must observe. These are transmitted to disciples, and even without divine texts, they speak as if presenting their own books. The spirits know their words, which are also connected to the years and months. After accumulating one thousand three hundred and twenty days, they are led to meet the great spirits, to communicate with the primordial qi, and to act in accordance with nature.

The Heavenly Lord receives the secret decrees and examines conduct, permitting no private trust or wavering of intent, ensuring no errors in action. The Great Spirits declare: "We have calculated the provisions bestowed by all spirits. On the last day of the eighth month, we record the registers of all mountains, seas, ridges, and pools, as well as the waterways, rivers, bridges, Huai, Ji, Yangtze, and lakes—all accounts of ingress and egress—each clearly distinguished."

The Heavenly Lord, when bestowing rewards for labor, personally reviews and verifies the records stored in the golden chambers. Those of sincere heart are appointed to attend the Heavenly Lord’s inquiries, and they must heed the teachings day and night without slackening. The appointed overseers must not fail in their duties, and those of sincere heart must ensure the registers are settled.

There are spirit-envoys who calculate the names of those destined to ascend. One hundred days prior, all documents must be submitted without omission. If any document is inconsistent or the accounting office fails to act, all involved shall be held accountable. The prior decree forbade transgressing the divine texts. Three years and eight months after this text’s issuance, it may be shown to the common people. If there are those of Daoist faith, it may be revealed to them.

The Heavenly Lord instructs: "This person bore prior burdens, and the decree commands the spirits to resolve and conceal them. Those not yet concealed shall be concealed." The Great Spirits say: "This person has long suffered poverty and emptiness, fearing they cannot endure. Having gained the Heavenly Lord’s trust, the spirits are ordered to conceal their fate."

Those who previously received decrees and expressed gratitude for the grace—though the appointed time has not yet arrived—shall be informed one month in advance. The Heavenly Lord declares: "Among the spirits, generals, soldiers, and armor under my command below, do not miss the appointed time for concealment. Record their names, so the earthly lords may show reverence, and spirits may come and go. If they seek to fulfill their wishes, permit it. Let future affairs turn from evil toward good, avoiding transgressions, so they may again behold the Dao’s teachings and transformations, none disobeying."

Thus, the overseers are made wings to guide the beginning and end, completing their tasks like fortified cities, clearly discernible. Knowing the great transformations above and harmonizing the primordial *qi*, they also understand human affairs. These are people of fortune and destiny, all foreknown. Following their transformations, their allotted years may be extended, and Heaven cherishes them. Benevolent spirits guard them, shielding them from harm. Their hearts incline toward goodness, and evil cannot claim them.

Thus, Heaven values goodness, allowing wishes to be fulfilled without encroachment or conflict, as it should be. Heaven further extends their years, bestowing this great favor. Repayment is not in jewels or treasures but in writing sincerity, returning to earnest faith, and not betraying one’s words—this is repayment.

When Heaven witnesses good deeds, they must be concealed, not shared, for fortune and misfortune follow. Only those who align with the great sagely and virtuous may receive the primordial *qi*’s natural radiance, moving the Great Spirits. They fully understand what is to be bestowed, always aligning with Heaven’s will, never losing the intent of the primordial *qi*. They constantly act above to assist the Great Spirits, like ministers serving a state. Their hearts know the Great Spirits’ directives, and the documents they submit are interconnected. Each memorial is fittingly presented, and the right person is chosen to safeguard their words. They act on the Heavenly Lord’s behalf, and upon receiving the texts, they transmit them without delay, receiving the grace of audience above.

The Great Sage should know: How could the Heavenly Lord’s decrees ever fail? The worldly do not understand, assuming it is like mortal officials—how could they know the celestial decrees and their proper transmission? In Heaven’s affairs, voices carry across distances—how could anything be hidden? This is naturally scrutinized, and thus the Heavenly Lord foreknows day and night, within Heaven, Earth, and the harmony between, all great and small, even the most secret matters. How could the spirits act freely?

Thus, the beginning and end of good and evil are recorded, and the spirits document them. The Heavenly Lord personally follows the monthly and stellar configurations, governing without fail, all rectified and untransgressed. Thus, it is said Heaven sends forth its decrees.

The spirit within the human abdomen sees afar and communes with Heaven, their voices heard—how could they not know the people’s good and evil? The Heavenly Lord says: "Those with good faith are elevated; those without are demoted. Not only Heaven desires the faithful—so too does the harmony of Earth below." People do not deeply understand future affairs, so those of sincere heart must persevere. Persevering, they walk the same path as the Great Spirits, drawing near to Heaven. Like loyal ministers and virtuous officials who never leave their lord’s side—yet people do not trust Heaven. How could Heaven trust those of divided heart?

Those who ascend to Heaven in broad daylight, seeking life with their names recorded, are listed in the Northern Culmen Heavenly Lord’s inner registers. How could the faithless be inscribed? Those of early and steadfast heart shall ultimately ride the refined *qi*, acting on Heaven’s behalf.

Within Heaven, Earth, and their harmony, all should follow Heaven’s grace to live—yet many disbelieve. This is the gravest sin; how can they hope the celestial spirits will take notice? If the worldly repent, toiling day and night, accumulating years, they may be pardoned and their names presented to the Heavenly Lord.

Those who reproach themselves shall have their names transferred by the spirits of life’s register to the Bureau of Longevity, where the One Hundred and Twenty Envoys grant them continued generations. The poor shall have descendants. Those Heaven destroys have persisted in evil, harming others—thus, they are cut off

Those of ancient times who attained immortality and transcended the world—how could they ever harbor evil thoughts? They beheld writings on loyalty and filial piety, revered and served their parents, lived in harmony with their siblings, and maintained no distinction between inner and outer. Above and below, all were united, aligning with Heaven’s great prohibitions. The Celestial Lord governs all, receiving mandates for fixed terms—how could one act with self-indulgence? A heart of loyalty and filial piety never strays from the will of Heaven and Earth, aiding the four seasons and the five phases, never daring to harm the living beings of their time.

Only the Most High’s benevolent ones act thus, accumulating deeds before Heaven.
