Heaven hears and trusts them, dispatching them to assist the Eastern August One in arranging all living things, bestowing blossoms and fruits to feed the people, ensuring warmth and sustenance. Their bodies grow robust, nurturing one another in turn; yin and yang unite, male and female take form, the old and young follow in succession, receiving their allotted lifespans from Heaven’s decree. The twenty-eight lunar lodges rotate in mutual completion, while the sun and moon illuminate without fail, taking turns to sustain life—how could there be any slackening?

Yet people do not know that lifespans vary in length, that spring, summer, autumn, and winter bring impermanence in life and death. Thus, the spirits oversee the shifting of destinies, increasing or decreasing the tally of years, passing them on in turn. Therefore, it is said that the four seasons, five phases, sun, moon, and stars all govern human life: the good have their years extended, the wicked have theirs diminished. The severity of transgressions is measured by fixed standards. Between Heaven above and Earth below, all is interwoven like inner and outer, with myriad spirits appointed to relay commands. Thus, when the Celestial Lord issues decrees to the bureaus, each transfers them in turn, serving as the current celestial tally—no private favor is permitted. From ancient times to the present, how could any escape?

Only the Most High’s virtuous ones act thus, for they discern the affairs Heaven and Earth are to carry out, each with its own charge, its own decree, its own cultivation, its own spirit, its own merit, its own loyalty, its own governance, its own bestowal upon others, its own path of advancement. Each gains the trust of Heaven and Earth, never straying from the generative and transformative work of the four seasons and five phases. Thus, the Most High’s virtuous ones receive Heaven’s trust, Earth’s protection, and the five phases’ confidence, never violating any prohibitions. They constantly aspire to perfect others, delighting in goodness, aligning with the will of Heaven and Earth’s divine spirits, penetrating from outer to inner, achieving success in their own bodies. They are inscribed in the register of long life and enduring vision, permitted to serve alongside Heaven and Earth’s great spirits. From loyalty and sincerity toward Heaven, they uphold the great transformation.

Thus, Heaven does not thwart human aspirations, nor does Earth deny human peace. Day and night, they reflect on karmic debts and burdens, fearing they may fail to meet the Celestial Lord’s expectations—how could they hesitate to repay with loyalty and filial piety? Only the Most High’s enlightened ones foresee Heaven’s affairs, knowing what to enact and what remains undone. Their actions arise naturally, determined by their conduct. Thus, they understand the inner and outer of good and evil, and all they do comes to fruition. Revering and emulating the divine, they perfect their merit and name their virtue. They commune with the great spirits in speech, walk the Dao, and advance their knowledge.

Only the Most High’s mindful ones each know their allotted domain, each with their own Dao, their own conduct, their own compliance, their own advancement, their own declarations, their own words, their own destinations, their own movements. Their hearts are bound within, constantly striving to fulfill loyalty and filial piety, truly serving Heaven. Accumulating deeds over the years, they never slacken or forget gratitude. They seek the Most High’s precepts to preserve their lives—how could they dare neglect the four directions? They submit to Heaven’s knowledge, their understanding extending to what is yet to come, their hearts fixed on the great spirits. In their advancement and declarations, they dare not rely on their own judgment, but constantly gather the spirits in counsel, discerning what may be adopted or not, ever fearful of failing to win the spirits’ trust.

When Heaven prospers, nations descend in radiant submission. Former masters, sages, and the Dao of Heaven and Earth’s joyous spirits emerge to aid humanity, granting long life and driving back the four barbarians. The formless divine beings of old sought the Dao of life, aligning their aspirations with the primal *qi*, never losing its intent. Their illumination pervades the four directions; their soundless voices emerge and enter above and below, all in accord with the law. The spirits and refined *qi* all come of their own accord, attending to their countenance. Fearing to lose their favor, all under their charge tremble in reverence. Their robes and sandals transform to match their hearts, bestowing kindness and spreading grace. Their fame flows above and below, reaching the eight extremities beyond the four directions, extending even to the earliest sages. Covered by their vast kindness, all respectfully uphold their commands, moving the august spirits.

Moving between Heaven and Earth, their light reaches the sun, moon, and stars, drawing brightness from before them. The twenty-eight lunar lodges proclaim in turn, examining the people’s use of the heavenly stems and earthly branches, the patterns of fortune and misfortune. Yet few people understand. Assuming themselves wise, their actions and rest bring no benefit to Heaven, inviting calamity and the severance of their lineage, leaving their ancestors without worship. When the three *qi* are not in harmony, those who admonish with goodness are favored; those who do not await their destined end beneath the earth, their misfortunes flowing to their descendants. This is Heaven’s decree—how can one escape?

Heaven has its four pillars, Earth has its four pillars; thus, the sun and moon push one another in turn. The stars have their degrees and measures, illuminating right and wrong. People have their nobility and baseness, their lifespans long or short, receiving their mandate from the six *jia*. Birth comes early or late, good and evil reside in different places, not a fraction of an ounce is lost. Yet people of the world do not know this, assuming there is no truth. Only by harmonizing with the divine spirits can one be called human. Those who win the trust of the divine spirits, who gain Heaven’s response—Heaven’s spirits elevate them. Those who gain Earth’s response—Earth’s spirits nurture them. Those who gain the response of harmony—human and ghostly spirits protect them. Those who gain a good response—goodness matches goodness; those who gain an evil response—evil follows evil. All have their roots, pervading above and below.

Those who wish for inherently good and unopposed people make them the *shi*-people. The spirits of the land desire good people. Each imposes prohibitions, communicating above with Heaven. Those who do evil and violate them bring ruin upon themselves.

Officials, great or small, derive their authority from the people’s karmic conditions. They ought to clarify their duties and not become a source of suffering for the people. Those with exceptional abilities who cherish the Dao, virtue, benevolence, and kindness align with Heaven’s principles, Earth’s will, and the intent of harmony. They contemplate how to be seen by the good spirits, each maintaining their own integrity and never deceiving the ignorant. They do not violate Heaven’s prohibitions or Earth’s punishments, comply with the four seasons, and avoid the reputation of killing. The Five Phases each have their proper domains—let each guard its own.

Those who cherish life receive Heaven’s protection; those who cherish nourishment receive Earth’s assistance; those who cherish benevolence are beloved by all. Those who do evil are Heaven’s enemies. Heaven knows their wickedness and sends malevolent spirits and vicious ghosts to enter their bodies, spreading through their limbs, head, face, abdomen, back, chest, flanks, and the Seven Governors. It ascends to the Hall of Light, manifesting in seventy-two forms—this is the gateway to death. Heaven cherishes human life; Earth cherishes human nourishment; people cherish human generosity. To do evil is to invite calamity that cannot be saved.

This is proclaimed in the Heavenly Scriptures. The words of the divine sages of antiquity never strayed from the fundamental principles; they had their own laws and standards, and people could not lightly transgress their prohibitions. Those in ancient times who attained the Dao of Great Peace simply upheld Heaven’s laws and did not violate its prohibitions—they became the peaceful subjects of the realm. Heaven possesses inexhaustible grain and boundless clothing; those who accumulate merit advance and receive their emoluments.

In the most ancient times, the divine sages foresaw future events and governed together with Heaven. They distributed authority across the four directions, above and below, and the center, each with its own jurisdiction. Above and below observed one another, and order was achieved without coercion—all was good. Fearing they might not align with Heaven’s will, Heaven sent forth its teachings, and they hastened to carry them out, each holding their records, aligning themselves without movement. Fearing inquiry, they acted with discipline, ensuring their conduct was proper. In spring, they cultivated qi; in summer, they fostered growth; in autumn, they gathered harvests so the people could offer sacrifices; in winter, they stored surplus grain to sustain continuity. Without slackening, the spirits’ bestowals brought glory to all, extending even to crawling creatures and plants—each received its due.

Thus, the wealthy were encouraged to lend and aid the poor, replacing the old with the new, enabling life and growth to be passed down to descendants. This was protected by the spirits—such was the great taboo. The officials of Heaven, Earth, the four seasons, the Five Phases, and the multitude of spirits directly oversee human destiny and emoluments. They must be revered and their kindness remembered and repaid.

Hasten to entrust this text to a virtuous ruler, so they may know Heaven’s love for humanity—and how humanity, in turn, fails to reciprocate. The *Dongji Jing*, known as the *Scripture of Great Peace*, brings fortune to those who practice it; those who do not will bring ruin upon themselves, their bodies never parting from suffering, for retribution is never unjust. Those who have long been remiss in this and have harmed others—people, regardless of status, are all born of Heaven. Love them, be cautious of them, think of them, and take care not to wrongfully harm or oppress others. Those who encroach and exploit will receive no response from Heaven, no sustenance from Earth, and malevolent spirits will follow them, cutting short their lives. The spirits of prayer and sacrifice will grow ever more enraged.

When you see goodness, advance it; when you see evil, retreat from it. What doubt can there be? Each acts according to their own strength, lest the spirits lead them astray. If one’s dwelling is unsettled, they should leave the old for the new, and the spirits will return. Only Heaven and Earth, from their very beginnings, formed their essences, upholding the natural order. All that is transformed and generated thereby attains glory. Through this system, the mechanisms of the sun, moon, and stars govern the seasons, while the Five Planets each report to their respective directions, carrying out their duties, dispersing clouds and rain.

The people’s concerns are overseen by the Ministry of Agriculture, and the primordial qi gathers and lingers. All plants, crawling creatures, those that creep and slither, and those that breathe—all contain primordial qi. Birds that fly, beasts that run, and creatures of the water are the same, enabling the people to use them for sacrifices and sustenance. Those not used by the people are left for the animals to consume. Yet today’s wicked people kill indiscriminately, even those with child in the womb, turning the living into the dead to feed their mouths. At the moment of killing, all tremble in fear. Thus, Heaven, in its sincerity, pities them and establishes prohibitions; those who violate them are punished accordingly.

Even the six livestock are cherished and not harmed without cause, yet people, who should value themselves, instead act as rebels and bandits, taking without restraint. Though they may not be immediately punished, their transgressions accumulate. Killing and destruction will not cease, leading to the annihilation of households and descent into ignominy. Even the unborn will not encounter fortune. The spirits pity them, and the overseers stand before them—when will they escape?

Thus, the weight of good and evil is recorded. The Perfected Ones share this text with the people, fearing it might be concealed, so they have adapted it to common script for clarity. Therefore, gain the trust of Heaven, gain the trust of Earth, gain the trust of harmony, and gain the trust of the Five Phases—all are the responses of Heaven’s trust. Not a fraction is lost—do you understand? This is the natural transformation of the qi entrusted to us.

The Three Terraces and Seven Stars assist in rectifying Heaven’s authority. The sun and moon illuminate right and wrong, ensuring each receives its natural retribution. Again, the commands are issued to all department heads, each to make their duties clear. Those who receive punishment have no cause for resentment—this is the meaning of it.

The records of disasters and calamities reappear every three *jiazi* cycles to restore order, but it would be better to admonish ten times so they may understand. Strive to seek knowledge and understanding—even the worthy and sagely can attain it. The sage should promote the worthy, seek life without evil, and then advance to the register of immortals and transcendents, located in the Northern Culmen, connected to Kunlun. The Perfected Ones of Kunlun’s ruins maintain constancy above and below, overseeing the registers of names, arranged in order. The high attain the high, the middling attain the middling, and the low attain the low. The first to arrive become teachers, revered as lords, honored as fathers. Thus, teachers, lords, and fathers must be enlightened; ministers must be loyal; disciples must be obedient, respecting and following their superiors.

Heaven does not forget the teacher’s kindness; Earth does not forget the teacher’s nourishment; people do not forget the teacher’s generosity. Heaven employs the Three Luminaries to illuminate harmony, Earth, and the depths below, without ceasing.

In a land devoid of virtue, yin qi obscures the sun, leaving it without light. The people live in fear, grain scarcely multiplies, and floods and droughts come without pattern, forcing them to wander toward fertile regions. Heaven takes pity on them, guiding them to dwell in places of vitality. Where there is an enlightened ruler, the state prospers; displaced people return to till abandoned fields, and all grains grow to ripeness. The people regain their sustenance, once more offering to their ancestors, and the spirits find peace.

Among them are the wise and sagacious who seek the registers and records of immortals and transcendents, where their names are inscribed. They are to become Heaven’s officers, traversing the land among the people, harmonizing wind and rain to bring stable governance. Through this text, they too shall be born into later generations. Thus, one must perform good deeds to benefit Heaven.

From this point onward, admonish your descendants: the span of extended years may yet be attained. The text reiterates this, for Heaven deeply cherishes humanity and desires that all fulfill their natural lifespans. Its exhortations are earnest and repeated, entrusted to the spirits. The good are recorded above, while the wicked have their names forgotten. Do not defy this text; let its meaning dwell in your heart.

In Heaven above, there is a pattern—a root for seeking life. This is what people desire, and thus this text is set forth. If one has transgressions, let them repent in accordance with it. The divine spirits are ever before and behind you, without ceasing.

When the qi of Great Peace arrives in full, people need only face one another in daily leisure, keeping musical instruments at hand as a constant practice. Through this, they harmonize and transform one another, benefiting the state above and bringing the qi of Heaven into balance. The world is permeated by its virtue and teaching, free from misfortune.

Is harmony or disharmony not the proof of this? Those who align with the will of Heaven and Earth cause Heaven and Earth to harmonize, and people emulate this with joy. When Heaven, Earth, and humanity are in harmonious delight, all things are free from illness, and rulers and ministers remain in constant gladness. This is the arrival of the qi of Great Peace, the joy of music made complete.

Thus, when music attains the great *jue* and upper *jue* tones, the Azure Emperor rejoices greatly, and the virtue and power of benevolence emerge. All things delight in life, the liver’s qi is free from illness, and the liver spirit emerges from the East. Evil is entirely dispelled, while goodness advances to assist transformation. Azure-clad jade maidens bring rare remedies to bestow upon people—this is the clear proof.

When the middle *jue* tone is attained, the transformation of water is balanced. When the lower *jue* is attained, it transforms the lower realms.

When the *zhi* tones of the South, great and small, are all in harmony, all things rejoice in longevity. The virtue of the South knows no displeasure; evil descends and departs, while goodness advances entirely. The red qi rejoices fully, and the Vermilion Emperor comes to wander. The heart is free from illness, and the heart spirit appears, awaiting the arrival of red-clad jade maidens who bring rare remedies to bestow upon people—this is the proof.

Thus, when the harmony of the yellow qi and *gong* tones is attained, all good *gong* tones come forth, while evil is entirely dispelled. When the harmony of the *shang* tones is attained, all good *shang* tones come forth, while evil is entirely dispelled. When the harmony of the *yu* tones is attained, all good *yu* tones come forth, while evil is entirely dispelled.

Perfected Ones, ponder this meaning deeply—it is what brings about Great Peace. The reason the five directions are not explained in full is that for the loftiest scholars, seeing one aspect allows them to grasp the whole, and comprehending one principle encompasses ten thousand. To reveal it fully might induce overwhelming joy. If lesser people were to obtain it, they might speak recklessly. Therefore, it is not fully disclosed, so that each may contemplate its meaning.

The highest scholars can take one principle to encompass ten thousand, thoroughly understanding its intent. The middling scholars may gradually come to know it, while the lowest scholars, if they obtain it, would only speak recklessly. Thus, the text presents the essentials in brief, outlining the matters to guide ordinary people, so they may ponder its meaning and thereby achieve understanding from top to bottom without error.

Therefore, the highest scholars govern music to enact non-action and transcend the world; the middling scholars govern music to harmonize the customs of the people and bring order; the lowest scholars govern music merely to entertain people and summon sustenance. These three types of people each comprehend the arrival of the qi of Great Peace and follow their own pursuits, playing lutes and zithers as they will. Take care not to prohibit this, for prohibition stifles the qi of music, making governance difficult to pacify. If it is not pacified, qi contends and disputes arise, leading to excessive punishment.

Music brings joy, while punishment brings suffering—like echo and shadow, not a fraction is lost. Music is meant to quell anger, just as anger is meant to quell joy. These two alternate: when there is joy, anger ceases; when there is anger, joy ceases. Thus, anger gives rise to punishment and is the root of conflict. Joy, however, is the gateway to virtue and power.

Therefore, one must follow joy to cultivate the root of virtue and power, never suppressing it. To suppress it is to open the gate to calamity and punishment. From this arise fortune and misfortune, safety and danger. Thus, music is yang, and punishment is yin. Yin and yang are inherently opposed: when yang wanes, yin waxes; when yin waxes, yang wanes.

Yang is the ruler, yin the minister. When the ruler is strong, the minister submits, and the people are easily governed. When the minister is strong, the ruler is disrespected and chaos ensues—this is the natural law of Heaven. Therefore, one must follow the ruler’s joy to restrain the people and ministers, curbing their frequent anger.

People of later ages were foolish and did not deeply understand this meaning, instead often severing it. Thus, yin qi flourished while yang qi declined. When yang qi flourishes, there are many thieves and criminals, and the myriad things do not grow. When harmed by excessive yin, great misfortune lies here.

When the ruler’s qi flourishes, it brings extended years and increased longevity. When the ruler is joyful, the virtues of the five directions emerge entirely; when angry, the evils of the five directions emerge entirely. Thus, great joy brings forth good responses, while lack of joy brings forth evil responses—this is the natural principle. How deeply one must be admonished!

In my text, the good are all depicted with azure heads and cinnabar eyes—why? My Dao is the truth of cinnabar and azure. Azure represents life and benevolence, while true red is the proper color of the Great Yang Heaven. My Dao is the Way of the Great Yang, the governance of benevolence, unwilling to cause harm.

May I inquire: now that the qi of the Supreme Peace and August Sovereign has fully arrived, what is the proper order of governance between Heaven and Earth? Might I hear of this?

Today, the laws of Heaven above are thus: those who find joy are met with joy, while those who suffer are met with suffering—such is the law of Heaven. Now that the qi of Supreme Peace has arrived, Heaven above follows this joy, complying and serving it, urgently abolishing weapons and halting punishments. Earth below does likewise.

Joy is yang, the constant principle of Heaven. Weapons, punishments, and legal disputes are yin, the wrath of Earth. When yin rises, it must harm the transformations of yang. Now that the qi of Supreme Peace has arrived, Heaven and the divine soldiers govern together, thus severing punishments, weapons, and contentious litigation, ensuring clarity for ten thousand generations without recklessness. All things are like the sun and moon, which cannot long remain concealed.

When the primordial qi naturally rejoices, it unites to generate Heaven and Earth. When pleased, yin and yang harmonize, and wind and rain are regulated. When wind and rain are regulated, the twelve thousand things are born together. When all things rejoice, auspicious omens emerge in response, and the manifestations of the myriad beings ascend as essence to Heaven, making the Three Luminaries shine ever more brightly. When the Three Luminaries rejoice and unite, the four seasons proceed in order: spring delights in birth, summer delights in growth, autumn delights in harvest, and winter delights in storage. When the four seasons rejoice, the Five Phases do not oppose one another, and the people flourish. When the people flourish, the Emperor’s longevity is secured; when the Emperor’s longevity is secured, all the common people rejoice. When the common people rejoice, spectral beings and demonic influences submit. When spectral influences submit, there are no deaths from heavenly calamities or premature harm, and the qi of Supreme Peace arrives. The myriad states do not wage war, and thieves, robbers, and the greedy and cunning are eradicated.

The six myriad spirits of Heaven and Earth all rejoice, and the true immortals of Heaven and Earth emerge. When the true immortals of Heaven and Earth emerge, the upright qi is fully manifest, while the perverse qi is entirely concealed. Evil people all sit in self-reflection, while good people act. The divine scriptures and records are all revealed, and false and deceptive writings vanish. There is none who does not rejoice and delight; yin and yang harmonize, hearts unite as one, and families transmit life in succession. In all matters, joy brings no evil.

When yin and yang rejoice, it is the beginning of life. All things receive their mandate and arise, all resembling humanity. When men and women rejoice, they unite in heart and generate together, and nothing fails to come to fruition. Without joy, they are unwilling to unite in harmonious union. If, in anger or displeasure, they are forced into union, misfortune will follow.

In this text of mine, I have merely outlined the great principles, showing how joy transforms what is not good—how could one exhaustively record it all? Having understood the goodness of joy, I have yet to expound the prohibitions against the lack of joy, so I shall further clarify its guiding principles.

When careless and displeased, unwilling to join forces and unite in heart to generate the primordial qi, one departs from the natural. The primordial qi, being natural, does not delight in division and strife; it cannot harmonize the body and unite in virtue to generate Heaven and Earth together. When Heaven and Earth are displeased, yin and yang contend, unable to harmonize the qi of the four seasons and Five Phases, regulate wind and rain, and abundantly generate the twelve thousand things. When the twelve thousand things are displeased and contend, many are harmed and die, and the year is greatly inauspicious.

In all matters, when displeased and contentious, the Three Luminaries lose their brightness, the Emperor is sorrowful and distressed, and the common people flee in exile. The good qi is concealed, and the evil qi prevails; the upright spirits depart, and demonic beings arise. The myriad beings and people die prematurely, without attaining their years. When the twelve thousand states contend in displeasure, punishments greatly increase, and weapons are raised. Joy is severed and abandoned, punishments surge, and the six directions are disharmonious—each day is inauspicious.

When the qi of Heaven is not regulated, it begins here, yet people do not know its cause. Instead, they blame the ruler above and reproach the Emperor. Failing to recognize the great fault, they reverse the order, blaming those below for the faults of those above, exhausting the perverse qi—how can Supreme Peace be achieved? Instead, misfortune is brought about, punishments daily increase, and joy is utterly lost. The blame lies with the teachings of the middle ages, where instructors repeatedly established methods that, on the contrary, opened the gates of weapons and closed the doors of joy, allowing evil and deceit to arise, which cannot be swiftly stopped. The great fault lies here.

Thus, when the penetrating and leveling qi of Heaven above arrives, great joy is unleashed, and punishments are abolished. Earth below does likewise. I cannot exhaustively record the goodness of unleashing joy, nor the evils of its absence.

Therefore, the Dao of yin and yang extends from Heaven above to Earth below, spreading boundlessly. The male and female kinds frolic and rejoice together, then unite in heart to generate, complete, govern, and transmit the mandate of Heaven and Earth, mastering the boundless arts. If they do not frolic together, unwilling to unite in heart as one, how could they willingly generate, complete, govern, and transmit the mandate of Heaven and Earth, mastering the inexhaustible defense?

To force unity through punishments and威, though it may endure for a time, will ultimately fail. Turning away and contending, yin and yang overcome one another, and the harm of banditry cannot be stopped. Even among the closest—father and son, mother and child, husband and wife—harm will arise, together disrupting the Dao of Heaven, and there will be no enduring world. Such are the consequences of great faults.

Joy is the constant principle of Heaven, the essence of the Great Yang. Filial piety is the constant principle of Earth, the essence of the Great Yin. Thus, joy initiates and generates, initiating harmony and completing success. Heaven constantly delights in good and delights in life, thus always uniting with Heaven and sharing its qi. Only when joy unites can things generate one another, establishing hierarchy.

Thus, joy represents Heaven and the superior, while filial piety represents Earth and the inferior. Earth, being below, submits to what is above; yin serves yang, children serve their fathers, ministers serve their lords, and the lord above serves Heaven, just as Earth serves Heaven. Heaven serves what is above it, thus sharing qi with Earth. Therefore, joy and filial piety most perfectly accord with Heaven and Earth.

The *Yi* (Changes) governs the qi of yin and yang, with the eight winds as its measures, sharing the same position as the Six Jia, embodying both yin and yang, and uniting with Heaven and Earth as one body—thus it is the divine Dao.

The application of punishments severs the profound yin and incites conflict—this is the qi of disharmony, thus it always arises in accordance with the rhythms of yin. Punishments intensify when yin prevails, yet yield in spring and summer; they flourish in autumn and winter. Thieves and bandits rise under cover of night; wickedness and deceit thrive in darkness and obscurity; ghosts, spirits, and all manner of illnesses erupt in gloom; resentments and grievances gather in perilous straits, leading to mutual slaughter. This is the great proof that joy does not follow punishment—how can one not be cautious? The foolish fear it. If you, my disciple, know to fear it, this is the sign of longevity; if you do not know to fear it, it is the gate of misfortune. I warn you: be vigilant.

Thus, in governing Heaven above, each promotes joy as the foundation of transformation, causing all people to delight in mutual transformation, to sit and reflect on their faults and failings—how could it be difficult to do good? Such is the governance of Heaven above, and so too is it on Earth below. Therefore, those who wish to swiftly bring order to chaos must first sever disputes and punishments, and promote joy as the priority—then the qi of imperial equilibrium will immediately arrive.

You ask: If the qi of Great Peace in Heaven above naturally arrives in due time, and all people spontaneously transform toward goodness, with all things naturally at peace and free from illness, then why, following the model of Heaven above, must people initiate joy to transform one another? All matters depend on prior guidance and instruction—good and evil are the precursors of transformation, the gate that opens the ignorant. Thus, when Heaven intends to act, it always first initiates the precursor, and its signs appear in the heavens, divine patterns emerge. The sages of antiquity modeled their intentions upon these signs. Therefore, the Three Sovereigns above taught transformation through the Dao, and their people were all imbued with the Dao, as were all things. The Five Emperors taught transformation primarily through virtue, and their people largely embodied refined virtue, as did all things. The Three Kings taught transformation primarily through culture, and their people were largely cultured, as did all things. The Five Hegemons taught transformation primarily through martial prowess, and their people were largely martial, prone to anger and prizing strength and bravery—this is not the origin of complete transformation.

Thus, in the villages of good people, there are many good people; in the villages of evil people, there are many evil people—this is not a matter of mutual exchange. All matters under Heaven above and below have their own models and laws, and each models itself after its teacher, so that what is transformed entirely resembles one another. Heaven delights in generating and nurturing things, and things will not generate if they are not joyful. Now, the qi of imperial equilibrium and the utmost profundity in Heaven above all emerge to govern, and the essence of yang flourishes—there is nothing that does not rejoice. Therefore, one must model this qi and greatly promote joy to accord with and assist Heaven’s love of this, so that the Dao of Heaven rejoices greatly.

Now, when emperors and kings govern with equilibrium, the people enjoy longevity, so they promote joy to serve the Dao of Heaven and cause each to sit and reflect on self-transformation—how could there be faults? Moreover, joy is Heaven, the essence of yang; when yang aligns, the essence of yin submits, just as spring and summer arise while autumn and winter submit—this is the natural pattern. True person, you must follow the words of my scripture, and punishments will naturally cease. Govern and transform in this way, and you will be no different from the divine.

Thus, when governance is difficult to bring to equilibrium, it is because transformation has been lost. Now, the Dao of Heaven naturally has cycles of decline and prosperity, fortune and misfortune—how can you reverse this and call it the origin of transformation? Heaven and Earth do not speak to people, so from time to time they generate sages and sagely teachers to transmit their affairs. When the timing of Heaven is auspicious and joyful, it generates good teachers to teach good words and good transformation. When the Dao of Heaven is about to descend into chaos, misfortune, and decline, it generates evil teachers to teach evil transformation. This is the sign that Heaven governs transformation, and that it is naturally good or evil.

Moreover, in years of joy, good things are abundant, the five grains mature to feed people, and the people are inclined toward goodness. In years of misfortune, evil things are abundant, good things are few, and evil things feed people, so the people’s countenance is evil. This is the clear proof that teachers transform people. Thus, when good teachers emerge, evil teachers submit—this is the sign of Heaven’s prosperity and decline, and that it governs Heaven.

Now, the Dao of Heaven has come full circle, so it has sent me down to expound the good affairs of the true person, to delight in transformation as the highest good, and thus to teach this as the first matter. When Heaven’s cycle is complete, all affairs are prepared, and there must be joy. You understand this intention: just as when all things and people are complete, each household has its joy. Now, Heaven’s cycle is complete—what is there not to rejoice in? How could there be misfortune?

This scripture will not change for ten thousand generations—such is the transformation of Heaven above. The five musical tones, when activated in proper sequence, align with the intentions of Heaven, Earth, and humanity, bringing about Great Peace, eliminating disasters and wickedness, and ushering in harmonious qi. When hearts and intentions unite, this is the greatest joy. When hearts and intentions diverge, this is discord and error, all leading to bitter qi.

What must joy necessarily be? Singing and dancing, the harmonious blending of many voices. What must bitterness necessarily bring? Strife and conflict, the simultaneous rise of many misfortunes. Mutual joy is what suppresses and severs punishments; mutual sorrow and suffering are what bring about rebellion. What is meant by mutual accord and shared intention? Whenever people, great or small, can unite in intention, there must be joy—how could it be otherwise? You should further refine and carefully consider this intention.

The teachers of imperial equilibrium and the utmost profundity in Heaven above add a word to weigh and resolve this intention. However, if you do not yet greatly attain the intentions of Heaven and Earth to benefit the governance of emperors and kings, you must then follow and employ the intentions of Heaven and Earth. You must not oppose the Great Year or the various spirits, nor abandon their qi when emperors and kings act. Share their joy, their intentions, their direction, their orientation, their movement, their pivot, their root, and their will.

Thus, the sages of antiquity established laws, causing emperors and kings to face the east in spring, the south in summer, the west in autumn, and the north in winter—this is to govern together with the qi of Heaven. When they align in this way, it is called following the Dao of Heaven, uniting with Heaven’s qi, and thus submitting in accord. Heaven and Earth are perpetually joyful and not wrathful, so disasters, wickedness, evil, and misfortune are all severed. Then the qi of Great Peace arrives, the qi of equilibrium in Heaven above descends to govern, and the qi of equilibrium on Earth below ascends to assist it.

Joy is expressed through raising one’s voice in song and dance. The "qi of kingship" should be stirred and made manifest through music, for it is fitting to offer reverence and compliance, to present support and assistance. The qi of decline, imprisonment, and death all abide in tranquility; they do not wish to be stirred, for such disturbance brings displeasure and joylessness, leading to strife and wrath, and thus giving rise to misfortune, wickedness, evil, and disaster. This is the inherent pattern and nature of Heaven and Earth, never failing even once.

The qi to be stirred begins with the qi of emperors and kings, followed by the qi of kingship, then the qi of ministers, then the qi of rest, and finally the qi of death and imprisonment. These qi all reside before the Celestial Dipper, advancing day by day to seek assistance and flourish, hence they are stirred. The remaining qi lie behind the Celestial Dipper, their influence waning as they turn away, and thus they are not fit to be aroused. To act contrary to this is to oppose Heaven and Earth, to fail in aligning with their will. Therefore, what Heaven favors is to be promoted, and what Heaven turns away from is to be abandoned—thus one knows the seasons of Heaven, and good or ill fortune may be discerned.

If you ask why the full activation of the Five Tones is insufficient to complete a song or dance, it is because only when the qi of emperors and kings prevails does the sound emerge first, just as when an emperor or king issues commands to the world, all people and things follow in compliance, and the world attains Great Peace. Each of the Five Tones stirs different forces: some summon Heaven, some Earth, some the sun, moon, and stars, some the four seasons and Five Phases, some mountains and rivers, and some the people and all things. Whatever is stirred by sound is set in motion, each producing its own effect. Thus, when harmony aligns with its intent, good is brought forth; when it fails to align, evil arises.

The spirits of all things first arrive in homage, and only afterward do their physical forms move. When activating music and sound, one must always strive to understand its purpose, carefully grasp its intent, and then Great Peace will arrive.

In spring, the stirring begins: the great *jiao* string vibrates, summoning Jupiter, while the Heart Star descends, stirring the Eastern Marchmount. The qi of Lesser Yang trembles, the sound of the Wood Phase resonates, the spirit Goumang is roused, the Azure Dragon stirs, the position of the Green Emperor is invoked, and the green-robed jade maidens ascend and descend in unison. All things of like kind come to pay homage, delighting in the sound. What has been described for one extends infinitely to all. By refining and examining these details, their essential meaning may be fully grasped.

Combining this with all common written texts establishes the model and standard. Thus, when performing music and grasping its highest intent, one may transcend the world; grasping its middle intent brings Great Peace and dispels misfortune; grasping its lower intent delights the people.

Those who further embody the highest intent may delight the divine spirits; those who grasp the middle intent may delight the refined spirits; those who grasp the lower intent may delight the body. When all intents are fully realized, the Supreme Thearch and kings may wander carefree, rejoicing while judgments are rendered, and the spirits become radiant and sated.

Music is the essence of Greater Yang. Punishment is the essence of Greater Yin. When Yang flourishes, Yin recedes; when Yin flourishes, Yang recedes—thus, when music flourishes, punishment vanishes. Yang moves and produces sound, while Yin is silent; therefore, punishment often harms through Yin. In ancient times, the sages who followed music aligned with the intent of Heaven and Earth: compliance brought fortune, defiance brought misfortune.

Thus, Heaven’s three qi: the upper qi is called *music*, the middle qi is called *harmony*, and the lower qi is called *punishment*. Music belongs to Yang, punishment to Yin, and harmony to the Center. The southeast, being Yang, favors life; the northwest, being Yin, favors killing. The qi of harmony follows and circulates, now hidden, now manifest, warding off harm.

Sound is the discourse of music. Whether divining near or far, one must align with the time, day, names, and characters, delineating boundaries, assessing the waxing and waning of sovereign and resting qi, and correlating them to form discourse. Listening thus ensures no error.

The Dao of Heaven is like a cycle, ever revolving and returning to its beginning. Always apply the sovereign qi in its proper time, aligning with the Dipper’s position, facing its direction, and activating its sound. When people intone it, they may also use its sound, reckoning with the Six Jia and Five Phases—these are the numbers of Heaven and Earth.

The qi of the seasons is what Heaven and Earth favor and promote. On the day of the Beginning of Spring, when the Dipper aligns with *yin*, it is called the time of the Supreme Thearch. First, the Great Horn is activated; at the midpoint of the month, it aligns with *jia*; in the second month, with *mao*; at the midpoint, with *yi*; in the third month, with *chen*. The rest follow this pattern, each adjusted for the earliness or lateness of the seasonal qi.

First, activate the sovereign sound and sovereign string, then the ministerial sound and ministerial string, each according to its number. This is called "receiving the qi of Heaven and complying with the qi of Earth." If Heaven and Earth delight in and employ it, how much more so for humans?

Humans are the most honored of all beings, the children of Heaven. Heaven delights when humans reverently employ its numbers; Earth delights when humans carefully employ its numbers. This is like a filial child obeying their parents’ teachings—how could the parents not love and favor them? Deeply ponder this intent and transmit it to later generations, so they may emulate it to dispel disasters, pacify the qi of Heaven above, and assist the Thearch and kings in governance below.

Now, when the hearts of all people are at peace and not inclined toward wickedness, the twelve thousand beings each attain their proper place—how could this not be joyous?

One asks: Among the affairs of the Six Caverns and Eight Directions, what is most auspicious, and what is most inauspicious? The most harmonious is auspicious; the most contrary is inauspicious. Evil is contrary; goodness is harmonious.

Thus, the qi of the Thearch, the ministerial qi, and the subtle qi all reside before the Celestial Dipper—this is auspicious, for it is what Heaven delights in and wishes to promote. Therefore, one should rejoice in and comply with it. The resting and waning qi are what Heaven and Earth jointly abandon; thus, they should be set aside and not celebrated. Celebrating them opposes the will of Heaven and Earth, constituting great defiance and dissonance with the seasonal qi.

The Dao of Heaven serves as the model: the sovereign and flourishing qi govern Great Peace, while the imprisoned, waning, and extinguished qi govern inauspicious years. In years of Great Peace, all things flourish, and many good omens appear—this is the great verification of Heaven and Earth. Thus, the ancient sages and worthies deeply divined and complied with these patterns, clearly understanding that like kinds and like affairs share the same qi. By divining through resonance, they obtained its image, then reformed their natures and altered their conduct, never daring to act wrongly.

The language of Heaven and Earth is revealed through these signs; by observing the images and categories obtained, one may know all. Thus, inauspicious years yield few good responses.

Therefore, those who would bring about Great Peace through music must comply with the sovereign qi. In inauspicious years, music must not be performed without cause, for the imprisoned and waning qi oppose Heaven and Earth—hence, they are inauspicious. The sovereign qi is where virtue resides; the imprisoned and waning qi are where punishment resides.

Heaven endows each being with its nature and spirit. Delighting in goodness brings good spirits; delighting in evil brings evil spirits—this is the natural disposition.

First, comply with and activate the seasonal qi of Heaven, Earth, and the Four Thearchs, then augment it threefold to delight Heaven. Thus, Heaven rejoices greatly, the Thearch’s lifespan extends, premature deaths and evil vanish, disasters are entirely dispelled, the qi of Greater Yang ceases its wrath, and the realm’s borders are secure. Those who know to first activate and comply with music align with Heaven’s intent to benefit humanity, and true spirits emerge. Even those dwelling in hidden caves delight in coming to assist governance.

Second, comply with and activate the seasonal and sovereign qi of Heaven and Earth, then augment it twofold to delight the qi of Earth. Thus, Earth rejoices greatly and ceases its wrath, granting the ruler longevity, dissolving treachery, banditry, and warfare, and fostering goodness within the realm. Below, all delight in complying with their superiors, and the worthy emerge to assist in governance, while Earth spirits comply and nurture.

Third, comply with and activate the ministerial and subtle qi, causing the qi of harmony to rejoice greatly. Thus, ruler and ministers, people and spirits, each safeguard their place; flatterers, bandits, and thieves do not arise; borders are secure; and the qi of harmony daily flourishes, while all things incline toward goodness.

Fourth, be cautious never to activate the qi of death and destruction, lest severe banditry arise, sudden deaths multiply, and the realm’s borders remain perilously unstable, bringing forth malevolent qi and ghosts in great numbers, causing severe harm.

Fifth, do not activate the imprisoned qi, lest great misfortune arise.

Sixth, do not activate the waning and resting qi, lest great misfortune arise.

The reason for tripling the music of the sovereign qi is that the sovereign qi is most honored and supreme, resembling the revered Heaven—thus, it is celebrated threefold.

All twelve thousand beings come into being, and the qi of goodness responds in full.

The reason for doubling the music of the ministerial qi is that the ministerial qi resembles Earth, and Earth dwells alongside humanity—thus, its music is doubled to honor Earth. Earth dwells with humanity, and when people see this, all rejoice; thus, the myriad things are well-ordered.

The reason for performing the music of the ministerial qi and subtle qi as one is that it resembles the balanced and harmonious person. The balanced and harmonious person is humbler than Heaven and Earth, so the music is less.

Humanity is tasked with ordering the myriad things for Heaven and Earth. When people delight in music, they rejoice and incline toward goodness, and the myriad things are well-ordered.

The music of the sovereign qi is modeled after the Three Sovereigns, like Heaven itself. The music of the kingly qi is patterned after the Five Emperors, resembling Earth’s virtue of nurturing beings while periodically applying punishment.

The subtle qi is modeled after the Three Kings, without fixed laws. The waning, imprisoned, and vanishing qi are modeled after the Five Hegemons, whose qi is chaotic.

Heaven and Earth possess martial power to punish evil and uphold goodness—this must be deeply examined.

Let the Perfected One accumulate goodness and wisdom, mastering all affairs. Now, the Supreme Qi of Great Peace from the Heavenly August Sovereign has fully arrived. The Most High desires what can be urgently attained: the Heavenly August Sovereign delights in good people, those who can harmonize wind and rain to nurture all beings.

Since the beginning of creation, those who do good have been few, and few align with Heaven’s will. Heaven has always regarded this as a source of sorrow. Now, among those on Earth, few meet Heaven’s standards for eternal harmony.

Beneath the Great Heaven, the twelve thousand states all differ according to their water and soil. The finest of good people are entrusted to Heaven, and the essence and radiance of the myriad things ascend to belong to Heaven. The middling are entrusted to humanity, to serve and harmonize with the yin-yang and the myriad things. The lowest are entrusted to Earth, to walk and labor upon it.

The Dao is what August Heaven takes as its model. It is the highest designation of goodness, crowning the supreme, enveloping the boundless, emerging without gaps, entering without crevices. It is the teacher of all matters under Heaven, the origin of a million affairs, the elder of past and present worthies and sages. When emperors and kings align with Heaven’s heart, they become the parents of the people, from whom all transformations arise.

The Dao of Heaven is Heaven itself—pure and luminous, unwilling to be defiled or dishonored. Yet today’s practice of the Dao consists entirely of four defiling acts, polluting the divine Dao of August Heaven and disrupting Earth’s principles. Such acts cannot serve as the foundation of transformation, cannot be a model for teachers, cannot be parents. Together, they destroy Heaven’s treasured vessel, and are called the great rebellious children. Thus, Heaven above knows them deeply and swiftly punishes them.

When the qi of Supreme Peace from the August Sovereign arrives, it cannot tolerate these four kinds of people:
First, the unfilial;
second, those who preserve their true nature but leave no descendants;
third, those who eat feces and drink urine;
fourth, those who act as beggars.
These four types all defile the true Dao of Heaven and are unfit for fostering transformation.

When rulers employ fools to govern, Heaven’s great limit is near. How is this known? When a ruler governs with such people, Heaven manifests many disasters and omens, and the barbarians frequently invade—this is clear proof of Heaven’s disapproval.

To align with the weightiest standards is no different from a binding contract. What people detest, Heaven detests; what people love, Heaven loves. Thus, the sages and worthies of antiquity deeply grasped this great principle and always modeled their conduct on Heaven, never daring to deviate even slightly. Therefore, they alone enjoyed Heaven’s favor and won Heaven’s heart. Without Heaven’s heart, great misfortune follows.

Heaven selects its officers to share in its work, administering the inexhaustible arts of governance. Long united in purpose and strength, they harmonize qi with a single heart—thus, they endure.

Now, Heaven values the transmission of mutual generation, so the four seasons receive Heaven’s teachings and generate one another endlessly. Thus, Heaven is called Father, Earth is called Mother, and the qi of the six jia, twelve branches, and eight trigrams serve as their principles. They generate one another in turn, taking turns to act, so the Dao of Heaven remains eternally unbroken—this is the constant aid to transformation.

Therefore, scholars must model themselves on Heaven and never sever Heaven’s lineage. Now, Heaven is pure and luminous, and the Dao is clear and unsullied. Heaven and the Dao dwell above as models for humanity. The pure and luminous delight in purity and luminosity, so the Three Luminaries ascend to Heaven, each following its kind, combining to form their shapes.

Heaven’s shape is like a bright mirror: just as a person’s eyes see clearly, it does not wish to be defiled but always desires fresh brilliance. When emperors and kings rise, they all obtain the Dao as their teacher. People cherish their glory and wisdom, using them to transform the people. What teachers value is the ability to know Heaven’s heart and will, modeling transformation upon it.

Goodness on Earth is goodness in Heaven; evil on Earth is evil in Heaven. Thus, when people do good on Earth, Heaven responds with goodness. When people do evil on Earth, Heaven responds with evil. Their qi ascends and connects.

The five qi link above and below in unison; the six extensions join above and below in thoroughfare; the twelve branches align above and below. There is no distance too far for this connection. Goodness below ascends and connects; evil below brings misfortune above. The Five Phases arise below, and the Five Stars shine above. This is what Heaven makes clear to the people of the world.

What does Heaven above delight in? What does it forbid? Only by knowing its prohibitions and heeding its warnings, pondering its will day and night and never daring to transgress, can one instruct future generations.

Now, the qi of Supreme Peace from the August Sovereign has fully arrived in abundance. The yang days grow bright first, evil qi halts and rests, and upright qi prevails. The waning dissipates, and the Dao and virtue flourish in yang.

Heaven urgently forbids setting fire to mountains and forests. Mountains are the great yang, the guiding principle of the land, its ruler. The gathering of roots and trees is its elder—this, too, is a ruler.

Fire is the eldest of the Five Phases, yang in nature. The Three Lords and Three Yangs, when they meet, reverse and weaken one another. Therefore, Heaven urgently forbids setting fire to mountains and forests where trees gather. If not burned, they flourish abundantly; when they flourish, fire reigns supreme, and fire’s supremacy delights the sun and moon, bing-ding, si, and wu. When the mother is abundant, her child receives qi and endures long—thus Heaven above halts such burning. When yin flourishes, yin’s treachery dissipates day by day; when yang wanes, yin’s treachery arises daily—this is the natural law.

One asks: when the Three Yangs converge, why is it inauspicious? The Three Yangs are Heaven’s yang, humanity’s yang, and Earth’s yang. The Three Yangs contain not a single yin; all three are lords, not a single subject; all three are male, not a single female. This is the path to annihilation, the Way without posterity. The Way without posterity cannot transmit its kind, cannot mutually engender—thus it becomes inauspicious. This is to have Heaven but no Earth, to have the sun but no moon, to have above but no below, to have exterior but no interior. In Heaven’s reckoning, this is the mark of imminent ruin.

One asks: may field grasses be burned? Heaven above does not forbid it—indeed, they ought to be burned. Why burn them alone? Grasses are the yin of wood and correspond to yi. Wood corresponds to jia, and jia is yang, of the same kind as wood—thus they correspond. Yi is yin and of the same kind as grasses—thus they correspond. Yi fears metal, and metal injures wood; when wood is injured, yang wanes, and when yang wanes, treachery arises—therefore they ought to be burned. Yi is yin, grasses are yin, Earth is yin—three yins oppose one another and together breed treachery. Thus it is said: when the year resides in the northern extreme of yin, extreme yin gives birth to yang. Fire is yang, and yin, receiving yang, compliantly gives rise to good affairs. Therefore, Heaven above instructs: burn the grasses of the lower fields to delight yin and comply with yang. Two share the office, together governing yin and yang, removing the illnesses of Heaven and Earth, so that the Emperor and kings know no sorrow, the twelve thousand things each attain their place, grasses and trees emerge in joy, and no grievances remain.

Now, the fine and virtuous qi of Supreme Peace has arrived, and Heaven constantly fears that the people may violate the seasonal ordinances and harm it. The myriad spirits above jointly record those who delight in killing and wounding, the sons who hunt and fish, those who do not follow the Dao of Heaven and do no good, who constantly delight in killing and wounding. Heaven reproves them, Earth detests them, the host of spirits condemns them, and together they record and punish them. Every three years, a minor reckoning; every five years, a major reckoning. Those with grave transgressions are sentenced, while minor offenses result in reduced years and diminished fate. Every three generations, a great reckoning; every five generations, a great annihilation.

Therefore, Heaven above has assembled the documents of the Three Ways, and the host of spirits jointly record transgressions of killing, wounding, and punishments.

Jia-zi is Heaven’s norm, the day when winter first returns. Yi-chou is Earth’s norm, when things spread their roots. Bing-yin is humanity’s norm, when at dawn people first rise and open their doors to their duties. These three are the beginnings of Heaven, Earth, and humanity, the root of all things. What is born first belongs to yang, the primordial qi of Heaven and Earth. Thus, Qian, Kan, Gen, and Zhen reside on the northeastern face, their harmony lying between Kan and Gen, where yin and yang unite and give birth in the center. Therefore, all who conceive dwell in the central abdomen, slightly below the harmony, born within yin—hence called “mother.” One must not allow the qi of punishment to reside in the center.

Now, the Dao of Heaven has completed a great cycle and begun anew, with pure yang governing Heaven and Earth above and below—thus punishments are urgently abolished. Heaven is called spirit, and yang is also called spirit. Those who now transgress our writings and delight in punishments will be punished by Heaven above. Therefore, the method of the divine sages arises from the heart alone, with nothing left unexplained. Thus, the flourishing of red is Heaven, the sun, and the heart. Heaven and the sun are ever bright, illuminating all without fail. Those who practice this Dao utterly eradicate all that is treacherous and perverse.

Yang is born within the dark and obscure. Thus, yang qi arises in the north, emerges in the east, flourishes in the south, and wanes and dissipates in the west. Such is the law of Heaven.

When the qi of Supreme Peace arrives, who is fit for the Dao? Who is unfit? The Dao and humanity are like wind and rain: those who practice it prosper, while those who do not simply desist. Those who practice well are its people; those who do not practice well are not its people. Those who practice without exertion, whose path opens easily, are its people. Those who do not open their path, who labor all day without success, are not its people. To practice is auspicious; not to practice is inauspicious.

In nurturing oneself, can one afford not to examine this carefully? The Dao is the tally of the upright.

The *Excerpts from the Scripture of Supreme Peace*, Geng Section, Volume Seven, concludes.
The *Excerpts from the Scripture of Supreme Peace*, Xin Section, Volume Eight.

One asks: to be sated without eating, to enjoy long life and enduring existence—this is the Way to enrich the state and preserve the people. If one wishes to cease eating, one must first employ the method of guiding life and thereby retain qi. After ingesting qi-nourishing medicines, hunger arises slightly on the third day, mildly on the seventh, and beyond ten days, one achieves minor success without doubt—having left death for life. After ingesting qi-nourishing medicines, for all solid and difficult-to-digest foods, one meal suffices as the measure. For formless foods, moderation and restraint are best. Beyond a hundred days, one may cease eating—this is called the inexhaustible Way, the means to assist the state in nourishing the people and aid Heaven and Earth as the masters of sustenance. Too little is auspicious; too much is inauspicious; complete abstention is also inauspicious, for it obstructs the intestines.

The method for unblocking the intestines: one meal is proper; two meals are excessive; three meals are inferior; four meals distend the intestines; five meals provoke great hunger; six meals bring grave misfortune. From this, a hundred illnesses arise, and in years of great famine, one will die.

After regulating one's diet for a thousand days, the large and small intestines become full, and one will never feel hunger. All illnesses depart, the complexion improves, and nothing is forbidden or guarded against. The ancients who attained the Dao in old age all did so by abstaining from food. Rulers, ministers, and common people may thus secure body and mind, fulfill their duties, preserve wealth if rich, and sustain life if poor. The noble person who practices this will thrive in years of plenty and avoid peril in years of famine.

Humans possess three lives, yet remain unaware: daily consumption of three meals sustains them. Skipping the morning meal severs one life; skipping the midday meal severs two; skipping the evening meal severs all three. After three days without food, nine lives are extinguished. Without stored provisions or hoarded treasures, hunger arises. From this, great deceit and wickedness begin.

By employing this Way, all affairs regulate themselves. In auspicious years, one may share prosperity; in famine years, one may preserve the people. One should always lightly bind the intestines to facilitate movement. Between Heaven and Earth, all things possess their own spirit and luminosity, ascending to Heaven as stars by which to observe safety and danger.

The nature of Heaven and Earth has its own patterns and laws—six jia stems, five phases, four seasons, and their measured cycles—by which one may divine and foresee future events, remedy decline and disorder, and prevent calamities before they arise.

**Seven Matters of Loyalty and Filial Duty:**

1. **Minister’s Duty to the Ruler’s Decline:** When a minister perceives the ruler’s decline and revives him to renewed prosperity, it is a great merit. To recognize the decline yet fail to remedy it—or worse, to speak ill and depart—is to incite misfortune, and the guilt remains unforgiven.

2. **Minister’s Duty to Avert Disaster:** If a minister knows the ruler is about to face misfortune and intervenes to prevent it, this is a great merit. To know and not act is to incite disaster, and the guilt remains unforgiven.

3. **Minister’s Duty to Correct Governance:** When a minister perceives the ruler’s governance has lost its essential purpose and disasters arise in succession, yet assists in restoring order, this is proper and marks a discerning minister. To know and not act leaves the guilt unforgiven.

4. **Minister’s Duty to Guide the Young Ruler:** If a minister knows the ruler is young and his wisdom insufficient for governance, yet aids him in attaining understanding, this is proper. To know and not assist—even to speak of his inadequacy—is disloyalty, weakening one’s superior, and the guilt remains unforgiven.

5. **Minister’s Duty to the Aging Ruler:** When a minister knows the ruler is aged and nearing the end of his years, yet seeks extraordinary methods and great sages to devise strategies and inner texts, extending the ruler’s lifespan, this is a great merit. To know and not act—even to speak of fortune or misfortune—is a grave transgression.

6. **Subordinate’s Duty to the Superior’s Peril:** If a subordinate perceives their superior in danger, whether through misgovernance or negligence, and aids in rectifying the situation, this is a great merit. To know and not act, instead evading responsibility and departing, is to be disloyal and unfilial, and the guilt extends to their descendants.

7. **Child’s Duty to Ailing Parents:** When parents fall ill, a child who, through divination and observation, exhausts all effort and spirit to save them fulfills their duty. To know and not act invites Heaven’s severe punishment.

8. **Child’s Duty to Aging Parents:** When a child knows their parents are aged and nearing the end of their years, yet seeks wise teachers and extraordinary methods to restore their vitality, this is the duty of a filial child. This is akin to consuming the food of others and returning it as sustenance—a great merit.

9. **Duty to Rescue the Afflicted:** When one knows another faces misfortune, great harm, or impending suffering, yet intervenes to restore them, offering extraordinary methods, strategies, inner texts, and good counsel to eliminate their sorrows, this is a great merit. To know and not act leaves the guilt unforgiven.

To abandon one’s parents in their hour of death, seeking pleasure while shunning hardship, is to be no different from beasts. How can such a one govern the Three Powers or succeed Heaven and Earth?

Thus, the sages emerge to teach and admonish, urging goodness and severing evil, rescuing Heaven and Earth from disaster, ensuring the Three Luminaries, Five Phases, and stars move in harmony. Is this mere empty speech?

Now, the heavens above have produced texts to transform and eliminate all disasters, bringing forth goodness. Therefore, I, having received the mandate of the Perfected, reveal these writings. The heavens above instruct me to speak boldly, without concealment or obstruction.

Now, Heaven and Earth undergo a great renewal, and disasters are about to vanish without remnant. Thus, I teach people to compile and collate ancient and modern texts of virtue, forming the *Canon of the Utmost Depth*, a definitive work of goodness that cannot be altered. Even sages and worthies cannot surpass its phrasing.

These words are the language of Heaven and Earth, yin and yang. They instruct and admonish worthy rulers, urging diligent practice to attain Great Peace. The purpose of speaking of concealment is that when a worthy ruler obtains this and treasures it in his heart, applying it to the world, nurturing the myriad things to achieve Great Peace, and ascribing merit to the Supreme Emperor, it will be as enduring as stone chambers and deep caves.

Heaven bestows good things, which must return to good places. Like pearls and jade, they are treasured by emperors and kings. Coarse and inferior things are discarded by the masses. How much more does Heaven love those who do good? How could emperors and kings not value them?

Now, the heavens above are the Heaven of the Utmost Limit; the heavens between are the Heaven of the Utmost Limit; the heavens below are the Heaven of the Utmost Limit; and the heavens extending in all directions are the Heaven of the Utmost Limit. The present method is such that the Three Ways gather qi and deliberate together, corresponding to the positions of Heaven, Earth, and Humanity.

When Great Peace arrives, Heaven rejoices, and the emperor’s lifespan extends. The Way’s numinous power protects Heaven and Earth; good qi responds without fail. Virtue and power arrive daily; deceit and falsehood retreat; treacherous ministers and corrupt officials vanish. All ministers are removed, and myriad virtues arise spontaneously. The Five Phases harmonize; the four seasons proceed in timely goodness.

In governance, one must begin with the root. The root lies in the human and spirit images between Heaven and Earth, where spirits mirror humans, each possessing their own domain. Gathering in pavilions, districts, townships, and counties, their preferences, aversions, joys, and sufferings each have their origin. All affairs are closely examined, their strengths and weaknesses, gains and losses illuminated as clearly as the sun and moon.

Thus, the great teachings convene their deliberations, where the worthy and unworthy together settle affairs in equanimity. Therefore, in every prefecture, county, township, and village under Heaven, sealed receptacles are established, and the myriad people are each to compose writings according to their abilities, speaking directly of their hardships, sufferings, benefits, harms, approvals, and disapprovals, then submit their writings into the seals. Local officials shall compile and present these to the Son of Heaven, enabling him to know the people’s preferences and aversions, the worthy and unworthy, the beneficial and harmful, so that they may be collectively deliberated and governed. Thereupon, the qi of Great Peace shall arrive, blessing the state, its lord, and the myriad people, so that the twelve thousand beings each attain their proper place.

The sealed receptacle is what is now called the *guǐhán*. The Way of Heaven has its urgencies and delays; human affairs are likewise urgent or delayed. When the Way of Heaven is urgent, wind, rain, thunder, and lightning arrive without fail at their appointed times. When human affairs are urgent, swift action likewise arrives without delay. For urgent matters, one must respond in accordance with the celestial model: the memorial is submitted in a single transmission, returned to the original office for handling, and rewards or punishments are meted out accordingly. For delayed matters, they are to be reported in a single day during the eighth month.

The celestial model is thus. Just as the principles of yin and yang operate in this manner, so too do human affairs. Within each person’s abdomen resides a Celestial Sovereign, and the Five Qi each have their ruling monarchs. Heaven possesses the Five Qi, and Earth has the Five Directions. One qi presides over movement, and the ruling monarch upholds rectitude. All affairs within the human abdomen are called the *heart*. The heart is the ruler of the Five Viscera, the root of the spirit, and the utmost essence of the body. It governs the pursuit of goodness; the heart takes no joy in falsehood, for internal wickedness is evil.

If one can uphold goodness, abide in clarity and stillness, refrain from reckless external pursuits, and maintain inner integrity, then one may meet the ruler within the abdomen—this is called "illuminating the heart to behold its clarity." The heart is the ruler; meeting it ensures longevity, and all affairs are governed rightly. Those who fail to meet the ruler are all deviant, no longer in communion with the ruler, and all their affairs go awry, leading to early demise.

Now, the virtue of the Great Yang flourishes, desiring that above and below Heaven, there be no bounds above and no limits below, extending even to the Eight Caverns beyond. The true spirits and true essences, radiant with light, all emerge to assist the Emperor in governance, bringing forth the qi of the Supreme Sovereign’s Cavernous Peace, which has never been seen before. The good enjoy long lives, and the myriad beings no longer suffer untimely deaths or self-inflicted grievances. Deviant spirits all vanish, and under Heaven, there are no longer those who suffer from oppression or illness. How could such wonders not be heard?

Excellent is your question! Heaven commands the complete eradication of deceit, falsehood, and malevolence, bringing forth true affairs. All paintings and diagrams possess their own spirits: true affairs have true spirits, deviant affairs have deviant spirits, good affairs have good spirits, and evil affairs have evil spirits. Those who accumulate deviance in their households will inevitably suffer deviant harm. Those who accumulate true texts and true Dao in their households will inevitably produce transcendents.

Thus, the manifestations of truth and falsehood each arise from their own essence. Heaven has the auspicious and the inauspicious: the auspicious has auspicious spirits, and the inauspicious has inauspicious spirits. Earth likewise has the auspicious and inauspicious: the auspicious has auspicious spirits, and the inauspicious has inauspicious spirits.

The Three Sovereigns and Five Emperors each had their kin and brothers; the Three Kings and Five Hegemons likewise had their own kin and brothers. Though distinctions may be minor, each follows its kind. When the world flourishes, they rise; when it declines, they fall. Like day and night, they follow one another in succession, continuing unceasingly from the opening of yin and yang to the present. The poor become petty men, and the wealthy become noble men, alternating in governance and mutual administration.

This is the kinship of Heaven and Earth. Though the myriad beings do not flourish, some resemble one another, yet in truth, they are not the same. Heaven has the Six Jia, the Four Seasons, the Five Phases, the firm and the yielding, the female and the male, the eldest, middle, and youngest—all forming kin and brothers. By revering and serving them without fail, one transforms the world, making them the masters of goodness: benevolence, righteousness, propriety, wisdom, culture, and martial virtue, each becoming kin and brothers in turn.

Where the Dao is kin to the Dao, all Dao converge as one, mutually verifying and generating one another. If one’s body today attains the Dao, all Daoists will come, and kindred spirits unite as one family, all harboring good intentions. Regardless of rank, none harm one another, and disasters and calamities all depart without misfortune. If the Emperor practices this, the world will flourish, and governance will be effortless, ensuring long life and transcendence. If officials and people practice this, their governance will grow ever clearer, and all Dao will emerge, shining with light.

The Dao is kin to the Dao, transmitted and practiced in succession. Thus, summoning the Dao with the Dao and seeking the Dao with the Dao makes the Dao one’s kin and brothers. When transformation reaches such a state, the world will all cherish life and detest killing. How could there be those without the Dao?

Where virtue is kin to virtue, if one today embodies great virtue and takes virtue as one’s intent, all virtuous people will yield and serve one another, and all virtuous people under Heaven will emerge. Taking this as the model, one may sit in tranquility without affairs. If the Emperor practices this, his state will prosper; if officials and people practice it, nothing will remain ungoverned. Summoning virtue with virtue, virtue will come of itself.

Where benevolence is kin to benevolence, if one today embodies benevolence, all benevolent people will come seeking one another. Summoning benevolence with benevolence, all benevolent people will come. If the Emperor practices this, the world will be entirely benevolent; if officials and people practice it, none will fail to be kindred. This is what it means for benevolence to unite as one family—kin and brothers.

Where righteousness is kin to righteousness, seeking righteousness with righteousness, if one today has attained righteousness, all righteous people will come to join them, uniting through righteousness. If the Emperor practices this, suffering and joy will be balanced; if officials and people practice it, life and injury will be balanced. Seeking righteousness with righteousness makes them kin and brothers.

Where propriety is kin to propriety, seeking propriety with propriety, if one today has attained propriety, all those who practice propriety will come. The living will not act recklessly, their abdomens empty within, their external conduct like a ring—hastening, walking, kneeling, rising—without awaiting commands.

When days grow short and clothing wears thin to rags,
if the Emperor practices this, sorrow and vexation multiply;
if officials and people practice it, their duties become tangled,
the able grow weary, the old and weak strain their sinews.

Where propriety is kin to propriety, they become kin and brothers.

Where refinement is kin to refinement—if one today has attained refinement,
all refined people will gather like floating clouds,
their inner and outer accumulations piling like mountains.
Yet if sincerity is lacking, great deceit arises.
Should the Emperor practice this to govern affairs,
some may succeed, some may fail.
If officials and people practice it, they deceive one another with false promises,
bringing harm, swift calamities, and myriad illnesses,
shortening lives day by day.
Refining one another with refinement, intimidating one another with refinement,
they take turns seizing and generating—
such are the kin of refinement.

Where martial force is kin to martial force—if one today has attained martial prowess,
all martial people will gather,
their qi blazing like the sun,
their weapons gleaming,
their strength doubled,
their eyes wide,
their rage uncontrollable.
Martial ghosts lurk in their ranks,
seeking only victory, sparing no lives.
If a noble ruler practices this, his governance grows ever more violent;
if officials and people practice it, they slaughter the world,
devoid of goodwill,
their governance a gathering of harm—
thus martial force begets martial force,
and these are the kin of martial force.

Where eloquence is kin to eloquence—if one today has attained great eloquence,
all eloquent people will come to join them,
eloquence begetting eloquence without end.
One word becomes a hundred, a hundred becomes a thousand,
a thousand becomes ten thousand,
exchanged back and forth in a storm of tongues,
devoid of truth.
If a ruler practices this, his governance becomes multifarious,
leaving officials and people nowhere to place their lives.
Seeking eloquence with eloquence—
these are kin and brothers.

Where law is kin to law—if one today has mastered law,
all legalists under heaven will gather.
No matter how great or small the affair, all is governed,
yet no one is without guilt.
From birth to old age, how many transgressions does one person commit?
None are without fault.
Through this mutual generation,
nineteen out of twenty noble rulers meet untimely deaths.
Ruling by this, the world’s great chaos cannot be halted.
Thus, in seeking kin and brothers, each follows its kind.
The root of order and disorder, the foundation of Great Peace—
examining these nine matters makes it clear.

The gods above declare:
Those who delight in practicing the Dao—
the qi of the Dao of Heaven and Earth aids them;
those who delight in practicing virtue—
the qi of virtue aids them.
Those who practice benevolence—
Heaven grants them benevolent qi;
those who practice righteousness—
Heaven grants them righteous qi;
those who practice propriety—
Heaven grants them the qi of propriety;
those who practice refinement—
Heaven grants them the qi of refinement;
those who practice eloquence—
eloquent qi aids them;
those who practice law—
legal qi aids them.
Heaven and Earth each act according to their kind in divine matters.
When Heaven aids them, spirits hasten to their side.
Ponder deeply its essential meaning,
and the qi of Great Peace can be swiftly attained.

I ask: is supreme goodness easy to achieve, or is supreme evil easy?
