When yang reaches its extreme, it becomes goodness;
when yin reaches its extreme, it becomes evil.
Yang’s extreme gives rise to immortals;
yin’s extreme slays all things—
these are the extremes of yin and yang.

Now, the common people cannot exhaust their strength in nourishing their parents,
seeking rare methods and Daoist arts to sustain them,
yet leave them grieving until death.
Instead, they teach one another fine clothing, food, song, and dance to amuse them—
these are the people most rebellious,
and how could Heaven bless them?

Above, Heaven mirrors the writings of mortals below.
Today, Heaven establishes a law:
the people of Heaven must not conspire in cunning,
for there are greater arts.
The same holds true on Earth.
Do you, Perfected One, truly understand?

From ancient times to now,
many have been the flattering ministers and cunning men,
who manipulate words to deceive their superiors,
distressing their lord and father to gain office,
eating their stipends without merit before Heaven and Earth.
Heaven detests them, Earth loathes them,
and above, they are named "disruptors of order."
Now, the balanced qi of Heaven descends,
wishing to sever them,
yet fearing these men will again disrupt governance.

Today, people accumulate folly,
easily deceived into office,
but the disasters of Heaven cannot be deceived and dismissed,
nor can they be removed by fraud.
Truth and falsehood correspond with Heaven.
If not fully revealed to the people of later ages,
test it in practice—
all calamities will vanish,
proving this is my true scripture,
aligned with the laws of Heaven above.
There can be no doubt.

If one speaks yet contradicts,
the truth becomes daily clearer.
If applied yet yields no success,
my Dao is false—
this, too, would be evident without words.

Heaven’s law does not reward clever speech,
but rather the achievement of success and completion.
It is like sitting facing the sun and moon,
both radiant with light.
How can one know their heat and coolness?
From afar, how can one verify?
By their effects.
Sitting facing the sun, one knows its warmth;
sitting facing the moon, one knows its coolness.
My true scripture is the same.

Heaven’s law sets the standard:
when the eyes are open, govern yang;
when closed, govern yin.
When open, govern the visible;
when closed, govern the formless.
When open, govern the body;
when closed, govern the spirit.
Using this as verification,
yin and yang are fully ordered,
and none neglect their duties.
The same holds true on Earth—
it is the ultimate, imperial, and perfect governance.

Today, when Heaven issues scriptures,
when spirits issue talismans and strategies,
when divine scriptures are composed,
when sages create texts and classics,
when the words of the highest worthies are spoken—
all are speech.
Thus, the gods of Heaven and Earth and the highest worthies
exert themselves for humanity,
accumulating words over the years,
able to establish Heaven and Earth,
eliminate disasters.
If the Emperor follows and applies them,
he may wander carefree without trouble,
ascend to immortality and extend his years,
gain Heaven’s favor,
and his descendants will continue without end.

When the world declines, it will rise again in great prosperity. All under Heaven look to the Mandate, and none fail to attain their proper place within the six directions and eight reaches of Heaven and Earth. Yin and yang are thoroughly harmonized, all rejoice in Heaven’s health, wind and rain come in their seasons, thunder and lightning do not arise untimely. The sun and moon grow brighter, the Three Luminaries do not stray from their courses, the four seasons and Five Phases proceed in order, each finding its proper place—all this is the achievement of the divine and sagely words of goodness. How vast is their merit!

In the heavens above, all things differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. In the boundless heavens, the Three Luminaries differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. In the central heavens, all things differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The Three Luminaries in the heavens differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The clouds and qi of the heavens differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The sounds, thunder, and lightning of the heavens differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The wind and rain of the world differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The central winds, clouds, and qi of the world differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The people of the earth differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The crawling creatures of the earth differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The grasses and trees of the earth differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The mountains and hills of the earth differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The rivers, valleys, waters, and marshes of the earth differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The regions beneath the earth differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The boundless yin and yang beneath the earth differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The Five Phases differ, each possessing its own natural qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The four seasons differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The Six Jia and Ten Stems differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The Six Jia and Twelve Branches differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The eight directions differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my written words, and Great Peace shall be attained. The spirits differ, each possessing its own natural primal qi and yin-yang, yet resembling my scriptures. Let each follow its customs, inscribe and practice my words of good and evil, and Great Peace shall be attained.

If they do not follow the teachings of their original kind, great chaos will ensue. Take heed!

Heaven has commanded me to fully reveal these writings to resolve the afflictions of Heaven and Earth, yin and yang, the Emperor and the people, and the myriad things. All the sufferings of the people and the myriad things shall be dispelled. Thus, I teach you to employ the boundless method and demonstrate it, collating and examining the sacred texts of former sages and worthies along with the common words of the people. After this, the afflictions of Heaven and Earth shall be entirely eliminated. Once eliminated, the Emperor’s years shall be prolonged, and he shall govern with folded arms, free from care.

Heaven is the Great Yang. Earth is the Great Yin. Humanity dwells at the center, and the myriad things are likewise. Heaven constantly descends and bestows, its qi flowing downward. Earth constantly ascends and seeks, its qi rising to meet. The two qi intersect at the center, where humanity resides in correctness. The two qi constantly interact and function, uniting at the center to jointly generate the myriad things. All things receive these two qi to take form, combining them into nature and disposition. Without these two qi, they cannot be born or completed. Thus, the lives of the myriad things depend on these two qi, which intermingle within their forms.

Therefore, when one does good, Heaven and Earth know it; when one does evil, Heaven and Earth also know it. Thus, the ancient people of utmost goodness and virtue inwardly understood Heaven’s intent and always acted rightly in goodness.

The Heavenly Prognostication states: Those who return to joy find joy; those who return to goodness find goodness; those who return to evil find evil; those who return to delight find delight; those who return to compliance find compliance; those who return to truth find truth; those who return to the Dao find the Dao; those who return to contentment find contentment. Whatever one returns to, Heaven and Earth and the host of spirits likewise return in kind, as swiftly as echo follows sound.

Those who return to refinement find refinement returned; those who return to deceit find deceit returned; those who return to eloquence find eloquence returned; those who return to flattery find flattery returned; those who return to martial prowess find martial prowess returned; those who return to rebellion find rebellion returned; those who return to misfortune find misfortune returned; those who return to perversity find perversity returned. Whatever one returns to, Heaven and Earth and the host of spirits all return in kind.

All principles of fortune and misfortune, safety and peril, lie in what one returns to. Why is it that households of great strength, which amass private wealth in abundance, later often fall into poverty and misfortune? The divine ones say: This is because some, though possessed of much wisdom, instead deceive those who lack it; or, though strong, instead bully the weak; or, though young, instead oppress the old—all acts of rebellion, and thus Heaven does not long protect them.

Why is this? Those with wisdom ought to nurture the foolish, yet instead deceive them—this is the first rebellion. The strong ought to support the weak, yet instead bully them—this is the second rebellion. The young ought to care for the old, yet instead oppress them—this is the third rebellion. Such conduct opposes the heart of Heaven, and thus misfortune must follow.

Wealth is but the surplus of Heaven and Earth, like water that ever flows and follows, ever humble and dwelling below. Those who obtain much wealth are those who are humble and thus receive more. Therefore, the greedy—Heaven does not protect them.

Since the loss of harmony among the three laws of Heaven, Earth, and yin-yang, there has been an excess of reckoning in Heaven, with accumulated stores left unspent. Why is this? Heaven’s mandate allots one hundred and thirty to the highest, called the surplus of the yang calendar. Next, one hundred and twenty, called the remainder after deducting the cycle of years. Then, one hundred years, called the harmonious reckoning of things and cycles. All people ought to model their years upon these. Yet since the loss of the three laws, many do not complete their allotted years. Each surplus year is recorded as one reckoning in Heaven, but as people’s conduct strays from the Dao of Heaven, none can claim them. Now, those who emulate this text and act with goodness—Heaven will bestow all these reckonings upon them, some attaining transcendence, others extending their years.

Since the [lacuna] of Heaven and Earth, emperors have been consumed by worry, for the world is not at peace, and the loss of proper order is the source of their distress. Without this, there would be no cause for concern. The world’s good people, loyal ministers, and filial children all share this worry. Yet by following this text, such worries will be dispelled.

Heaven declares: When yang qi flourishes greatly, ghostly beings cannot act recklessly to cause harm. Why is this? When yang is abundant, yin must wane, and thus such beings cannot act recklessly. Who restrains them? The essence of yang restrains them. How does the essence of yang restrain them? The essence of yang is spirit, belonging to Heaven, associated with red, and governing the heart. The heart-spirit is the spirit of Heaven. Essence belongs to Earth. Ghosts are the ghosts of humans. Earth is the mother; ghosts are the children. Mother and child follow the same path and dwell together in the way of yin. When the qi of Great Peace arrives and yang qi flourishes greatly, the Dao of Heaven is strict, and the way of spirits is luminous. When luminous, Heaven enables people to employ it together. When the way of spirits is employed, it descends to dissolve the way of ghostly beings. When the way of spirits flourishes, it aligns with the noble person. The way of ghostly beings aligns with the petty person. Thus, the noble person governs with impartiality, and the spirits likewise govern with impartiality. The petty person governs with deceit and perversity, and ghostly beings likewise govern with deceit and perversity—clearly, they are of the same kind.

Now, when the yang Dao flourishes like fire, weapons will be dissolved and extinguished by fire. Thus, weapons accumulate yin qi, and fire accumulates yang qi. When yang flourishes, it dissolves weapons—this is a natural response.

Human life must accord with Heaven’s qi. Those of utmost goodness are entrusted to Heaven; those of middling goodness are entrusted to people; those of lesser goodness are entrusted to fields and acres. Thus, the highest scholar studies to transcend the world; the middling scholar ought to govern the people; the lowest scholar ought to manage the fields and wilds. The highest scholar should come with cloud qi; the middling scholar rides in a carriage; the lowest scholar walks on foot. These three types each have distinct duties and do not interfere with one another. The highest scholar transcends the world and ascends to Heaven, regulating the winds and rains of harmony. The middling scholar serves as an official, governing the people. The lowest scholar manages property. Each has their proper duty and does not interfere.

The methods of those who study the Dao in Heaven are such that one must seek the Dao with utmost sincerity. A small alignment with the lesser Dao allows one to see minor spirits and attain a lesser realization of the Dao. If the gateway does not yet align with the middle Dao, one cannot reach the great Dao. Only by attaining the great Dao can one summon the true spirits. Those who align with the lesser Dao summon lesser spirits; those who align with the middle Dao summon middling spirits; those who align with the great Dao summon great spirits. When the great spirits arrive, one attains transcendence and eternal existence. Yet even here, there are great demonic spirits and ghosts that do not wish for people to transcend the world. They confuse and delude people, causing them to falter, and then manifest as strange transformations, mingling truth and falsehood. Only by discerning the true from the perverse at this point can one transcend the world.

In Heaven, the highest scholar, from birth to death, harbors not a single evil thought and is thus beloved by all people. The people of the five directions and local officials all bestow gifts upon them. The middling scholar is beloved by their neighbors, who together bestow gifts upon them. The lowest scholar, devoid of any good intentions, receives no gifts but instead steals from their own household. This is what the people of the world [lacuna] do.

What does [lacuna] mean? The highest scholar is purely good, their heart and mind free of evil—this is the highest yang. The middling scholar’s heart and mind are half good—this is the middle yang. The lowest scholar’s heart and mind are entirely devoid of goodness—this is the lowest yang. Thus, they are called [lacuna]. [Lacuna] does not become substantial, empty within like a husk without grain, for they lack true sincerity. Those without sincerity are called [lacuna] people.

The highest scholar who receives gifts from local officials and people from all directions bestows them upon their household, signifying they do not forget their ancestral roots. The middling scholar who receives gifts from their neighbors bestows them upon their household, signifying they do not forget their parents. The lowest scholar, in contrast, steals from their own household’s wealth to give to neighboring villages—this mirrors their [lacuna], hollow within yet full without, turning their back on their origins. All such acts harm the heavens above, for to betray one’s household is to rend its harmony, and all discord stems from such a person.

When a minister engages in external alliances, their state will surely be emptied; when a household member engages in external alliances, their household will surely be emptied. The calamities of heaven all arise from this. Indeed, safety and peril originate within the human heart, while the numinous and divine are perceived from afar. Above and below, near and far, their vision penetrates a hundred million miles—how can one not be cautious?

The Way of Great Peace is concise in its teachings yet enriches the state; it is the mandate of heaven and the treasure of the self. Emerging close from the heart and mind, it circulates throughout the world. When this teaching is practiced, the state may be secured, and households may prosper. The laws of heaven and earth decree that the good govern the wicked, the upright govern the perverse, and the pure govern the turbid. One must not allow the wicked to govern the good, the perverse to govern the upright, or the turbid to govern the pure—such are the commands of rebellion. Banditry will not cease, villainy will multiply daily, and great chaos will arise from this.

When an emperor or king appoints a minister, they must carefully examine their selection, ensuring their choice aligns with the celestial heart and the constellations before daring to appoint them. The sun embodies the virtue of the ruler; the moon embodies the virtue of the minister. If the constellations do not align, great peace cannot be achieved, and villainy will arise.

Consider the heavens above and the earth below, the eight directions and the central crossroads—what are the lodgings, provisions, and resting places like? Those who practice the Dao and virtue yet harbor doubts may resolve them through this prophecy.

Today, in the heavens above, there are official lodges and postal stations to accommodate travelers, just as on earth there are official lodges and postal stations to accommodate travelers. In the eight directions and the central realm, all have them. The celestial lodges house immortals and transcendents; the earthly lodges house sages and worthies; the subterranean lodges house the yin spirits, the good gods, and the benevolent dead. The lodges in the distant eight directions, the famous mountains, and the great rivers house the spirits of heaven and earth. For those immortals who have yet to ascend to heaven, the clouds and winds provide shelter. The lodges and postal stations at the North Pole and Kunlun await the sages, worthies, and meritorious good spirits.

The Dao is the head, virtue the belly, and benevolence the feet that carry one forward. Heaven establishes lodges and postal stations for those who dwell within them. Those who seek the power of heaven must practice the Dao; those who seek the power of earth must practice virtue; those who seek the power of humanity must practice benevolence. These three are the endless path. To lose them is the root of chaos. To disregard these three is to rebel against heaven.

Thus, the sage embraces the Dao, practices virtue, and acts with benevolence. To go beyond this is to belong to the realm of the myriad things.

May I ask: How do the spirits of the four seasons assist in governance, bringing forth goodness and eliminating evil? Which invokes the great spirits, which the middling spirits, and which the lesser spirits?

To contemplate the imperial qi of the sun, the moon’s phases, and the establishment of the month is to invoke the great spirits. To contemplate the ministerial qi is to invoke the middling spirits. To contemplate the destructive qi is to invoke the lesser spirits. To contemplate the aged qi following the moon’s establishment is to invoke aged beings. To contemplate the ailing and declining qi following the moon’s establishment is to invoke malevolent ghosts. To contemplate the dead qi following the moon’s establishment is to invoke pure ghosts. To contemplate the broken qi following the moon’s establishment is to invoke destruction, slaughter, misfortune, and harm.

The generative qi belongs to heaven, to yang, to what lies ahead. The heavenly Dao uses spirit qi to give life, thus the six spirits before the Dipper are all generative. The six spirits behind the Dipper belong to earth and to yin. The heavenly Dao uses the dead qi to create ghosts and bring misfortune and calamity to beings.

If one wishes for future generations to always be reverent and trustworthy, to cherish and love themselves, so that the numinous spirits and essence qi never depart from their bodies, they will neither know old age nor death. For the numinous spirits and essence qi follow the movements of the mind and do not leave the body. When the numinous spirits remain constant, one does not fall ill or age, and one’s journey is not beset by evil. But if the numinous spirits depart, the sick will die at once, and the traveler will encounter misfortune—this is the great proof.

If one wishes to avoid illness, one must guard their essence with care. In all matters, one must not exceed what is natural, for within the natural there is no spirit. In all matters, if one does not become spirit, one does not surpass the great Dao and the nature of heaven and earth. Without great spirit within, nothing can be accomplished, and one cannot preserve oneself. Thus, the Dao of heaven and earth relies on spirit to act naturally.

Therefore, in all matters, great or small, there is spirit. The great have great spirit, the small have small spirit, and each preserves and nurtures their own spirit to endure. When spirit diminishes, one ages; when spirit departs, one dies—this is the natural division. How can one forcibly contend against it?

In all matters, safety and peril lie in spirit. Thus, the body is the household, qi the carriage and horses, and spirit the magistrate who governs rise and fall, coming and going. If there is a body but no spirit, it is like having fields, a home, and city walls but no magistrate. The magistrate is the arbiter of life for the people.

Loyal ministers, filial children, and those who greatly accord with the Dao should act accordingly. If one’s body is not loyal to their superior nor filial to their parents, they betray themselves, invite punishment, and lose their foundation. Always contemplate good spirits, and they will gather and follow you. Contemplate evil spirits, and they too will gather and follow you, entering your belly and moving as your thoughts direct, causing distress and restlessness that cannot be forgotten.

May I ask: The child in the womb does not eat but absorbs qi. The natural qi within the womb is already born, breathing the qi of yin and yang. If one guards the Dao and studies diligently, they return to the natural qi. To return to the natural qi, the heart must be like that of an infant—then life is born. To follow the breathing of the qi of yin and yang is to die.

*End of the Eighth Scroll of the Abridged *Scripture of Great Peace*, Xin Section*

*The Ninth Scroll of the Abridged *Scripture of Great Peace*, Ren Section*

Ordinary people cannot restrain one another, so each must govern their own fate. Those who do evil will be punished by Heaven. Thus, petty men may be punished by mediocre men, mediocre men by superior men, and superior men by the great. Even minor transgressions against the law lead to peril and ruin.

The judgments of spirits, great and small, follow the same principle. If one cannot restrain themselves, Heaven will surely punish them. Heaven reveres the Dao, and the Dao reveres the natural. That Heaven reveres the Dao is because Heaven embodies the utmost conduct. If the Dao is abandoned and not practiced, the Way of Heaven falls into chaos and ruin, leading to peril and the loss of all laws and measures.

Thus, the natural compels the Way of Heaven and Earth to be preserved. When the Dao is practiced without ceasing, yin and yang transmit and bequeath life to one another. The Dao is the master of life; if the Dao is severed, the myriad things will not be born. If the myriad things do not arise, there will be no generations to transmit, and without transmission, all will perish—how then could Heaven and Earth endure? Heaven and Earth, yin and yang, must transmit and beget one another. If this ceases, they will perish. Thus, Heaven fears the severing of the Dao and the ensuing peril.

That the Dao reveres the natural is because the Way of Heaven cannot be accomplished without it. All things are completed only through the natural; without it, nothing can be truly achieved. Even if something is accomplished, it will be false and cannot endure.

Though Heaven and Earth are vast and distant from one another, their governance of fate allows no escape.

May I ask: When the qi of Great Peace arrives in full, and one wishes to constantly employ good intentions to dispel wickedness, what should be prioritized?

The nature of Heaven and Earth is half yang and half yin. Yang is good and governs rewards and bestowals. Yin is evil, and evil brings punishments and penalties, governing deceit and falsehood. When rewards are many and punishments few, when the cunning are many and the rewarded few, the gates of deceit open. The reason is this: when punishments are many and executions frequent, those who violate the law become wicked criminals, thus opening the gates of deceit and multiplying the cunning.

Yang governs rewards and bestowals. When its bounty is abundant, virtue and power prevail. Yang and virtue govern nurturance and life—this is the law of the natural. Thus, day is yang, the sun, the ruler, and virtue; night is yin, the moon, the minister, and deceit. The nature of Heaven and Earth is half good and half evil.

Therefore, the noble person, through supreme goodness, shuts the gates of deceit. Those who promote goodness receive goodness; those who promote evil receive evil. This is like pitting a dou against a dou—what is not a dou naturally flees; like measuring with a chi against a chi—what is not a chi naturally falls away. It is as though square and circle cannot align, compass and square cannot meet, and warp and weft cannot join.

Thus, when yang arises, it moves in accord with its kind. When fire blazes, thunder roars, and the Vermilion Bird appears within. This is why thunder comes in summer and hides in winter. All things follow their roots—only then can the Way of Heaven be understood. Without tracing their kind, how could the sage and worthy attain profound knowledge?

Since the opening of Heaven and Earth, the goodness, evil, truth, and falsehood of people can be discerned by observing their conduct and seeking its kind. Their success or failure, the good and the bad, the worthy and the unworthy—all can be seen. Why engage in futile disputes?

May I ask: From ancient times to the present, the worthy, the enlightened, the wise, the eloquent, the strong, and the brave—these six types of people all possess talents a myriad times greater than others. Could they be without good or evil?

These six possess talents a myriad times greater than ordinary people. If their talents harmonize with Heaven and Earth, preventing the rise of all evil and harmful influences, the emperor will live long without worry, free from illness, fulfilling their natural lifespan, and their benevolence will flow to all people. Such worthy, enlightened, wise, eloquent, strong, and brave individuals are of great goodness and benefit.

Yet if they cannot harmonize with Heaven and Earth, if the emperor suffers worry and short life, if they themselves fall ill, are afflicted by disasters they cannot dispel, or die prematurely like ordinary people—then these six are of no benefit. One need only examine their achievements. Those who succeed are right; those who fail are wrong.

Acting thus aligns deeply with the will of August Heaven. The emperor’s lifespan is extended, and the myriad things are all well-governed.

May I ask: Among all things, some fail to be born at their appointed time, some are not nurtured, and some do not mature—where do these great faults originate?

When things that should be born are not born, the fault lies with Heaven. When things that should be nurtured are not nurtured, the fault lies with Earth. Heaven and Earth are the dwelling of the myriad things; the worthy are their artisans. The emperor embodies Heaven and constantly desires to give life. The empress embodies Earth and constantly desires to nurture. The great ministers embody humanity and constantly desire to bring things to completion. When these three work in unison, all things, from birth to end, suffer no harm.

To emulate the Way of equilibrium, those who establish laws must do likewise.

May I ask: Does the Way of Heaven aid the weak, the strong, the few, or the many?

The divine person says: The Way of Heaven aids the weak.

Why? The weak are the function of the Dao. The few are the essence of the Dao. Thus, the North Star, though one, commands the host of stars—ruling the many with the few. The essence of the Dao is one, and the Dao follows it.

Therefore, the king is few, yet the world aids and governs itself—this is the efficacy of aiding the few. Parents, though strong, instead aid the infant—this is the efficacy of the strong aiding the weak.

The supremely good are few and weak, while the ungood are strong and many. Yet when many, they become few; when strong, they become weak. Thus, the noble person seeks weakness, not strength; seeks fewness, not multitude. Therefore, the Way of Heaven protects them.

They do not contend with others, yet others contend among themselves. They do not vie for strength, yet others aid them in becoming strong. Thus, without contention, they achieve good victory.

Distinguish the essence of the Way of Heaven from the body and virtue without separation.

May I ask: If the Dao is truly joyful and desirous of practice, what is its clear proof?

The Divine Person says: I received this text from the celestial deities, who declared, "We hear that it harmonizes with yin and yang, wind and rain, cold and heat—this is its great efficacy. Heaven delights in the practice of its Way, yet people do not clearly believe in it, so we demonstrate its efficacy by granting or withholding rain. When the Way of Great Peace is practiced, all prayers are answered. When the Way of Great Peace is not practiced, prayers go unanswered, clearly showing that the Dao of Heaven resides in Great Peace.

Thus, when the myriad things fail to be born, the fault lies in the Great Yang. When born but not nurtured, the fault lies in the Great Yin. When nurtured but not brought to completion, the fault lies in the harmony of the center. Therefore, birth is the father, nurturing the aged is the mother, and completion is the child. Birth is the Dao, nurturing is virtue, and completion is benevolence. If a single thing is not born, one aspect of the Dao is blocked and obstructed. If a single thing is not nurtured, one aspect of virtue is left uncultivated. If one aspect of virtue is not completed, one aspect of benevolence is not practiced. To know for oneself whether one possesses the Dao, virtue, and benevolence, observe the myriad things and you will know.

For the Five—Emperor, King, Lord, Father, and Teacher—who deeply wish to understand the excellence or deficiency of the Dao, virtue, and benevolence, they need only observe this. Thus, the foremost good in governance is none other than delighting in birth; the next good is delighting in nurture; and the next is delighting in bestowal. Therefore, birth resembles Heaven, nurture resembles Earth, and bestowal resembles benevolence. These three are the great principles of Heaven, Earth, and humanity. Those below this are merely reserved for times of exhaustion before being employed.

When this is so, the qi of Heaven naturally becomes peaceful, perverse qi naturally vanishes, good people naturally arrive, and evil people naturally depart—all respond without fail. The one who clarifies this is the Teacher, for the Teacher is the title of the one who knows first and should take evidence as the basis for clarification. From ancient times to the present, all texts emerge from Heaven and Earth; thus, Heaven and Earth produce them first, and the one who clarifies them is the Teacher. Therefore, every text that emerges has a Teacher, and the one who practices it is the magistrate.

In ancient times, the Emperor and King received the Mandate of Heaven, accepted the Teacher’s instruction, and diligently practiced it to eliminate disasters and calamities, thereby fulfilling Heaven’s will. This is how they attained longevity and extended their mandate. The Creator is Heaven, the clarifier is the Teacher, and the practitioner is the Emperor and King. These three matters depend on one another to be accomplished. If Heaven does not produce the text, the Teacher has no way to know it; if the Teacher does not clarify the text, the Emperor and King have no way to know how to govern.

Thus, when Heaven intends to raise up an Emperor or King, there must be an extraordinary text that emerges, and a wise Teacher is sent to instruct the Emperor, King, and magistrates, enabling them to attain longevity—this is the clear proof of Heaven’s protection of the Emperor and King.

When the people and the myriad things fail to be born, are born but not nurtured, are nurtured but do not grow, grow but do not reach completion, or do not fulfill their natural lifespan, where does the fault lie? When the people and the myriad things are not born, it is Heaven’s fault; when they are not nurtured, it is Earth’s fault; when they grow but do not reach completion, it is humanity’s fault. Does the fault lie with humanity?

When the myriad things do not receive the timely opportunity to be born, it is the ruler’s fault; when born but not nurtured, it is the minister’s fault; when they grow but do not reach completion, it is the people’s fault. Heaven and the ruler-father preside over birth—this is the leadership of the Great Yang, the origin of birth. If Heaven does not desire birth, things cannot be born; if the father does not desire to bestow, things also cannot be born; if the ruler does not desire birth, things also cannot be born. Thus, Heaven and the ruler-father preside over birth.

If the ruler-father constantly contemplates birth and does not delight in killing, all things will flourish. A single thought of killing results in the death of one thing; ten thoughts of killing result in the death of ten things; a hundred thoughts of killing result in the death of a hundred things—from this up to ten thousand thoughts, all are like this. The Earth-mother and ministers, receiving the bestowal of Yang, preside over the nurturing and growth of the myriad things. Do they constantly contemplate nurturing without fail? A single thought of failing to nurture injures one thing; ten thoughts injure ten things; a hundred thoughts injure a hundred things—from this up to ten thousand, it is likewise so.

Thus, the Emperors and Kings of high antiquity, in appointing ministers, always sought those who were compassionate and benevolent, who delighted in nurturing the myriad things and governing accordingly. In middle antiquity, they were half compassionate and benevolent, so half of the things were harmed. In later antiquity, they did not carefully select and appoint ministers, so all the myriad things were harmed. The virtue of the August Emperor and King is radiant indeed!

The Emperor acts as wisdom between Heaven and Earth, preventing them from falling into calamity and evil—thus he is called Emperor. The King is one to whom the people and the myriad things turn without harm—thus he is called King. *Wang* means "to go forth." The Lord ensures that each remains within their proper bounds, and people turn to him without harm—thus he is called Lord. *Jun* means "title." The official governs and assists the superior in managing things, ensuring that all people and things, great and small, do not lose their proper governance—only then is he worthy of being called an official. The Teacher thoroughly understands all the words under Heaven—only then is he worthy of being called a Great Teacher, that is, one who can interpret all the texts of Heaven and Earth. Thus, they are worthy of being called August Emperor, King, Lord, and Teacher.

Therefore, the August Way is the head, the Emperor’s Way is the torso, the King’s Way is the thighs, and the officials are the hands and feet. The Teacher’s Way is the plumb line, the law, and the standard, upon which the above and below depend to stand. Thus, those who govern well constantly contemplate the August Way, moderately contemplate the Emperor’s Way, and below contemplate the Lord’s and officials’ Way. They constantly recite the Great Teacher’s laws and standards, adhering to their plumb line. Only then can Heaven’s will be at peace, Earth’s intent be attained, the four seasons naturally follow their course, the Five Phases do not contend, the Three Luminaries remain bright, ghosts, spirits, and essence-qi do no harm, the Five Offices and Five Scholars each attain their proper place, bandits and thieves do not arise, and the Emperor and King govern with folded arms, all proclaiming "ten thousand years."

The Dao of Heaven is the law—without my text, it is truly difficult. Carefully ponder its meaning and practice these two matters; there are also warnings therein. The nature of Heaven and Earth is such that essence, qi, ghosts, and spirits act, governing, learning from, and teaching people. The spirit resides in the yin of the human heart, essence resides in the yin of human worthiness, and ghosts reside in the yin of the human liver. When people contemplate upright goodness, they thereby teach others to do good. They constantly reside in the yin of the viscera, urging people toward evil and teaching them to do evil, thereby also urging people toward evil.

The sages and worthies of antiquity constantly harbored yin thoughts of goodness within their bellies, thus receiving good responses. Ordinary people constantly harbor yin thoughts of evil within their bellies, thus receiving evil responses, unable to restrain themselves. The fault lies in the constant yin contemplation of good and evil; ghosts and spirits thereby incline toward good or evil. That ghosts reside here can be verified. When the qi of Great Peace prevails, wind and rain come in their seasons, the myriad things flourish and grow abundantly, and the earth is well-fertilized, becoming daily more robust and prosperous, capable of nurturing life. In inauspicious years, rain and moisture do not come in their seasons, the myriad things on earth grow sparse and few, short and stunted, unable to fertilize themselves, so the earth becomes daily poorer and thinner, with little possibility of bringing the myriad things to fruition.

The movements of Heaven and Earth still require the mutual attainment and harmony of yin and yang before Great Peace can be achieved, thereby bringing about the officials of the four seasons and five phases. The Emperor and King govern according to the monthly establishment before and after; their office is to manage the Emperor’s qi and expel the officials of evil and wickedness. The establishing qi and the kingly qi are indeed the Emperor’s qi of Heaven’s four seasons and five phases. The ministerial qi and the removing qi come before the first, serving as the officials who straighten the forelocks and point directly ahead. What they face are hidden villains, prevented from acting harmfully. The removing qi, the filling qi, and the pacifying qi are all good and virtuous officials. The five executors who reside in the forefront act in advance as the Emperor’s qi, executing and removing great evil. The five generals who establish the forefront all receive the correct qi of Heaven, all being divine officials of Heaven, serving as Heaven’s envoys. Without exception, the ten thousand things of the twelve thousand categories all don the virtue of these officials and follow their transformations.

When the kingly qi should die, when the monthly establishment should be broken—this is the most revered and majestic qi, thus it cannot be withstood. When it should die, it is called the great consuming killing qi. The period after the monthly establishment is closed, blocking and sealing away evil and villainy, fearing that the resting and hidden qi that follow may encroach upon the Emperor’s establishing qi. Thus Heaven closes what comes after, and when it opens again, it dispels the resting evil qi, teaching it to depart. What comes after becomes the accomplice of villainy, so it should be gathered in. The latter five are perilous; perilous because their position is near Heaven’s great executioner, and with one turn, destruction strikes, hence it is perilous. These latter five generals Heaven wishes to rest, aligning them with Earth’s qi, governing closure and concealment, where villainous ghosts and spirits reside together, and they must not be employed.

Someone asked: The north is the beginning of the Sovereign, the east is the beginning of the Emperor, the south is the beginning of the King, and the west is the beginning of the Hegemon. Now Heaven has the six jia and twelve branches; where should the Sovereign’s Way begin? It is thus: Heaven has three systems, each with great absence. The first is the Heavenly Sovereign, the second is the Emperor, the third is the King, and the fourth is the Hegemon. The Heavenly Sovereign begins with the first jia-zi, the Earthly Sovereign begins with yi-chou, the Human Sovereign begins with bing-yin, and the Hegemon’s Way begins with ding-mao. These are the celestial reckonings of qi and numbers. As for the earthly reckoning, the Sovereign’s Way begins with zi, the Emperor’s Way begins with chou, the King’s Way begins with yin, and the Hegemon’s Way begins with mao. These four, having initially received the subtle qi of Heaven and Earth to bring forth life, must not incur punishment. Those who incur punishment harm the Sovereign’s Way; the Way’s law must not be harmed. Thus, zi punishes mao, chou punishes xu, and yin punishes si—all emit punitive qi and do not reside together.

Someone asked: Heaven bestows ranks upon people according to degree, Earth bestows ranks upon people according to degree, and people bestow ranks upon people according to degree—may this be heard? It is said: Heaven bestows upon people through the Dao, Earth bestows upon people through nurturing virtue, and people bestow upon people through emolument and sustenance. Why? Heaven, by means of the Dao, is distinct and enduring, thus it bestows the Dao, enabling longevity and satiety through consuming wind and qi. Earth, governing the nurturing of good land, makes people prosperous, thus it bestows upon people with virtue and wealth. The ruler bestows upon people with emolument and sustenance, granting them clothing. These three matters are all good. Those who love the Dao without ceasing are thus bestowed by Heaven. Those who love virtue and the earth, knowing how to select land to dwell in, avoiding misfortune and attaining good fortune, are bestowed by Earth. Those who love learning and benefit the governance of their superiors cannot be distanced by the ruler and father, who must manage affairs with principle, thus they are bestowed by people. These are the three matters the sages and worthies of antiquity diligently studied, never daring to lose. Thus, some attained the Dao and departed, some withdrew from the world and returned to the earth, and some obtained the ruler’s emolument and sustenance.

Someone asked: As for the enjoyment of the five notes, what is it like to attain their sound, and what is it like not to attain their sound—may both be heard? Sound is not empty; it achieves true matters, brings reality through emptiness, and is the method of summoning the embodied from the formless. Music, through sound and resonance, summons matters—like a person opening their mouth to emit sound, which may be good or evil. Good brings fortune, evil brings misfortune. This scripture all emerges from the human mouth, thereby bringing responses of good and evil. The sounds of music are the language of Heaven and Earth’s yin and yang and the five phases. By listening to their sounds, one knows the sentiments of Heaven and Earth, the harmony of the four seasons and five phases’ qi—there is no end to what can be known. Thus, the superior person attains its meaning to govern with balance and measure; the middling person employs it to assist the ruler in governance and attain longevity; the worthy person employs it to attain freedom from worry. Sound, uniting one with the myriad things, the myriad things uniting without limit, all under Heaven is fully prepared.

Someone asked why *The Scripture of Great Peace* has one hundred seventy scrolls. It is said: The number one is the beginning of all numbers. Thus, when Heaven and Earth were not yet divided, accumulated qi formed a single unity. Divided into two, they became husband and wife. Heaven spread upon Earth, conceiving in the dark and obscure, named jia-zi, spreading roots in the northeast. Chou became the beginning of yin, appearing in the east. The sun rises at mao, completing birth in the southeast. Chen and si hang branches in the south, nurturing at wu, turning old toward the southwest, wei and shen, maturing in the west. The sun sets at you, completing concealment in the northwest, xu and hai.

Thus, numbers begin with one and culminate in the root of the twelve stems and the foundation of the Five Phases. Therefore, one completes ten and a hundred to achieve fullness. Hence, when Heaven generates things, spring resounds for a hundred days, desiring to bring all to completion. Thus, the celestial Dipper establishes *chen* and is broken at *xu*. *Jian* means to stand—all things fully arise in *chen*. *Po* means to decay—all things fully perish in *xu*. Therefore, numbers descend from Heaven and ascend from Earth across the eight directions, completing ten in fullness. Yin and yang establish and break, moving in cycles of seven, returning to their origin. Following the Dipper’s pointer to clarify affairs, the Dipper’s seven stars illuminate the beginning and end of yin and yang. Thus, *The Scripture of Great Peace* in one hundred seventy scrolls models the numbers of Heaven and Earth, accords with the patterns of yin and yang, and follows the Four Seasons and Five Phases as its practice, not daring to err by even a fraction. To lose this is to sever from Heaven, leaving affairs without foundation, failing to align with the intent of Heaven and Earth, and not following celestial numbers to form scripture—rendering it useless for governing the world. Without modeling the laws of Heaven and Earth, it cannot dispel harm. To know its efficacy: gather the scattered texts of the world, amass them across thirty *li*, and even if Heaven were to enact them, they could not dissolve disasters. Beneath the great Heaven, within eighty-one regions and ten thousand one hundred states, each possesses its own writings, all desiring to eliminate evil, bring forth goodness, and dispel calamities. Yet if all were collected and assembled within a hundred *li*, even if raised to Heaven, they could not eradicate disasters. Though these texts are few, if the emperor and kings could practice them, they would surely await manifest efficacy.

In highest antiquity, the first were the Divine Persons, the second the Perfected Persons, the third the Immortals, and the fourth the Dao Persons—all modeled Heaven to grasp the true intent of the Dao. Dazzling the eyes to look inward, they ordered their minds within, their hidden brightness reversing to penetrate the Great Yang, inwardly attaining the essentials of the Dao alone. Like fire making light shine within but not without, they preserved constancy without disorder. Those who now study transcendence of the world model the ancients by turning their gaze inward—this is what it means. Over time, transmission begets transmission, and it again declines, turning daily to loathe its own deeds. Transmission loses the Dao’s intent, failing to illuminate within, and daily grows more disordered. Thus, Heaven produces sages, modeling celestial patterns to order the world, for celestial patterns are self-evident. When celestial patterns are correct, Heaven is correct; when earthly patterns are correct, Earth is correct; when human patterns are correct, humans are correct. When Heaven, Earth, and humans are all correct, the myriad things are wholly correct. Humans are the foremost of the myriad things. If humans lose their proper role and suffer harm, not dying of old age, the myriad things follow suit, as do Heaven and Earth. Perverse *qi* surges greatly, and people fall ill, not exhausting their Heaven-appointed years. Only the practices of past and present each have their proper sequence, not transgressing one another.

The Most Exalted Divine Sovereign of the Highest Antiquity, who names himself the Duke of Entrusted *Qi*—also called the Great Spirit—dwells perpetually at the left side of the Celestial Lord, presiding over the governance of the texts of the Luminous Hall’s patterns, ensuring their distinctions are clear and their great duties meticulously administered. He enables the ruler to commune with the immortals, recording those yet unborn, each with their names, years, months, days, and hours. When the time for their ascension arrives, spirits are dispatched to instruct and transform their bodies, that they may ascend. Each has their name, years, months, days, and hours; when the appointed time for ascension comes, spirits are sent to instruct and transform them, that their bodies may ascend.

According to their wisdom and ability, each is assigned roles without forgetfulness, their distinctions made known, allowing them to declare their own capacities before being entrusted with duties. They submit and proclaim: "The Great Spirit, supreme above all, oversees the host of spirits, each with their own domains. These must be clearly understood, leaving no room for doubt. The registers of longevity must be meticulously examined. Those of sagely illumination and intent should be granted all that lives beneath the sun."

Again, through ledgers, tallies, and calculations, their accounts are made clear, entrusted to the Bureau of Accounts, which oversees the quantities of money and treasures. All those who must submit accounts do so in advance, and the Bureau of Accounts, in concert with the Ministry of Agriculture, presents them on the thirtieth day of long months and the twenty-ninth of short months, assembling before the Great Spirit of the Luminous Hall. No delay is permitted, as the Celestial Lord commands, and none may miss the appointed time within the first three *ke* of dawn. The Great Spirit of the Luminous Hall, receiving the reports at the fifth *ke*, acts in accordance with the Celestial Lord’s established decrees.

The Great Spirit receives the Celestial Lord’s mandate and delegates it to the Minister of Agriculture, who in turn transmits it to the subordinate prefectures and kingdoms. Each domain reports what it oversees, submitting ledgers of what is to be delivered to the Ministry of Agriculture. Should any be remiss in timely submission, the Minister of Agriculture reports to the Great Spirit of the Luminous Hall, who then informs the Celestial Lord. A decree is issued to the Minister of Agriculture, commanding the prefectures and kingdoms to hasten compliance, ensuring no delay beyond the prescribed time. The transmission of hours and *ke* is strictly ordered, with no disorder permitted; all documents must be uniform, each with its duplicate.

In Heaven, there are no disasters of flood or drought, and no records may be falsified with additions or omissions. When the Wheel of Fate turns, no delays or pretexts are tolerated, lest one be found guilty of self-serving deception. Those who become aware of such matters must report them, for Heaven is ever watchful, and transgressions are never pardoned. Let each attend diligently to their duties and clarify their affairs. The Celestial Lord foreknows all, though he does not speak aloud; one must carefully consider his inquiries and not disregard his words.

Floods and droughts are without constancy, disasters and calamities arise together, people fall ill and die in countless numbers—all due to the failure to follow the Celestial Lord’s teachings. The Celestial Lord’s decrees are issued to the Great Spirit, the ministers and officials of the two-thousand-*shi* rank, and all spirits in office, charging them to devote themselves wholly to loyalty and action, aligning their hearts with the Celestial Lord’s will. The Celestial Lord, together with the masters of transformation, rectifies those worthy of ascension. Each is made to embody divine radiance, their transformations corresponding to their rank and station, all ordered by hierarchy and office.

The Celestial Lord commands the Great Spirit to perpetually transform and perfect them. Each person measures their own capacity, their aspirations growing daily, yearning for ascension. Their transformed bodies shine with luminous splendor, visible even at midday, their pure spirits penetrating all, drifting and roaming beyond the eight directions. They observe Heaven’s works, discerning its movements, each following what is fitting. Their audiences with Heaven occur on fixed days. At the establishment of each month’s first day, the greater and lesser spirits arrange themselves in order, their ranks and precedence clearly delineated.

The morning court assemblies of the great ministers do not exceed the dawn gathering; the host of spirits each clarify their domains, conducting inspections without fixed schedule, ensuring the accuracy of their documents and holding accountable those in office. Those who have matters to report must first open the Luminous Hall before speaking. Each must demonstrate their clarity and bear their responsibilities, never lacking in merit or efficacy.

The Celestial Lord commands the Great Spirit and the assembled officials to rectify their deportment, ensuring no errors or deviations, each examining their domains according to the statutes. Should Heaven become aware of their faults, they will not be absolved. Let each be vigilant in their duties, lest they be found wanting by the spirits.

The Celestial Lord commands the Great Spirit: "Within the prefectures and kingdoms, those of sagely wisdom and intent, who constantly yearn for the arts of life and wish to walk the path of divine immortals, aligning their thoughts with Heaven—those who desire to bestow kindness upon others, contemplating generation and transformation, aiding Heaven in governing life and Earth in nurturing form, and who aspire to benevolent transformation—let their names be submitted to the Great Spirit, with their merits recorded in documents, their trustworthiness attested. Their intentions shall be reported, and the Celestial Lord will personally determine their number, each recommended spirit being held accountable. The prefectures and kingdoms must select only the most excellent."

The Celestial Lord commands the Luminous Hall: "All who serve the Celestial Lord in governing the myriad offices must cultivate impartiality of heart. Each must act within their Heaven-appointed domains, ensuring order and distinction, devoting themselves wholly to loyalty and sincerity, communicating all they know, striving to perfect their works and govern their affairs. Let their reputations be steadfast and their insights advanced; let their voices carry far, their thoughts expressed without reserve. Though the Celestial Lord foreknows their words, how can one conceal anything and fail to act with utmost loyalty?"

It is asked: "Now, wishing to further illuminate the methods of sagely worthies and benevolence, and to utterly eradicate perverse texts, how can this be made clearer?"

Heaven suffers from these false and deceptive texts, which must be abolished to embrace the clarity of Heaven’s Dao. The texts of the sages of past and present are the means by which Heaven and Earth are ordered. When the texts of the sages are luminous, the Dao of Heaven is greatly ordered. What the August Heaven finds displeasing and unjoyful gives rise to warfare, floods, droughts, and unending disasters. The rulers grieve, saying that the texts of the sages have gradually fallen into disorder and obscurity, hence the Dao of Heaven is clouded and difficult to govern. When the texts of the sages are disordered, the Dao of Heaven is likewise disordered; when the texts of the sages are abandoned and unused, the Dao of Heaven is also abandoned and unused.

---

Someone asked: "In ancient times, there were no texts, yet the Dao of Heaven was not in disorder. At that time, the celestial contract had not yet emerged. The Supreme August Ones, the divine beings, and the ancestral spirits governed the primal ancestors, originally sharing the same body as August Heaven. Over time, they drifted far from the Dao of Heaven, and chaos arose as they no longer understood Heaven’s intent. Thus, Heaven produced the contract, causing the sages to record and transmit it. Yet the sages did not remain long, so they inscribed it and left it for later generations. When the qi of Great Peace arrives, the Dao of Heaven will be properly ordered."

Someone asked: "If one wishes to govern qi and affairs to attain longevity, may this be heard?"
"Carefully consider my words: August Heaven has its constant laws. For those who rule as sovereigns, they must emulate Heaven and act accordingly, employing the three norms of Dao, virtue, and benevolence. If the sovereign delights in desirelessness and tranquility, in the morning they must constantly contemplate the Dao, at midday they must constantly contemplate virtue, and in the evening they must constantly contemplate benevolence—then there will be no affairs at all."

"May I hear why in the morning one contemplates the Dao, at midday virtue, and in the evening benevolence?"
"The Dao of Heaven may be followed but not opposed. Those who follow Heaven prosper; those who oppose it perish. Now, may I speak of its essential meaning? Heaven has four seasons and three divisions: morning governs generation, midday governs nurturance, and evening governs bestowal. Thus, the southeast generates, the southwest nurtures, and the northwest bestows. Therefore, humans emulate Heaven in their conduct: in the southeast, they plant and generate; in the southwest, they nurture and grow; from mid-autumn onward, within the summer months, they dwell, marry, and transmit their kind—this is the natural teaching of August Heaven. Thus, the people silently follow it. Those who can constantly emulate this attain Heaven’s intent. Those who cannot emulate this are called opposers of Heaven’s teachings, and thus they inflict much harm. If the harm is slight, spring things are harmed; if the strong and mature are harmed, summer things are harmed; if the elderly are harmed, autumn things are harmed; if the pregnant are harmed, winter things are harmed—this is the natural law. The sage-kings of antiquity constantly reflected on the Dao of Heaven in their actions, not daring to err even by the slightest measure."

Someone asked: "Is it possible to hear how one may attain enduring thickness with the Earth?"
"Those who constantly follow what Heaven does will long share thickness with Heaven; those who lightly oppose it will long incur Heaven’s enmity. Thus, the governance of the ancient sage-kings consisted of: first, constant generation; second, constant nurturance; and third, constant bestowal. Acting in this manner, they carefully upheld and revered the name of the Dao of Heaven, which is not disordered. Fourth is governing through punishment without order, and fifth is killing—these are the extremes. By this distinction, the first type of sovereign purely generates, the second purely nurtures, the third purely bestows, the fourth purely punishes, and the fifth purely kills. Those who generate extend years and prosper the state; those who nurture increase lifespans; those who bestow commit no transgressions; those who punish incur illness; and those who kill meet violent ruin. The sage-kings of antiquity observed Heaven’s prohibitions clearly and dared not act recklessly. On the days when the six *jia* and prosperous *qi* were in ascendancy, they did not rage nor speak of evil matters. On such days, they spoke only of good things, partook in food and drink, and made music to halt disasters and dispel inauspicious and malevolent influences. Thus, the royal *qi* always desired to manifest reverence. Therefore, the people of the ancient era who measured the world, and the governance of the sage-kings who followed this, could lie down to govern and reflect, completing their tasks without a single affair. In spring, they lay with their heads to the east; in summer, to the south; in autumn, to the west; in winter, to the north; and during the four seasons, with their heads toward the corners. When rulers, ministers, and the people all knew this method, the inauspicious *qi* of the world was entirely dispelled. The celestial model of governance required that on royal days, weapons from the armories be taken down and buried in the earth. On days of rest and cessation, they were returned, so banditry did not arise, and warfare ceased."

Someone asked: "Does Heaven alone grow angry and not respond in harmony with humans—can this be known?"
"Heaven’s principle uses *qi* as its language, manifesting in the four seasons. If the *qi* of the *jue* (wood) angle is unknown, the liver’s pulse does not move, the *jue* cluster is not harmonized, and the clear tone does not resonate—this is when Heaven is displeased and does not speak. The sage-kings of antiquity, seeing this, reflected on the principles of gain and loss to reverse it. When the royal *qi* resides in a place, it attains benevolence to assist its governance. These two *qi* together generate and complete this. When the *qi* of rest and cessation returns, inauspicious *qi* arrives to assist its governance—this makes three *qi*. The *qi* of petty people appears in this, lacking the alignment of Heaven’s position, thus resembling petty people. Heaven sees and illuminates its kind, commanding the worthy and sagely to devise strategies and reflect, seeking reclusive Daoists, virtuous ones, and benevolent ones to reverse and restore its *qi*, establishing resonance. Thus, the ruler who governs the Dao of Heaven uses the people and ministers as limbs; if the governance is not good, the Dao is thrown into disorder. When the sages of antiquity were about to govern the Dao of Heaven, they sought those of Dao, virtue, benevolence, and wisdom to govern together, thereby attaining peace. Thus, Daoists belong to Heaven, virtuous ones to Earth, and benevolent ones to the center and harmony. If the three norms are not harmonized, the three worthies govern them. When the *qi* of Great Peace arrives, all things are properly ordered."

Someone asked: "How can all the people be made entirely benevolent?"
"The Dao of Heaven generates virtue; virtue generates benevolence. Now, if the sovereign takes the Daoist as their teacher and models themselves on the Dao, the sovereign models the Dao, and their ministers attain virtue. The people model themselves on the ministers; if the ministers attain virtue, the people attain benevolence. The lower emulate the upper, and the upper emulate Heaven. As they transform and generate one another, how can the people not all attain benevolence? The sage-kings of antiquity took great Daoists as their teachers to transform those below. The superior sovereign governs like Heaven, the middling sovereign governs like Earth, and the inferior sovereign governs like humans. Those who govern like Heaven do not lose Heaven’s intent, serving the great Dao as a father. Those who govern like Earth do not lose Earth’s intent, serving Earth’s Dao as a mother. Those who govern like humans do not lose human intent, reflecting on and delighting in attaining the Dao of the center and harmony. The sages, seeing all things generated, knew the principle of revering the Dao. Seeing all things nurtured, they knew the truth of virtue."

Seeing all things fully matured, they knew the truth of benevolence.

Those who embody the true Dao possess only the mind of generation;
those who embody true virtue possess only the nurturing mind;
those who embody benevolence possess only the bestowing mind.
Without these three—Dao, virtue, and benevolence—one cannot be called a sovereign of Great Peace.

The celestial scholars above are born of Heaven, receiving the entrusted qi, generated without form.
Knowing the celestial scholars, what do they not know? What do they not illuminate? What do they not see?
They are the primordial qi itself, sharing duties and acting in unison.
The celestial scholars constantly reside in the Hall of the Boundless, managing celestial documents in harmony with Heaven.
When upper and lower do not fail in their duties, they know what beings may be generated;
then descending to the earthly realm, they enable completion, and all things receive glory.

The celestial scholars are revered by Heaven and looked up to by all spirits—like the crown prince of an emperor, who would dare show disrespect?
The Celestial Sovereign, having received the entrusted qi, is thus named "Supreme and Unsurpassed Celestial Sovereign."
Whatever he commands or teaches, who would not obey?

It is asked: When the Dao of the sovereign of Great Peace flourishes, his virtue is second only to Heaven.
Receiving the scripture and practicing it alone, his transformative influence flows throughout the world—then there can be no imbalance.
The greatest spirits are none other than Heaven and Earth; the greatest luminaries are none other than the sun and moon—yet even they are two halves forming one.
Heaven and Earth each contribute half their power, uniting in heart and desire to harmonize, only then can they generate the myriad things.
Day and night each contribute half their power to complete one day.
Spring, summer, autumn, and winter each contribute half their power to complete one year.
The moon begins to wax in the west, grows and moves eastward; by the fifteenth day it is called yang, after the fifteenth it wanes and is called yin.
Each contributes half its power to complete one month.
Man and woman each contribute half their power, uniting in shared purpose to form one household.
The Dao of Heaven and Earth is one yin and one yang, each contributing half their power to unite as one, only then can they together complete the whole.

Thus, when ruler and minister unite in heart and strength, each contributing half their power, thinking and striving in unison, only then is the principle of Great Peace achieved.

It is asked: Though the writings of people today are many, and they claim all things are complete, disasters, harms, thieves, and bandits still abound.
They are constantly beset by sorrow and suffering, and on these inauspicious days, they worry—officials and people join together to save them, yet cannot.
What is cut off sprouts anew; now I can long supplement what is lacking and ensure no further calamities arise.

Since the emergence of the Celestial Contract, among all the writings of sages and worthies, are there any that are the same? All are different.
Thus, Heaven commands the masters to emerge, to eliminate inauspicious virtue, to shelter the people and ministers, their radiance covering the four directions, their influence echoing near and far, their grace extending even to plants and trees.
This is the opening of their intent and purpose—all their scriptures are distinct.

It is asked: The essential Dao of past and present all speak of "guarding the One" as the way to long life and agelessness.
Those who know to guard the One are said to practice the Dao of the Boundless.
A person has one body, which should always unite with essence and spirit.
The form is the master of death; essence and spirit are the masters of life.
When they are constantly united, it is auspicious; when they depart, it is inauspicious.
Without essence and spirit, there is death; with essence and spirit, there is life.
When they are constantly united, they become one, enabling long existence.
The constant danger is that essence and spirit scatter and do not gather within the body, instead following human thoughts to wander.
Thus, the sages teach to guard the One, meaning to guard the unity of the body.
Focus the mind without ceasing, and essence and spirit will naturally come—nothing will fail to respond, and all illnesses will be dispelled.
This is the talisman of long life and enduring vision.

Yang guards the One; yin guards the two—hence it is called "destruction."
Thus, daytime is yang, and the human hun-soul constantly resides within;
nighttime is yin, and the hun and po souls contend in activity, giving rise to dreams and illusions, losing their form and dividing into two, leading to death.
When essence and spirit are entirely lost, yet the form alone remains—those who guard the One truly unite as one.

The essence and spirit of human life are all fully possessed; guarding them without scattering enables transcendence of the world, becoming good parents to the people, meeting the sovereign of Great Peace, and being beloved by spirits and numina.

*End of Scroll Nine of the Abridged Taiping Jing, Ren Section*
*Beginning of Scroll Ten of the Abridged Taiping Jing, Gui Section*

The first is the *Divine Dao Writings*, the second is the *Verified Records of Affairs*, and the third is the *Discourse on Discarding Floridity*—together they are called the *Dao of Great Compliance*.

*Tai* (太) means "great." "Great" refers to Heaven. Heaven covers and nurtures the myriad things, its merit being the greatest. *Ping* (平) refers to Earth. Earth is level, yet it nourishes and sustains the myriad things. *Jing* (经) means "constancy." Heaven takes the sun, moon, and five planets as its constancy; Earth takes the mountains, rivers, and waterways as its constancy. When Heaven and Earth lose their constant Dao, the myriad things all suffer calamity.

The Emperor-King models himself above on August Heaven, below on Primal Earth, and in the center on the warp and weft of the stars, mountains, and rivers, nurturing and fostering the myriad things. Thus it is called the *Dao of Great Compliance*.

Divine Persons, Perfected Persons, Sages, and Worthies each divine for themselves what is right and wrong in the law. In ancient times, Divine Persons divined right and wrong, whether they would attain or not—such matters could be observed immediately. Not only was it obscure and indistinct, but it was luminously clear. The divine Dao is most numerous; when one cultivates and accustoms the body’s spirits, rectifies the heart-mind, nothing remains hidden. Good emerges, evil is suppressed, and one knows the methods of good and ill fortune as if gazing into a mirror.

At such a time, the worthy and enlightened are naturally at peace. The moment does not return, and things do not respond twice. Thus one attains singular flourishing, harmonizing distant regions. When affairs appear, their responses manifest—take care not to resist or oppose them. Compile them as treasured vessels, and it may be called grasping the heart-mind of Heaven and Earth.

When affairs are timely, all duties are fulfilled; the divine Dao arrives, the worthy deliberate, the auspicious come, the perverse do not approach, clarity and brightness appear, the four directions rejoice, recluses and hidden scholars emerge, the heart of Heaven is attained, the arts of governance are obtained, perversity does not arise, natural penetration is achieved, Perfected Persons come to assist, the world responds with goodness, each comes with their own affairs, and confusion and disorder depart.

This response emerges from the abdomen and issues from the heart-mind—it is like the verification of thunder and lightning. Auspicious responses return from within the heart-mind, following thoughts as they come and go. In an instant, they circulate throughout the world. What the heart-mind desires moves August Heaven; yin and yang shift in response. When speech is utterly sincere, it moves Heaven—this is precisely it.

Thoughts can bring forth rectitude or give rise to perversity, all arising from the will. They can move Heaven and Earth, harmonize yin and yang, unite the myriad things, enter to transcend the body, and exit to achieve fame. Worthiness and unworthiness all arise from this. Thus the worthy master it without a single error.

When a person has faults within, why does their face turn red? The heart is the ruler of the five viscera, and the ruler is the king. The king upholds rectitude; when there is fault, it is reported to Heaven. When startled, why does the face turn green? The liver is the master of the person, and the person is sorrow. When the liver and gallbladder are agitated, anger arises, thus green appears above.

All spirits have their respective rulers, corresponding with the myriad things. Thus one must always be cautious and good, aligning with Heaven and Earth, so that calamities cannot arise again.

External learning is abundant, internal learning is scarce; external affairs daily flourish, while internal affairs daily decline. Thus people are often sick, and floridity abounds. *Fu* (浮) means "surface," and *hua* (华) means "tip." The Dao of Heaven is distant when it enters human perversity, and one cannot return on their own.

The *Divine Dao Writings* root themselves in union with yin and yang, aligning with the divine luminaries. The *Verified Records of Affairs* examine and verify differences and similarities, leaving no doubts or errors. The *Discourse on Discarding Floridity* has strayed far from the root, dwelling in the wild. Its texts are disordered and cannot be used regularly; they may only be recorded occasionally.

Those who guard the root govern as if divine. Those who guard the center are slightly disordered and troubled. Those who guard the tip are benighted. Thus the worthy guard the root and caution against the center, never daring to follow the tip.

If one can guard it without ceasing, goodness will come from all directions—do not resist or oppose it. Compile it as a treasured vessel, and it will never need replacement for ten thousand generations.

Can human effort alone achieve goodness? Can perverse and deviant barbarians be repelled? Can weapons and armor be abolished? Can staffs and ropes fall silent? Can the four directions be at peace? Can roads be open? Can the lord of men be enlightened?

The divine strategy: when a great person guards it, the four directions are moved; when a middling scholar practices it, their commands and ministers are good; when a petty person practices it, they do not harm one another. Its words are concise, its laws clear—how can the divine writings of divination not be practiced?

If one cannot uphold it, take care not to harm or restrain perversity—this is the method of self-protection against inauspiciousness. Follow the four seasons and five phases, inwardly and outwardly rectify the body, disperse perversity and repel inauspiciousness. Contemplate and guard the suspended images, act in accord with the qi of the four seasons, harmonize yin and yang, and weave the net of governance to control ghosts and spirits, preventing them from recklessly harming people.

After the Beginning of Winter until the Beginning of Spring, vigorously employ the qi of Great Yin, while subtly employing the qi of Lesser Yang. Constantly observe its intent: what illnesses are caused by human agency? Its spirit-officials wear black garments. Contemplate it in seclusion for forty-five days, up to ninety days, and it will make one’s ears and eyes keen.

At the Beginning of Spring, the flourishing virtue resides in benevolence; the qi governs Lesser Yang. The royal qi turns to the east, activating the Wood phase. Its qi is weak yet benevolent. Its spirit-officials wear green garments. Contemplate it in secluded tranquility for forty-five days, up to ninety days, and it will cause illnesses to abate. If one continues to practice this without ceasing, it will make one daily practice benevolence and love.

Before the Spring Equinox, vigorously employ the qi of Lesser Yang, while subtly employing the qi of Great Yang to assist Lesser Yang. Observe its intent without doubt, deeply contemplate its meaning, and the hundred perversities will submit.

On the day of the Beginning of Summer, the flourishing virtue is Fire. The royal qi turns to the south. The qi of Great Yang governs with centered harmony. If one employs its spirit-officials and grasps its intent, sweetness arises in the mouth. Its spirit-officials wear red garments and guard it, causing the hundred ghosts to flee a thousand miles away.
