On the day of the Summer Solstice, the flourishing virtue is the qi of Great Yang, the qi of centered harmony. Its spirit-officials contemplate it to cure the hundred illnesses.

In the sixth month of late summer, the flourishing virtue governs in harmonious union. The royal qi turns to the southwest, returning to the central palace. Its spirit-officials wear yellow garments; contemplating it causes sweetness to arise in the mouth. Each season’s late period, contemplate it for eighteen days.

On the day of the Beginning of Autumn, the flourishing virtue resides in Metal. The royal qi turns to the west, severing and completing the myriad things. Its spirit-officials wear white garments; contemplating it for forty-five days, extending to ninety days, can dispel illness. Grasping its intent strengthens the bones and grants longevity in old age.

On the day of the Autumn Equinox, the qi of Lesser Yin prevails, subtly employing the qi of Great Yin. If illness arises in opposition, follow its sequence.

On the day of the Beginning of Winter, the flourishing virtue resides in Water. The royal qi turns to the north. Its spirit-officials wear black garments. It sharpens the will and sharpens the ears; guarding it for forty-five to ninety days dispels the hundred illnesses.

These are the qi of the Five Phases and the four seasons. Internally, they can govern the body; externally, they can govern perversities. Thus, Heaven employs them to purify, and Earth employs them to pacify. Heaven employs them to generate, and Earth employs them to store. Humankind employs them to flourish. Those who accord with the seasonal qi are called loyal ministers and filial children.

This is called the Great Accordance with the Dao of Heaven and Earth, yin and yang, the four seasons, and the Five Phases. Thus, the Dao emerges for the benevolent and worthy; it does not arise for the foolish.

**Method for Flourishing the Body and Repelling Disaster:**
At ten years of age, the spirit endures for twenty years.
At twenty, the spirit endures for forty years.
At thirty, the spirit endures for sixty years.
At forty, the spirit endures for eighty years.
At fifty, the spirit endures for a hundred years.
At sixty, the spirit endures for a hundred and twenty years.
At seventy, the spirit endures for a hundred and forty years.
From eighty to a hundred and twenty, the spirit is exhausted.

In youth, the spirit grows; in old age, the spirit wanes. This refers to the spirits of the five viscera, the internal signs. One thousand two hundred and twenty good spirits serve as its envoys, advancing and retreating to oversee and attend. The ten thousand spirits are its people, all following the rise and decline of the person.

This is the constant principle of Heaven and Earth. If one treats the spirit as a city and skillfully governs it, calming the body and preserving the spirit, then illness will not afflict, and years and longevity will be long. The numinous will protect it.

Thus, Heaven and Earth establish the body with tranquility, guard it with the spirit, and flourish it with the Dao. Therefore, if one can be pure and still, embrace the spirit, and not lose clarity in thought, then inauspicious perversities cannot enter.

The true spirit resides within, causing one to be constantly joyful, content, and without desire for wealth, litigation, or competition for fame and merit. Over time, one can naturally perceive the spirit. The spirit is two feet and five inches in length, and its attire follows the Five Phases and the five viscera.

When the ruler is benevolent, the Dao flourishes; when the ruler is yielding, virtue arises. If the heart harbors even a slight perverse intent, distant regions will be thrown into chaos. The spirit-qi circulates swiftly, faster than thunder and lightning. Swiftly return to the numinous luminosity to illuminate the interior, and illness will naturally heal, and the person will naturally govern themselves.

Thus, the upper limit of human longevity is a hundred and twenty years, the middle is eighty, and the lower is sixty. Beyond this is premature death. This is because the spirit wanders outside while illness attacks within.

Contemplating the fundamental and rectifying conduct causes people to cherish one another. The ancients who sought longevity did not lose the Dao.

Heaven and Earth have constant movements; one cannot depart from the root. Therefore, those who seek peace and long existence must carefully not forget this fundamental origin of the Dao.

Thus, illustrations are drawn to instruct later generations. They depict the time when people receive life and destiny, from distant antiquity to the present, without losing the transmission of yin and yang, mutually generating and enduring for myriad generations, never ceasing.

In decline and flourishing, high and low are balanced. In flourishing, one becomes a ruler; in decline, one becomes a commoner. In flourishing, one attains the Dao; in decline, one receives punishment.

Of filial piety, nothing is greater than preserving the form, for it is the lineage of one’s ancestors, spreading one’s name to later generations. This is called the good person who carefully guides the people. Heaven and Earth love them, the Five Phases bestow merit upon them, the four seasons benefit them, the hundred kings employ them, the myriad people cherish them, ghosts and spirits protect them, and the spirits of the five viscera abide within them.

Meeting once, one gains life; now, one nearly loses it. Departing from my spirit-vessel, one returns to ashes and dust, transforming without constancy, becoming the myriad things again.

Distinguishing forms and appearances, perversities naturally dissipate. Purify the body and practice the method.

The Dao’s generation of people is fundamentally all essence-qi, and all possess spirit. The temporary appearance is called a person. Foolish people do not know how to return and preserve their spirit-qi, thus losing the Dao. Those who can return and restore their spirit-qi will complete their Heaven-appointed years, or even double them—these are all persons of high talent.

For those seeking to transcend calamity, the method is as follows: Establish a fasting chamber, secure its doors and windows, and prevent others from entering carelessly. Go daily to test yourself; if not refined, do not force it but leave and return. Proceeding thus repeatedly, gradually refining and becoming familiar, one will find peace. Once at peace, one will no longer wish to leave, nor speak, nor see food and drink, nor hear human voices.

Accumulate goodness through concentrated refinement. Close the eyes and inwardly observe the form and appearance, as if residing in a mirror or gazing at a reflection in clear water—this is called minor accomplishment. Without whips or rods, there is strictness; without weapons or staffs, there is awe. All affairs govern themselves—how can this not be numinous?

This is called the path to entering the spirit. Guarding three is not as good as guarding two; guarding two is not as good as guarding one. Deeply contemplating these words, one attains the Dao and explores its mysteries.

**Method for Communicating with the Spirit and Transcending Worldly Calamity:**
Heaven’s generation of people is complete in all affairs. Thus, they are born in ten months, beginning and ending with things. Therefore, one can transcend disaster and calamity and attain Great Peace.

The superior person studies the Dao to assist the emperor and king, accumulating merit for long endurance. The middling person studies the Dao to transcend their family; the inferior person studies the Dao merely to free their body.

The Dao emerges for the worthy and enlightened; it does not arise for the foolish. Those who can employ it will be auspicious; those who cannot employ it—would it not be better to avoid harm and injury?

The worthy and unworthy know the method for themselves.

The superior person, highly worthy, regards all matters, great and small, with reverence. The middling person reveres half of them, while the inferior person has nothing to revere.

The superior person’s reverence arises from turning inward, not from seeking others. With an open heart and penetrating insight, free from obstruction, they know the root of the primordial qi in its natural state. They honor Heaven and esteem Earth, recognizing that the sun, moon, and arrayed stars; the Five Phases and Four Seasons; the Six Jia spirits and yin-yang; and all creatures that crawl, walk, or sway—none are born in vain. Spirits, demons, and spectral beings within the Six Directions; the inner and outer workings of wind, clouds, thunder, and lightning—none act without purpose. All possess their own spirits and rulers, much as humans have their signs, and thus they are revered without reckless action.

The middling person, who reveres only half, does not grasp the arts of primordial qi in its natural state. They merely recognize the wind, rain, clouds, and living things before their eyes, yet still claim Heaven has no spirits and show no awe for the arrayed stars, the sun, or the moon—knowing only the Great Fire and the Northern Dipper. The inferior person, however, does not comprehend the vastness of lands, mountains, and rivers; they know only how to till fields, plant what they possess, and manage their household and kin. They do not understand how the Four Seasons and Five Phases govern their steps, but merely follow the seasons to plant and harvest for profit. They deny the existence of the Six Jia spirits and yin-yang, dismissing them entirely.

Through foolishness, one may study and become worthy; through worthiness, one may study without cease and become a sage; through sageliness, one may study without cease and attain the Dao; through the Dao, one may study without cease and become an immortal; through immortality, one may study without cease and become a perfected being; through perfection, one may study without cease and become a spirit. All arise from unceasing accumulation of study.

One method is called "Extending Life and Subduing the Barbarians." Though the myriad kinds differ, all may attain long life. Heaven and Earth cherish them, and their bodies remain free from fault. The reason is this: it is called the Way of Great Compliance. When the Dao is achieved, one’s entire life shares the same domain as Heaven and Earth. Those who practiced it in ancient times found the myriad spirits naturally at ease. To know its efficacy, observe how auspicious signs arrive of themselves and misfortunes subside. When emperors and kings govern by it, they need not exert force—knowing and practicing this, the barbarians submit of themselves. Practicing it without cease, one becomes a perfected person.

Thus, the teachings of the sages do not require coercion or struggle to succeed; they establish instruction based on natural disposition. The reason emperors and kings can pacify the world is that they pacify it according to the hearts of all under Heaven, thereby winning the hearts of the world.

This is the ancient scripture of the Dao.

When humans are first born, they are called spirits. They share authority with Heaven and Earth, dividing body and form, spirit and essence, qi and affairs, duties and dwellings. Thus, they occupy three realms: one qi becomes Heaven, one qi becomes Earth, and one qi becomes humanity. The remaining qi scatters to complete the myriad things. Therefore, Heaven is honored, Earth esteemed, and humanity valued.

Thus, the Three Sovereigns and Five Emperors all established teachers, and those with doubts knelt to inquire. Therefore, the state remained orderly, and even disasters could be healed.

The method for rulers to be free from worry: the path of Great Compliance enables rulers to be without care or trouble, bringing about Great Peace. When Heaven and Earth do not shake violently, when wind and rain do not rage, when the hundred spirits rest in their abodes, the world is free from disaster. When the myriad things each dwell in their proper place, they rejoice without sorrow. How is this achieved? Through benevolence, the emperor and king remain joyful; through the Dao, they are free from suffering. If the emperor and king suffer, the world cannot be at peace.

The emperor and king are the heart of the world; the ministers are its limbs; the common people are its hands and feet. When the heart is troubled, the limbs act recklessly, the hands and feet move without rest, and the people drift and scatter. This is their natural interaction, and Heaven acts likewise. When Heaven loses the Dao, clouds and qi become chaotic; when Earth loses the Dao, it cannot contain things. The ruler communicates with Heaven. When a child delights in their father, when a minister delights in their lord, when Earth delights in Heaven, and when Heaven delights in the Dao, then the qi of Great Peace may be attained.

When Heaven’s qi is once governed, the Supreme August Emperor descends in peace. When Heaven and Earth harmonize, the emperor and king practice my Dao—what fault could there be? The Dao is the heart of Heaven, the head of Heaven. Once the heart and head act, how can the limbs not follow? Thus, deviant spirits naturally dissipate.

Distinguish the strengths of the three qi and return the spirit to guard the body. The qi of Great Yang is Heaven, hence called *shen*. The form is governed by Great Yin, which envelops and nurtures the myriad things, so the spirit and essence are stored in the abdomen—thus, the Earth spirit is called *qi*. Essence is the harmonious essence within the myriad things, advancing and retreating without constancy. The essence of Heaven and Earth’s yin and yang together generate the myriad things—this is the reckoning of the Three Systems. Spirit governs life, essence governs nurturing, and form governs completion. These three together constitute the vessel of spirit, modeled after ruler, minister, and people—thus, none can be without the others.

When the heart’s spirit stirs, it unsettles the form. If one preserves it without ceasing, it remains where it finds peace; if one does not employ what brings peace, it departs. Begin by teaching what brings peace, and over time, it will naturally settle and not leave.

Yin qi and yang qi alternately grind and sharpen each other, thereby generating one another. Human qi likewise circulates through the body, and spirit and essence ride it in their comings and goings. Spirit and essence depend on qi as fish depend on water. When qi is cut off, spirit and essence scatter; when water is cut off, the fish perish. Thus, the Way of nurturing life lies in calming the body and cultivating qi, avoiding frequent anger and joy.

The enlightened teachers of old taught emperors and kings to calm their bodies, freeing them from worry, so that the rulers could focus inwardly. When Heaven delights, the qi of Great Peace emerges, and nothing fails to be born and completed. When Heaven is angered, the qi of punishment emerges, and nothing escapes harm—all suffer its poison, hence the shared sorrow.

When Heaven does not guard its spirit, the Three Luminaries dim. When Earth does not guard its spirit, mountains and rivers collapse. When humans do not guard their spirit, the body dies. When the myriad things do not guard their spirits, they are damaged. Therefore, one must return to it—this is called strength. Failing to return and guard it is called dissipation.

The harmony of yin and yang: from Heaven comes Earth, from the sun comes the moon, from yin comes yang, from spring comes autumn, from summer comes winter, from day comes night, from left comes right, from outer comes inner, from white comes black, from brightness comes darkness, from hardness comes softness, from male comes female, from front comes back, from above comes below, from ruler comes minister, from *jia* comes *yi*, from *zi* comes *chou*, from five comes six, from wood comes grass, from female comes male, from rooster comes hen, from mountain comes hill—these are the root and handle of the Dao.

The pivot and mechanism of yin and yang are the profound intent of the numinous. They constitute the method for human longevity, governance, and great peace. The three qi unite as one—this is the root of spirit. One is essence, one is spirit, and one is qi; these three share a single position, fundamentally the qi of Heaven, Earth, and humanity. Spirit is received from Heaven, essence from Earth, and qi from harmony between them, together forming the singular Dao. Thus, spirit rides qi to move, essence resides within it, and the three assist one another in governance. Therefore, those who desire longevity must cherish qi, revere spirit, and value essence. Those who wish to rectify great matters should do so through non-action. For non-action begets non-action—this is the eternal law of Heaven and Earth, the art of spontaneity. Like echo follows sound, shadow follows form: the superior person employs it to pacify the state, the middling person to prolong life, and the inferior person to govern the household. This may be called "achieving without acting" and "ordering without governing." The great Dao is smooth and broad, not far from the self; by inwardly cherishing one’s body, governance naturally reverts to its source.

The method for resolving the seven affairs and dispelling delusion:
To govern the body with virtue—how much more so to govern the myriad people? To attain the qi of great harmony—how can one be good yet fail to reach it, how can one be at peace? To govern the body with benevolence and righteousness—how much more so to govern the myriad people? How can one be good yet fail to reach it, how can one be at peace? To govern the body with ritual—how much more so to govern the myriad people? How can one be good yet fail to reach it, how can one be at peace? To govern the body with culture—how much more so to govern the myriad people? To be good yet restrain them, preventing wrongdoing—how can one be good yet fail to reach it, how can one be at peace? To govern the body—how much more so to govern the myriad people? How can one be good yet fail to reach it, how can one be at peace? To govern the body by abolishing weapons and warfare—how much more so to govern the myriad people? How can one be good yet fail to reach it, how can one be at peace?

Yet these seven affairs cannot be entirely absent, nor can they be purely practiced. The divine persons of antiquity governed their bodies with fundamentals, and only then did they possess great arts for governing the people. They enabled the myriad things to live, each attaining its proper place, making the six directions and eight quarters—near and far—rejoice, ensuring nothing lost its place. Only then could spontaneity prevail, pacifying the eight directions and four reaches, bestowing grace without losing even a hair. If one cannot nurture the root and branches today, how can governance be achieved?

Now, this highest virtue—benevolence, righteousness, ritual, culture, law, and martial arts—these seven affairs differ, and though governance may be good, it may not reach fulfillment. Each has its strengths, yet none can be abandoned, nor can any be purely practiced. To govern the body, pacify the state, and bring about great peace, one must deeply grasp their secrets; to master them is the Dao. Unite them in guarding the One, and though divided, they are without limit. The Supreme Lord enacts this—profound beyond measure, named the model of penetrating illumination.

The method for teaching the four seas to discern superiority and inferiority:
Heaven generates humanity in three ranks: the first is Heaven-born, the second Earth-born, and the third of human kind. Those who receive their mandate from Heaven become rulers; those who receive it from Earth become ministers; those who receive it from humanity become the people. The ruler acts in accordance with Heaven, the minister in accordance with Earth, following and serving their superiors. The people belong to the ministers, serving in turn. Only when these three qi govern as one can success be achieved. Thus, when the superior is at peace, his ministers are good. When ministers fulfill their duties, the people follow the constant way. When both people and ministers are good, the ruler is enlightened, and governance endures.

Great peace is achieved through the Dao in practice. When the three qi are all good and unite in accord, embracing virtue and power without harming one another, the great person governs the Dao to pacify the world, rescuing the four frontiers, extending grace to the barbarians, preventing calamity from arising. Goodness daily manifests, and misfortune cannot come. The middling person studies the Dao to become a state minister, aiding in governance, measuring his household, and averting disaster. The lesser practitioner of the Dao harms his parents, wanders far away, his virtue slight and power meager, merely preserving his body—how can he assist an enlightened king or aid the state? Those who can pacify the four seas receive Heaven’s aid. Ministers assist in governance, consulting with Earth. Those who seek only self-preservation find the Dao narrow and small, unable to achieve governance. These three types of people all transcend the world and attain longevity, though their greatness differs.

This is the method of spirit’s departure and abiding, the efficacy of the Dao:
The divine person says: "Illuminating conduct and the efficacy of the Dao—whose mandate do they reflect?" They make people clearly awaken, knowing the source of their mandate and discerning who upholds its rectitude. Humanity follows the pattern of yin and yang in life: yang is always upright, yin always deviant; yang always exists, yin always vanishes; yang always grows, yin always diminishes; yang always generates, yin always destroys. People transform thrice daily, reflecting the three qi. Their governance differs, their distinctions contend, discordant and unaligned. Yet through habituation, one maintains constancy, and preserving the human form brings fortune. Only those with the true Dao can focus their essence and stand apart. The unlearned do not know the efficacy of spirit’s departure and abiding; what is manifest cannot be concealed.

Thus, the noble person controls the corpse but not the ghost. When one is not asleep—walking, sitting, speaking—the distinction between right and wrong is clear, conduct upright, words and deeds serving as standards. This is when the human spirit is present. When one closes their eyes to sleep, light and shadow withdraw inward, thoughts arise but are unspoken—spirit remains within. When sleep deepens, spirit departs to wander, the body unable to move, the mouth unable to speak, the ears unable to hear, merging with myriad spirits. Only qi remains—clear proof. Therefore, spirit must be constantly guarded; guarding it brings longevity, losing it exhausts one’s mandate. Those who attain the Dao do so through focused intention, and those who lose it do so through the same.

To rescue the deluded and transform the laws of emperors and kings.

The Great Dao’s transformations are boundless—spanning ten thousand leagues in mutual regard, limitless above and below, circulating through the six directions. To abide by it brings fortune; to neglect it brings harm. The opening and closing of yin and yang are its constant principle.

It is bestowed upon those of the Dao, enabling the virtuous to practice it, so their lifespan matches heaven and earth. Virtue has degrees of excellence, matters have roots and branches, and all things follow the Dao. Those on the rise encounter goodness; those in decline encounter misfortune.

For example, land: fertile soil yields goodness, while barren soil yields adversity. The noble align with heaven; the base are mired in marshes. The settled are masters; the wandering are transient guests—all is encompassed by the Dao.

The virtuous cultivate fortune through their conduct; the wicked cultivate disaster. The virtuous gain it as blessing and power. The exalted ride in carriages by its grace; the lowly walk by its support. The sagely and wise attain liberation through it; the petty, though they gain it, do not harm one another—all is the Dao.

Teachings do not appear twice; time does not return. Hasten to instruct emperors and kings, that they may practice the Way of Great Peace. When the Dao is practiced, the self attains liberation, and merit extends to all living beings in the six directions.

*Excerpts from the Gui Section, Scroll Ten of the* Abridged Scripture of Great Peace *concludes.*

*(Note: According to textual research, this scroll should be an abridged version of Scroll Seventeen of the Jia Section of the* Scripture of Great Peace. *The* Orthodox Daoist Canon *contains errors.)*
